English Question: Good farming soil is dark, crumbly, and has a pleasant earthy smell. Push your finger 5cm into the soil — if it holds shape but breaks apart easily, it is good. You can also send a sample to an agricultural office for a proper soil test.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na ɛkyerɛ sɛ m'asase yɛ yɛ papa ma okuafo adwuma?
Twi Answer: Asase pa wɔ okuafo adwuma mu yɛ ɛda, na ɛpepee yie, na ɛwɔ asase hua. Fa wo nsateaa wura asase no mu sɛntimita 5 — sɛ ɛkura ne ho nanso ɛpae yie a, ɛyɛ asase pa. Wobetumi de asase bi kɔ okuafo ofisi sɛ wɔhwɛ so yie.

English Question: For maize, use NPK fertilizer (15-15-15) at planting, then top-dress with urea about 4-6 weeks after planting. Apply 2 bags of NPK per acre at planting and 1 bag of urea per acre when top-dressing.
Twi Question: Ferefere bɛn na ɛyɛ papa ma aburo?
Twi Answer: Aburo ho, fa NPK ferefere (15-15-15) de to asase mu bere a wode aburow to mu no. Afei fa urea gu so sɛntɔ 4-6 akyi a wode aburow to mu no. Fa NPK bɔtɔ 2 gu acre baako biara mu bere a wode aburow no gu fam, na fa urea bɔtɔ 1 gu acre baako biara mu bere a wode to so.

English Question: Yes, animal manure from cows, goats, or chickens is an excellent organic fertilizer. Apply well-composted manure 2-3 weeks before planting. It improves soil structure and provides slow-release nutrients.
Twi Question: Metumi de mmoa dɔteɛ adi dwuma mmom sen nnuru ferefere?
Twi Answer: Aane, mmoa aguare fi boo, abirekyi, anaa akrɔma yɛ ferefere papa pa ara. De aguare a ɛawie wo yie no to asase so wiemu 2-3 ansa na wobede aba to mu. Ɛsiesie asase mu na ɛma aduan ho nhwiren ba bebree.

English Question: Mix green materials like grass and vegetable waste with brown materials like dry leaves and straw in a pile. Keep it moist and turn it every 2 weeks. After 2-3 months, you will have rich compost ready for your farm.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ compost wɔ fie?
Twi Answer: Fa Nneɛma a ɛyɛ ahabammono te sɛ sare ne nnuaba funu fra nneɛma a ɛyɛ bruu te sɛ nhaban a ɛwo ne sarew. Ma ɛnnyɛ nwini na dane no dapɛn abien biara. Abosome 2-3 akyi, wobɛnya compost pa a ɛawie wo yie wɔ wo afuo ho.

English Question: Add organic matter like compost, animal manure, or crop residues to sandy soil. This helps retain moisture and nutrients. Mulching the soil surface also reduces water evaporation. Consider drip irrigation for better water management.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi yɛ asintiɛ asase a ɛwo ntɛm no yiye?
Twi Answer: De nhwiren foforo te sɛ compost, mmoa aguare, anaa nnuaba ho nsennua ka asintiɛ asase no ho. Eyi boa ma nsu ne nnuaba mu nnuane nka mu yie. Sɛ wode mulch kata asase no so a, ɛma nsuo nwo ntɛm. Fa nsuo gu fam nkakrankakra (drip irrigation) di dwuma de hwɛ nsuo so yiye.

English Question: Plant cover crops or grass along slopes, practice contour farming, build terraces on steep land, and mulch bare soil. Avoid leaving soil uncovered during heavy rain seasons.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mema asase amma ɛnhuru wɔ m'afuo mu?
Twi Answer: To nnuaba anaa atɛntɛnni wɔ kwantempon ho, yɛ contour farming, si terrace wɔ asase a ɛkwan so, na de mulch sɛɛ asase a ɛda. Bɔ hwɛ asase da ho akyɛ wɔ nsuo tenten bere mu.

English Question: Apply agricultural lime (calcium carbonate) to raise the pH of acidic soil. Typically apply 1-2 tonnes per hectare. Apply lime at least 3-4 weeks before planting and mix it well into the soil.
Twi Question: M'asase yɛ acidic dodo. Dɛn na metumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: De agricultural lime (calcium carbonate) to asase acidic no so sɛ ɛma pH no sor. Taa de tonne 1-2 to hectare biara so. De lime to asase so wiemu 3-4 ansa na wode aba to mu na ka ho yie wɔ asase mu.

English Question: Most vegetables grow best in soil with a pH between 6.0 and 7.0. Below 6.0 is too acidic and above 7.5 is too alkaline. You can test your soil pH using a simple pH testing kit from an agro-input shop or send a sample to your nearest agricultural laboratory.
Twi Question: Asase pH bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ ma nnuan?
Twi Answer: Nnuan bebree da sor pa wɔ asase a pH yɛ 6.0 ne 7.0 ntam. Ɛsua 6.0 a ɛyɛ acidic dodo na ɛboro 7.5 a ɛyɛ alkaline dodo. Wobetumi hwɛ wo asase pH wɔ pH testing kit fi agro-input adeɛtɔ hɔ anaa de asase bi kɔ agricultural laboratory a ɛbɛn wo.

English Question: Green manure means growing specific crops like legumes or grasses and then plowing them back into the soil while still green. This adds organic matter and nitrogen to the soil. Common green manure crops include cowpea, mucuna, and lablab. Plow them in at least 3 weeks before planting your main crop.
Twi Question: Dɛn na nhwiren-tew ferefere yɛ na ɛdeɛn na mefa di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Nhwiren-tew ferefere kyerɛ kura nnuaba bi te sɛ abɔdweɛ anaa atɛntɛnni na afei boro wɔn gu asase mu bere a wɔda koraa. Eyi de nhwiren foforo ne nitrogen ka asase ho. Nhwiren-tew ferefere nnuaba a wɔtaa di dwuma ne abɔdweɛ, mucuna, ne lablab. Boro wɔn gu asase mu wiemu 3 ansa na wokura wo nnuaba titiriw.

English Question: Signs that fertilizer is working include: darker green leaves, faster plant growth, larger leaves, and higher yield compared to unfertilized plots. If plants remain yellowish and grow slowly after 2-3 weeks of fertilizer application, the fertilizer may not have been applied correctly or the soil may have other problems.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'ferefere yɛ adwuma?
Twi Answer: Ahohyenam sɛ ferefere yɛ adwuma ne: nhaban a wɔyɛ tuntum-akyen pa ara, nnuaba a wɔda sor ntɛm, nhaban kɛse, ne nnuaba a wɔda sor dodo sen beae a wɔanto ferefere. Sɛ nnuaba da hoho na wɔda sor brɛ akyi a ferefere to so wiemu 2-3 a, ferefere no beɛ to so yie anaa asase no wɔ nsɛm foforɔ.

English Question: Yes, over-fertilizing can burn plant roots and leaves, cause excessive leafy growth with poor fruiting, pollute water sources, and waste money. Always follow the recommended rates on fertilizer bags or advice from your extension officer. Start with less and increase gradually based on crop response.
Twi Question: Ferefere dodo tumi sɛe m'nnuaba anaa?
Twi Answer: Aane, ferefere dodo tumi hyew nnuaba ntini ne nhaban, ma nnuaba nhaban da sor dodo na aba ba sua, ha nsuo mu, na seaa sika. Bue ferefere bag so krataa nhyɛso anaa fa wo extension officer nsɛm di. Fi ferefere sua na fa dodo so kakra kakra wɔ nnuaba tebea so.

English Question: NPK stands for Nitrogen (N), Phosphorus (P), and Potassium (K) — the three main nutrients plants need. Nitrogen helps leafy growth, Phosphorus supports root development and flowering, and Potassium strengthens stems and improves fruit quality. The numbers like 15-15-15 show the percentage of each nutrient in the bag.
Twi Question: Dɛn na NPK kyerɛ wɔ ferefere bag so?
Twi Answer: NPK kyerɛ Nitrogen (N), Phosphorus (P), ne Potassium (K) — aduan titiriw mmiɛnsa a nnuaba hia. Nitrogen boa nhaban da sor, Phosphorus boa ntini ne abode, na Potassium ma tibo yɛ den na aba yɛ pa. Nɔma te sɛ 15-15-15 no kyerɛ kɛse a aduan biara wɔ bag mu.

English Question: Do not apply fertilizer when: heavy rain is forecast as it will wash away the fertilizer, the soil is very dry as it can burn roots, plants are severely stressed from pests or disease, soil is waterlogged, or crops are very close to harvest. Always apply when soil has some moisture and weather is stable.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na nsɛ meto ferefere?
Twi Answer: Mto ferefere bere a: osu tenten rebɛba efisɛ ɛbɛhoro ferefere no kɔ, asase yera pa ara efisɛ betumi hyew ntini, nnuaba hia adwummakers anaa yadeɛ kɛse, nsuo hyɛ asase mu, anaa nnuaba rebɛwie ase ntɛm. To ferefere bere a asase wɔ nsuo kakra na ɛwim tebea yɛ pɛ.

English Question: Simple home tests: for pH, mix soil with vinegar — if it fizzes the soil is alkaline. Mix soil with baking soda and water — if it fizzes the soil is acidic. For texture, squeeze moist soil — clay soil holds shape, sandy soil crumbles, and loam soil holds shape then crumbles. For organic matter, dark soil has more organic matter than pale soil.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ m'asase wɔ fie a menwɔ kit?
Twi Answer: Fie hwɛ anammɔn ketewa: pH ho, ka asase ne vinegar — sɛ ɛpɔ a asase no yɛ alkaline. Ka asase ne baking soda ne nsuo — sɛ ɛpɔ a asase no yɛ acidic. Nsusuw ho, hia asase nte — amane asase kura ne ho, asintiɛ asase pae, na loam asase kura ne ho na afei pae. Nhwiren foforo ho, asase ɛda wɔ nhwiren foforo dodo sen asase hoho.

English Question: Soil becomes hard from: overuse of heavy machinery which compacts the soil, lack of organic matter, repeatedly plowing at the same depth creating a hardpan layer, frequent flooding followed by drying, and low biological activity. To fix it, add organic matter, practice deep tillage occasionally, and use cover crops.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛma asase yɛ den na ɛhia yiye?
Twi Answer: Asase yɛ den fi: egyapade kɛse ho di dwuma dodo a ɛhia asase, nhwiren foforo aduan ho hia, bere biara boro asase sukyerɛ koro so a ɛyɛ hardpan, nsuo tenten a ɛto akyi na asase yera, ne nkwa a ɛdi asase mu hia. Sɛ wohwehwɛ siesie no a, de nhwiren foforo ka ho, bere bi boro asase mu tenten, na kura asase-bo nnuabas.

English Question: In Ghana, the best time to plant maize is at the beginning of the rainy season — March to April in the south, and May to June in the north. Plant when you have received at least 2-3 good rains so the soil is well moistened.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ sɛ wode aburow to mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Wɔ Ghana, bere pa ara sɛ wode aburow to mu ne nsuo bere mfiase — Ɛbɔ kwan so Oforisuo wɔ apuei fam, na Ayɛwohomumo kwan so Mumu wɔ atifi fam. To aba mu bere a wanya nsu mmɛn 2-3 yie na asase no atenante yie.

English Question: Plant maize seeds 3-5 cm deep. If the soil is dry, plant slightly deeper to reach moisture. Space seeds 25-30 cm apart within rows and 75-90 cm between rows.
Twi Question: Ɛsukyerɛ bɛn na mede aburow aba to asase mu?
Twi Answer: De aburow aba to asase mu sɛntimita 3-5. Sɛ asase no yera a, to mu kakra dodo na wo nsa adu nsukuro ho. Gyae asukyerɛ 25-30 sɛntimita wɔ aba biara ntam na 75-90 sɛntimita wɔ nnua so ntam.

English Question: Crop rotation means growing different crops on the same land each season. For example, grow maize in season 1, then cowpea in season 2. This breaks pest cycles, improves soil fertility, and increases yields.
Twi Question: Dea ɛyɛ sɛ wosesa nnuaba gu asase mu na adɛn na ɛyɛ papa?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba sesae kyerɛ sɛ wokura ahorow nnuaba wɔ asase koro so bere biara. Nhwɛso so, kura aburow bere 1 mu, afei kura abɔdweɛ wɔ bere 2 mu. Eyi bubu adwummakers ntam, yɛ asase mu aduan ho nhwiren na ɛma nnuaba da sor dodo.

English Question: Choose certified seeds from reputable agro-input dealers. Good seeds are uniform in size, free from damage, and have a high germination rate of at least 85%. Avoid using seeds from the previous harvest for hybrid varieties.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mepaw aba pa sɛ mede to mu?
Twi Answer: Paw aba a wɔakyerɛw won fi agro-input atɔfo a wɔn din ayɛ pa. Aba pa yɛ pɛ wɔ boɔ mu, wɔ mfomso, na wɔn nyini yɛ kɛse sen 85%. Bɔ hwɛ de aba a wogye fi dɛm nnuaba meto aba hybrid aba no ase.

English Question: Clear the land of weeds and old crop residues. Plow or dig to loosen the soil to about 20-30 cm deep. Break up large clods and remove stones. Level the surface and apply basal fertilizer or compost before planting.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesiesie asase aba to mu ansa?
Twi Answer: Yi sare ne nnua funu fi asase no so. Twa anaa hwe asase no mu kɔ sɛntimita 20- 30 mu. Bubu asase akɛse no na yi abo. Siesie fam no yiye na fa basal ferefere anaa compost gu so ansa na wode aba no agu fam.

English Question: Yes, you can grow vegetables in the dry season with irrigation. Crops like tomatoes, pepper, onions, leafy vegetables, and cucumbers grow well in dry season with proper watering.
Twi Question: Metumi adua nnɔbae wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu?
Twi Answer: Aane, wobetumi kura nnuan wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu sɛ wode nsuo gu so. Nnɔbae te sɛ ntomate, mako, gyeene, nhaban nnɔbae, ne cucumber nyini yiye wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu sɛ wode nsuo gu so yiye a.

English Question: Water seedlings well the day before transplanting. Transplant in the late afternoon or on a cloudy day to reduce heat stress. Dig the hole bigger than the root ball. Remove seedling from container carefully without disturbing roots. Firm soil around roots and water immediately. Provide shade for 2-3 days if needed.
Twi Question: Kwan bɛn na ɛyɛ papa a yɛfa so si nnua nketewa baabi foforo a ɛrenwu?
Twi Answer: Gu nnua nketewa no nsuo pii da a ɛdi kan ansa na wosi wɔn baabi foforo. Si wɔn baabi foforo anwummere anaa da a ewim yɛ nwunu na ama owia nhyew wɔn. Tu amoa a ɛsɛ kɛse sen ntini no. Yi nnua nketewa no fi nkuku mu brɛoo a wunhaw ntini no. Fa asase kata ntini no ho yiye na gu nsuo ntɛm ara. Fa sunsuma brɛ wɔn nna 2-3 sɛ ɛhia2.

English Question: Check germination 5-10 days after planting depending on the crop. Good germination means at least 80% of planted seeds have sprouted uniformly. If germination is poor, check if seeds were planted too deep, soil was too dry or waterlogged, temperature was too extreme, or seeds were old. Replant gaps with fresh seeds immediately.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'aba apue yie?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ sɛ aba no afifi nna 5-10 akyi a wode agu fam5. Sɛ aba no fifi yiye a, ɛkyerɛ sɛ aba a wode agu fam no 80% pɛ afifi pɛpɛɛpɛ80. Sɛ aba no mfifi yiye a, hwɛ sɛ wode agu fam dodo, asase no yɛ kusuu anaa nsuo dɔɔso wɔ mu, ewim yɛ hye anaa nwunu dodo, anaa aba no dedaw. Fa aba foforo gu mmeae a ɛda hɔ no ntɛm ara.

English Question: A nursery is a protected area where seeds are germinated and young plants are raised before transplanting to the main field. Use a nursery for: small expensive seeds like tomato, pepper, and onion; crops that need a head start before rains; and crops where seedling survival in the field is uncertain. Nurseries save seeds and improve stand establishment.
Twi Question: Nursery yɛ dɛn na bere bɛn na ɛsɛ sɛ yɛde di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Nursery yɛ beae a wɔbɔ ho ban a wɔde aba gu mu na wɔtete nnua nketewa ansa na wɔde akɔdua wɔ afuo kɛse no mu. Fa nursery di dwuma ma: aba nketewa a ne boɔ yɛ den te sɛ ntomate, mako, ne gyeene; nnɔbae a ɛhia sɛ wofi ase ntɛm ansa na osuo aba; ne nnɔbae a ɛnyɛ awiegye sɛ ɛbɛtena ase wɔ afuo no mu. Nursery boa ma aba no yɛ yiye na ɛma nnua no nyini yiye.

English Question: Yes, mixing vegetables is called companion planting and can be very beneficial. Good combinations include tomatoes with basil (basil repels tomato pests), maize with beans and squash (the Three Sisters method), onions with carrots (they repel each other's pests), and marigolds with any vegetable (repels many insects). Avoid planting crops from the same family together as they share pests.
Twi Question: Metumi adua nnɔbae ahorow pii wɔ afuo koro mu anaa?
Twi Answer: Aane, nnɔbae a wudua no bom yɛ companion planting na ɛboa pii. Nnuaba a wɔyɛ adwuma yie wɔ bom ne ntomato ne basil (basil kora ntomato adwummakers ase), aburow ne abɔdweɛ ne squash (Three Sisters anammɔn), gyene ne carrot (wɔkora wɔn ho adwummakers ase), na marigold ne nnuan biara (ɛkora adwummakers bebree ase). Hwɛ yiye na woannua nnɔbae a ɛwɔ abusua koro mu wɔ beae koro efisɛ wɔtaa nya yare koro.

English Question: On slopes, always plant across the slope (contour planting) rather than up and down. Make ridges along contour lines to hold water. Plant cover crops or grasses on the steepest parts. Use tied ridges (ridges with cross-ties every few meters) to capture rainwater. Mulch heavily to protect soil between plants.
Twi Question: Kwan bɛn na ɛsɛ sɛ mefa so dua nnɔbae wɔ mmepɔw so na ama nsuo anntu kɔ?
Twi Answer: Wɔ kwantempon so, to aba twa kwantempon so daa (contour planting) na mmom kɔ sor na gu ase. Yɛ ntwaho wɔ contour lines no ho na ama nsuo akora. To asase-bo nnuabas anaa atɛntɛnni wɔ beae a ɛkwan pa ara. Fa tied ridges (ntwaho a wɔne kyɛ ɛtɔ so baako biara) sɛ ɛgye osu nsuo. De mulch to so papaapa sɛ ɛkora asase nnuaba ntam.

English Question: Transplant tomato seedlings when they are 4-6 weeks old, have 4-6 true leaves, are 15-20 cm tall, and have a sturdy stem. Seedlings that are too young may not survive transplanting shock. Seedlings that are too old (over 8 weeks) become root-bound and may not establish well in the field.
Twi Question: Mfeɛ bɛn na ɛfata sɛ mesi ntomato nnuaba mfoforo ananmu?
Twi Answer: Si ntomato nnuaba mfoforo ananmu bere a wɔdin nnawotwe 4-6, wɔwɔ nhaban 4-6, wɔn soroɔ yɛ sɛntimita 15-20, na wɔwɔ tibo den. Nnuaba mfoforo a wɔkum dodo betumi ankyɛ si ananmu no ɔkɔm. Nnuaba mfoforo a wɔadin dodo (nnawotwe 8 kenkan) yɛ root-bound na betumi ansi yie wɔ afuo mu.

English Question: Raised bed farming means growing crops on elevated soil mounds or frames above the ground level. Benefits include better drainage, improved soil structure, easier weeding and harvesting, higher yield per square meter, better pest management, and ability to farm in poor soil areas. It is ideal for small spaces and home gardens.
Twi Question: Dɛn na asase-sor afuo farming yɛ na mfaaso bɛn na ɛwɔ?
Twi Answer: Asase-sor afuo farming kyerɛ kura nnuaba wɔ asase mounts anaa frame a ɛda sor sen asase soronko. Mfaaso ho ne: nsuo pue mu yie, asase mu siesie pa, nhaban tia ne nnuaba gye yɛ mmerɛ, nnuaba da sor dodo wɔ square meter biara mu, adwummakers hwɛ ase yie, na tumi kura wɔ asase a enni pa mu. Ɛfata afuo ketewa ne fie afuo.

English Question: Growing in containers is called container gardening. Use large buckets, old tires, plastic bags, or purpose-made pots. Fill with a mix of soil, compost, and sand for good drainage. Good container crops include tomatoes, peppers, leafy vegetables, herbs, and onions. Place in a sunny spot and water frequently as containers dry out faster than ground soil.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura nnuaba wɔ nkuku anaa pots mu sɛ menni asase?
Twi Answer: Kura wɔ nkuku mu sɛ container gardening. Fa bucket kɛse, tayɛ kedee, plastik bags, anaa nkuku a wɔyɛ wɔn ho. Hye asase, compost, ne asintiɛ bom mu sɛ nsuo pue mu yie. Nnuaba a wɔda sor yie wɔ nkuku mu ne ntomato, mako, nhaban nnuan, nduaba aduan, ne gyene. Si wɔn wɔ beae a owia hye na de nsuo to pɛ efisɛ nkuku yera ntɛm sen asase.

English Question: This is likely the Fall Armyworm. Look inside the whorl for worms. Apply insecticides like emamectin benzoate early morning or late evening. Sand mixed with ash applied into the whorl also helps as an organic option.
Twi Question: M'aburow nhaban wɔ tumtum na wɔredidi won. Dɛn na meyɛ?
Twi Answer: Eyi tumi yɛ Aborɔnoma Adwummaker Kɛse adwummaker. Hwɛ nhaban mu sɛ wɔhwehwɛ adwummakers anaa wɔ ho ntama. De adwummakers dawuro te sɛ emamectin benzoate guare owia da ano anaa nnɔnhwerew mu. Asintiɛ a waka nkamfo ka ho no tumi de gu nhaban mu sɛ nhwiren dawuro.

English Question: Dry the grain properly before storage to below 13% moisture. Use hermetic airtight bags which suffocate insects. You can also mix grain with diatomite dust or apply approved grain protectant chemicals.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi de weevils hyɛ ase wɔ m'aduan a maguina mu?
Twi Answer: Yaw aduan no yie ansa na waguina mu na ɛsua 13% nsuku. Fa hermetic bags a wɔapo so yie a ɛkum adwummakers wɔ mu. Wobetumi de aduan ka diatomite tukutuku ho anaa de aduan adwummakers dawuro a wɔagyei no to so.

English Question: Wilting despite watering could be bacterial wilt or fusarium wilt — soil-borne diseases. Cut the stem — if the inside is brown or oozes liquid, it is wilt disease. Remove infected plants and rotate crops for 2-3 years.
Twi Question: M'ntomato nnua rewo na mede nsu hyɛ won. Dɛn na ɛhia?
Twi Answer: Nwonwon a ɛba wɔ nsuo a wode hyɛ won akyi no betumi yɛ bacteria nwiinwii yadeɛ anaa fusarium yadeɛ wilt — yadeɛ a ɛfiri asase mu. Twa tibo no — sɛ mu yɛ ɛda anaa nsuo pue a, ɛyɛ wilt yadeɛ. Yi nnua a wɔayarɛ no fi afuo mu na sesa nnuaba mfe 2-3.

English Question: This could be Cassava Mosaic Disease spread by whiteflies. Symptoms include yellowing and leaf curling. There is no cure — remove and destroy infected plants immediately. Plant resistant varieties and control whitefly populations.
Twi Question: M'bankye nhaban redan sika na rekyekye. Dɛn na ɛhia?
Twi Answer: Eyi betumi yɛ Cassava Mosaic Yadeɛ a fitaa abowa adwummakers de brɛ. Ahohyenam ho ne nhaban hoho ne kyekyere. Enni dawuro — yi nnua a wɔayarɛ no na seaa won ntɛm ara. To aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase na kora fitaa abowa adwummakers ase.

English Question: Fall Armyworm is a highly destructive caterpillar that mainly attacks maize. It can destroy an entire field within days. Control with insecticides like emamectin benzoate, apply early morning, and target the whorls where larvae hide.
Twi Question: Dɛn na Aborɔnoma Adwummaker Kɛse ne ɛyɛ ɔkɔmm bɛn?
Twi Answer: Aborɔnoma Adwummaker Kɛse yɛ aborɔnoma adwummaker a ɔsɛe dodo na ɔtaa kɔ aburow so. Ɔtumi seaa afuo koro nyinaa wɔ nnafoa mu. Kora ase wɔ adwummakers dawuro te sɛ emamectin benzoate, de to owia da ano, na hyɛ nhaban mu a adwummakers no kɔfa ho.

English Question: Aphids are small soft insects that cluster on young shoots. Spray them off with a strong jet of water, or apply neem oil, insecticidal soap, or systemic insecticides like imidacloprid. Introduce natural predators like ladybirds if possible.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora aphid ase wɔ m'nnuaba so?
Twi Answer: Aphid yɛ adwummakers ketewa a wɔhyia wɔ nnuaba mfoforo so. De nsuo kɛse guare won afi, anaa de neem dawuro, adwummakers dawuro sabɔ, anaa adwummakers dawuro te sɛ imidacloprid gu won so. De aborɔkyir adwummakers a ɔdi wɔn te sɛ ladybird fa ba sɛ wonya tumi.

English Question: Dark spots at the bottom of tomatoes are Blossom End Rot caused by calcium deficiency and irregular watering. Maintain consistent watering and apply calcium-rich fertilizers. Dark spots on the sides may be from fungal diseases.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛma m'ntomato aba so wɔ ntuntum nsono?
Twi Answer: Ntuntum nsono a ɛwɔ ntomato aba ase no yɛ Blossom End Rot, a calcium hia na nsuo to nsɛ ama. Kora nsuo to pɛ na de calcium ferefere to so. Ntuntum nsono a ɛwɔ afã so betumi fi fungal yadeɛ.

English Question: Leaf spots on groundnuts are usually Early Leaf Spot or Late Leaf Spot fungal diseases. Spray with fungicides like mancozeb or chlorothalonil every 2 weeks. Plant resistant varieties and practice crop rotation.
Twi Question: M'nkatie nhaban wɔ nsono. Yadeɛ bɛn na ɛyɛ?
Twi Answer: Nhaban nsono wɔ nkatie so taa yɛ Early Nhaban Nsono Yadeɛ anaa Late Nhaban Nsono Yadeɛ fungal yadeɛ. De mancozeb anaa chlorothalonil guare mmere 2 biara. To aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase na yɛ nnuaba sesae.

English Question: Practice crop rotation, remove crop residues after harvest, use pest-resistant varieties, plant trap crops like marigolds, use nets or row covers, and monitor your farm regularly.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mema adwummakers amma wɔnba m'nnuan afuo mu?
Twi Answer: Yɛ nnuaba sesae, yi nnuaba nsennua akyi a wogye, fa aba a ɛtumi adwummakers ase, to trap crops te sɛ marigold sɛ ɛtwe adwummakers fi nnuaba pa ho, fa nets anaa row covers, na hwɛ wo afuo so pɛ.

English Question: Control grasshoppers by early morning spraying with approved insecticides like lambda-cyhalothrin. Biological control using Metarhizium fungi is also effective. Community-wide spraying is more effective than individual farm treatment.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora totrobonini ase wɔ m'afuo so?
Twi Answer: Wobetumi kora totrobonini ase wɔ owia da ano guare adwummakers dawuro a wɔagyei te sɛ lambda-cyhalothrin. Metarhizium fungi biological control nso yɛ adwuma pa. Oman nyinaa guare yɛ adwuma pa sen afuo baako biara.

English Question: Whiteflies are tiny white insects that suck plant sap and spread viruses. Control them by spraying insecticidal soap, neem oil, or imidacloprid. Yellow sticky traps also help. Avoid excessive nitrogen fertilizer which attracts them.
Twi Question: Adwummakers fitaa a wɔwɔ m'nnuan so yɛ dɛn na metumi yi wɔn?
Twi Answer: Fitaa abowa yɛ adwummakers fitaa ketewa a wɔnom nnuaba mogya na wɔde yadeɛ brɛ. Kora wɔn ase wɔ adwummakers dawuro sabɔ, neem dawuro, anaa imidacloprid so. Yellow sticky traps nso boa. Bɔ hwɛ nitrogen ferefere dodo efisɛ ɛtwe wɔn.

English Question: Use bird scaring methods: move scarecrows regularly to remain effective, hang reflective tape or old CDs around the field, use noise-makers, and recruit children to chase birds during grain-filling stage. Growing early-maturing varieties reduces the bird damage period.
Twi Question: Anomaa redidi m'ɔtɛ ne ɔtɛ pa. Ɛdeɛn na mekora m'nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Fa anomaa kora anammɔn: tware anomaa kyerɛma pɛ sɛ ɛyɛ adwuma yie, si reflective tape anaa CD kedee wɔ afuo ho, fa nne adeɛ, na fa mmofra boa sɛ wɔtaa anomaa no bere a aba no repuo. Kura aba a ɛwie ntɛm maa anomaa sɛe bere sua.

English Question: Mango mealybugs appear as white cottony masses on stems and fruits. Control by pruning heavily infested branches, applying insecticidal soap or neem oil, banding tree trunks with sticky tape to prevent crawlers from climbing, and introducing natural predators like Cryptolaemus beetles.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora mangoro mealybug ase?
Twi Answer: Mangoro mealybug ba sɛ dodow fitaa wɔ nnua tiboo ne aba so. Kora wɔn ase wɔ twa ntini a wɔhyia so kɛse, de adwummakers dawuro sabɔ anaa neem dawuro gu so, de sticky tape kaa ntini ho, na de Cryptolaemus beetle a ɔdi wɔn fa ba.

English Question: Bean rust appears as orange-brown powdery spots on leaves. Remove and destroy severely infected leaves. Spray with fungicides containing mancozeb or sulfur. Plant resistant varieties. Avoid overhead watering which spreads spores.
Twi Question: M'abɔdweɛ wɔ rust yadeɛ. Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ?
Twi Answer: Bean rust ba sɛ nsono ɛda-bɔɔ wɔ nhaban so. Yi na seaa nhaban a wɔayarɛ kɛse. De mancozeb anaa sulfur fungicide guare. To aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase. Bɔ hwɛ nsuo guare firi sor efisɛ ɛde yadeɛ tete.

English Question: Striga is a parasitic weed that attaches to crop roots. Control includes using Striga-resistant varieties, applying Imazapyr-coated seeds, hand pulling Striga before it flowers, growing trap crops like Sudan grass, and applying fertilizer to help crops outcompete Striga.
Twi Question: Striga nhaban foforo resɛe m'ɔtɛ. Dɛn na metumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: Striga yɛ nhaban foforo a ɔkyerɛ ne ho wɔ nnuaba ntini so. Kora ase wɔ de aba a ɛtumi Striga ase hyɛ, de Imazapyr-coated aba, twe Striga wɔ nsa ansa na ɔba abode, kura trap crops te sɛ Sudan grass, na de ferefere to sɛ ɛboa nnuaba no nko ɔkan.

English Question: Always read the label before use. Wear protective clothing including gloves, boots, mask, and long sleeves. Mix pesticides in open air away from water sources. Never eat, drink, or smoke while handling pesticides. Store in original containers away from children.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mefa adwummakers dawuro di dwuma a ɛho tumi wɔ m'afuo mu?
Twi Answer: Kenkan krataa a ɛwɔ so ansa na wodi dwuma. Hye ntoma a ɛkora wo ho te sɛ nsatea nhoma, mbotɔ, aboa, ne ntama tenten. Ka dawuro no wɔ baabi a mframa wɔ hɔ tete fi nsuo ho. Mmu aduan, nnom nsu, anaa mfa sigaret bere a wode dawuro no di dwuma.

English Question: Aflatoxin is a toxic substance produced by molds that grow on grains, groundnuts, and spices when stored in humid conditions. It is harmful to humans and animals and causes liver disease. Prevent it by drying crops properly and using clean airtight storage.
Twi Question: Dɛn na aflatoxin dze yɛ na ɛyɛ m'nnuaba dɛn?
Twi Answer: Aflatoxin Dze yɛ nsɛm a ɛyɛ ɔkɔm a fungus a ɛda sor wɔ nnuaba, nkatie, ne nduaba so bere a wɔaguina wɔ huhu mu na ɛba. Ɛyɛ onipa ne mmoa ɔkɔm na ɛma afu yadeɛ. Kora ase wɔ yaw nnuaba yie ansa na waguina na de nkuku a apo so yie guina.

English Question: Integrated Pest Management (IPM) is an approach that combines multiple pest control methods to minimize chemical use. It includes: monitoring crops regularly to catch problems early, using resistant varieties, practicing good agronomic practices, using biological controls like beneficial insects, and only using chemicals as a last resort when pest populations exceed economic thresholds.
Twi Question: Dɛn na adwummakers hwɛ anammɔn kaa bom (IPM) yɛ?
Twi Answer: Adwummakers Hwɛ Anammɔn Kaa Bom (IPM) yɛ anammɔn a wɔka adwummakers kora anammɔn bebree bom sɛ chemical fa sua. Mu wɔ: hwɛ nnuaba so pɛ sɛ wuhu nsɛm ntɛm, fa aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase, yɛ okuafo adwuma pa, fa biological controls te sɛ adwummakers a wɔboa, na fa chemicals pɛ bere a adwummakers a ɛyɛ dodo sene sika mu a wobɛnya.

English Question: Blend 10-15 hot chili peppers with 1 litre of water. Strain through cloth, add a little liquid soap, and dilute with 5 more litres of water. Spray on affected plants in the morning or evening. The capsaicin in chili repels and kills soft-bodied insects like aphids and mites. Reapply every 3-4 days and after rain.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ fie nhwiren adwummakers dawuro fi mako?
Twi Answer: Blend mako hye 10-15 ne nsuo litre 1 bom. Hun wɔ ntama mu, de liquid soap kakra ka ho, na fa nsuo litre 5 bio ka ho. Guare nnuaba a wɔayarɛ so owia da ano anaa anwummere. Capsaicin a ɛwɔ mako mu kora adwummakers a wɔn ho yɛ mmerɛ te sɛ aphid ne mite ase. To so bio nnafoa 3-4 biara na osu akyi.

English Question: Nematodes are microscopic worms that live in soil. Some are harmful to crops — they attack roots causing galls (swellings), stunted growth, and yellowing. They are common in sandy soils and warm climates. Control by rotating crops, using resistant varieties, adding organic matter to soil, and solarizing soil (covering with clear plastic to heat it and kill nematodes during the dry season).
Twi Question: Dɛn na nematode yɛ na ɛyɛ m'nnuaba dɛn?
Twi Answer: Nematode yɛ nwirɛntwi a wɔte asase mu a wɔhunu da. Bi yɛ nnuaba ɔkɔm — wɔtwe ntini ho ma ɛyɛ kɛse, nnuaba nni sor yie, na nhaban hoho. Wɔtaa wɔ asintiɛ asase ne ahuhuro mu. Kora ase wɔ sesa nnuaba, fa aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase, de nhwiren foforo ka asase ho, na solarize asase (fa plastik fitaa sɛɛ so sɛ ɛhye mu na kum nematode wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu).

English Question: Powdery mildew appears as white powdery patches on leaves and stems. It is caused by fungi and thrives in warm, dry conditions with high humidity. It weakens plants and reduces yield. Control by: removing infected leaves, improving air circulation by pruning, spraying with diluted baking soda solution (1 tablespoon per litre of water), neem oil, or sulfur-based fungicides.
Twi Question: Dɛn na tukutuku fitaa yadeɛ yɛ na ɛdeɛn na metumi kora ase?
Twi Answer: Tukutuku fitaa yadeɛ ba sɛ fitaa tukutuku a ɛwɔ nhaban ne tibo so. Fungus ama na ɛda sor pa wɔ ahuhuro mu a ɛwɔ huhu. Ɛma nnuaba yɛ mmerɛ na eba nnuaba a wɔda sor sua. Kora ase wɔ: yi nhaban a wɔayarɛ, ma mframa pue mu yie wɔ twa nnua so, guare baking soda a wɔasusu mu (tablespoon baako wɔ nsuo litre biara mu), neem dawuro, anaa sulfur-based fungicide.

English Question: Leaf tip burn can be caused by: fertilizer burn from too much nitrogen or potassium, salt stress from poor quality irrigation water, calcium deficiency, water stress during hot weather, or wind damage. Check your fertilizer rates and water quality first. Apply calcium fertilizer and ensure consistent watering. The condition often improves once the cause is corrected.
Twi Question: M'nnuaba nhaban ɔkyɛ yɛ sɛ wɔahyew. Dɛn na ɛhia?
Twi Answer: Nhaban ɔkyɛ hyew betumi fi: ferefere burn fi nitrogen anaa potassium dodo, salt ɔkɔm fi nsuo a enni pa, calcium hia, nsuo hia wɔ ahuhuro mu, anaa mframa ɔkɔm. Hwɛ wo ferefere kɛse ne nsuo ho pa ansa. De calcium ferefere to so na kora nsuo to pɛ. Tebea no taa yɛ pa bere a wuyɛ dawuro.

English Question: Spider mites are tiny red or brown creatures barely visible to the naked eye. Signs include: fine webbing on leaves and stems, tiny yellow or white dots on leaves (feeding damage), and leaves turning bronze or yellow. Control by spraying with strong water jet, neem oil, insecticidal soap, or miticides. Mites thrive in hot and dry conditions — adequate watering helps prevent them.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehunu spider mite na metumi kora wɔn ase?
Twi Answer: Spider mite yɛ adwummakers ɛda-kɔkɔɔ anaa ɛda-bɔɔ ketewa a wohunu wɔn yie. Ahohyenam ho ne: nwirɛntwi a ɛwɔ nhaban ne tibo so, nsono hoho anaa fitaa ketewa ketewa wɔ nhaban so (adidi akyinnye), na nhaban a wɔredan kɔkɔɔ anaa hoho. Kora ase wɔ de nsuo kɛse guare, neem dawuro, adwummakers dawuro sabɔ, anaa miticide. Mite da sor pa wɔ ahuhuro ne ɔpɛ bere — nsuo pa boa sɛ wɔnba.

English Question: Root rot is caused by soil-borne fungi, mainly when soil stays waterlogged for too long. It causes roots to turn brown and mushy, plants to wilt even when soil is wet, and eventual plant death. Prevent by: improving soil drainage, avoiding overwatering, not planting in low-lying waterlogged areas, using raised beds, treating seeds with fungicide before planting, and rotating crops.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛma ntini sɛe na ɛdeɛn na metumi kora ase?
Twi Answer: Ntini sɛe fi asase fungus, titiriw bere a nsuo da asase mu tenten dodo. Ɛma ntini dan ɛda ne mmerɛ, nnuaba nwo bere a asase nte, na nnua wu. Kora ase wɔ: siesie asase nsuo pue anammɔn, bɔ hwɛ nsuo to dodo, mto nnuaba wɔ asase ase a nsuo hia mu, fa asase-sor afuo, de aba ka fungicide ho ansa na woto mu, na sesa nnuaba.

English Question: Thrips are tiny insects that feed on onion leaves causing silvery streaks and distorted growth. Control by: removing heavily infested leaves, spraying with neem oil or insecticides like spinosad or imidacloprid, mulching to prevent thrips from pupating in soil, avoiding planting near other infested crops, and using blue sticky traps for monitoring.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora thrips ase wɔ m'gyene so?
Twi Answer: Thrips yɛ adwummakers ketewa a wɔdi gyene nhaban so ma ɛkyerɛ silver ne nnuaba a wɔnni sor yie. Kora ase wɔ: yi nhaban a wɔhyia so kɛse, guare neem dawuro anaa adwummakers dawuro te sɛ spinosad anaa imidacloprid, de mulch to sɛ thrips ansi asase mu, bɔ hwɛ to nnuaba bɛn nnuaba foforɔ a wɔahyia so, na fa blue sticky traps hwɛ wɔn so.

English Question: Damping off is a fungal disease that causes seedlings to suddenly collapse and die, usually at the soil level where the stem meets the ground. The stem appears water-soaked and constricted. It is caused by overwatering, poor drainage, overcrowded seedlings, and unsterilized potting mix. Prevent by using sterilized soil, avoiding overwatering, ensuring good air circulation, and treating seeds with fungicide.
Twi Question: Dɛn na nnuaba-mfoforo wu yadeɛ yadeɛ yɛ wɔ nnuaba mfoforo mu?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba-mfoforo wu yadeɛ yɛ fungal yadeɛ a ɛma nnuaba mfoforo tu ntɛm na wɔwu, titiriw wɔ asase so a tibo ne asase hyia hɔ. Tibo no yɛ sɛ nsuo da mu na ɛhyia. Nsuo dodo, nsuo pue anammɔn a enni pa, nnuaba mfoforo a wɔhyia so, ne potting mix a wonsi amu ama. Kora ase wɔ fa asase a wɔasi amu, bɔ hwɛ nsuo dodo, kora mframa pue mu yie, na de aba ka fungicide ho ansa na woto.

English Question: Common deficiency signs: Nitrogen deficiency — older leaves turn yellow starting from the bottom of the plant. Iron deficiency — young leaves turn yellow but veins stay green. Phosphorus deficiency — leaves turn purple or reddish. Potassium deficiency — leaf edges turn brown and crispy. Calcium deficiency — new leaves distort and curl. A soil test will confirm which nutrients are lacking.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehunu sɛ m'nnuaba hia aduan?
Twi Answer: Aduan hia ahohyenam a wɔtaa hu: Nitrogen hia — nhaban kedee a wɔwɔ nnua ase hoho fi nnua ase. Iron hia — nhaban foforo hoho nanso nhwiren ho da tuntum-akyen. Phosphorus hia — nhaban dan purpura anaa kɔkɔɔ. Potassium hia — nhaban ho dan ɛda ne den. Calcium hia — nhaban foforo pae ne kyekye. Asase hwɛ bɛkyerɛ aduan a ehia.

English Question: Tomato leaf miners are larvae that tunnel inside leaves creating winding white trails. Control by: removing and destroying heavily mined leaves, applying spinosad or abamectin insecticides, using yellow sticky traps to catch adult flies, releasing parasitic wasps as biological control, and avoiding planting tomatoes after tomatoes in the same location.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora ntomato nhaban miner ase?
Twi Answer: Ntomato nhaban miner yɛ larvae a wɔkɔ nhaban mu mu na wɔyɛ kwan fitaa a ahwimhwim. Kora ase wɔ: yi ne seaa nhaban a wɔahyia so kɛse, de spinosad anaa abamectin guare, fa yellow sticky traps gye sorɔ a ɛyɛ hogua mu no, de parasitic wasp guare sɛ biological control, na bɔ hwɛ to ntomato akyi ntomato wɔ faako koro.

English Question: Citrus greening (also called Huanglongbing or HLB) is a deadly bacterial disease spread by the Asian citrus psyllid insect. Symptoms include yellowing leaves, misshapen bitter fruits, and tree decline. There is currently no cure — infected trees should be removed and destroyed to prevent spread. Control psyllid insects and use certified disease-free planting material.
Twi Question: Dɛn na citrus greening yadeɛ yɛ na wobetumi ayɛ dawuro?
Twi Answer: Citrus greening (a wɔfre no Huanglongbing anaa HLB) yɛ bacterial yadeɛ a ɛkum na Asian citrus psyllid adwummaker de tete. Ahohyenam ho ne nhaban hoho, aba a asɛe ne a wɔn dɛm yɛ den, na nnua hia. Enni dawuro saa ara — yi nnua a wɔayarɛ na seaa wɔn sɛ yadeɛ anntete. Kora psyllid adwummakers ase na fa aba a wɔakyerɛw wɔ ho to mu.

English Question: Most crops need about 25-50mm of water per week. Signs of water stress include wilting and dry soil. In the dry season, water deeply but less frequently to encourage deep rooting. Early morning watering reduces evaporation.
Twi Question: Nsuo bɛn na m'nnuaba hia?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba bebree hia nsuo sɛntimita 25-50 dapɛn biara mu. Nsuo hia ahohyenam ho ne nwonwon ne asase a ɛyera. Ɔpɛ bere mu, de nsuo to asase mu kɛse nanso mmere pii bi no de nsuo to ho sɛ nnua no na wɔde wɔn ntini kɔ ase yie. Owia da ano nsuo guare mma nsukyerɛ yɛ dodo.

English Question: Push your finger 5cm deep into the soil — if dry, water is needed. Watch for early morning wilting as a sign of drought stress. Sandy soils need watering more often than clay soils. Tomatoes and vegetables need more frequent watering than cassava.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim bere a m'nnuaba hia nsuo?
Twi Answer: Hia wo nsateaa asase mu sɛntimita 5 — sɛ ɛyera a, hia nsuo. Hwɛ owia da ano nwonwon sɛ ɛkyerɛ nsuo hia. Asintiɛ asase hia nsuo pii sen amane asase. Ntomato ne nnuan hia nsuo pii sen bankye.

English Question: For small farms, drip irrigation is the most water-efficient method. Sprinkler irrigation is good for larger areas. Watering cans or buckets work for very small plots.
Twi Question: Nsuo to anammɔn bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ wɔ afuo ketewa mu?
Twi Answer: Afuo ketewa ho, nsuo tete-tete kyɛ yɛ anammɔn a ɛfa nsuo nkyɛn pa ara. Sprinkler irrigation yɛ ɔkorɔ wɔ beae kɛse. Nsuo kyɛ anaa bucket yɛ adwuma wɔ afuo ketewa ketewa.

English Question: Yes, borehole water is generally good for irrigation. However some borehole water can be salty or have high mineral content which can damage crops over time. If possible, test the water at an agricultural lab.
Twi Question: Metumi de borehole nsuo to nnuaba so?
Twi Answer: Aane, borehole nsuo yɛ ɔkorɔ sɛ wode nsuo gu so. Nanso borehole nsuo bi tumi yɛ ɛwa anaa minerals wɔ mu dodo a ɛtumi sɛe nnuaba bere akyi. Sɛ wonya tumi a, hwɛ nsuo no wɔ agricultural lab.

English Question: Maize is ready when the husks turn brown and dry, the silks are dark brown/black, and the kernels are hard. This is usually 90-120 days after planting depending on the variety.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'aburow awie ase na ɛyɛ a megye no?
Twi Answer: Aburow awie ase bere a ntwaho no dan ɛda na ayera, nhwiren no adan ɛda kɔkɔɔ/tuntum, na aba no ayɛ den. Eyi taa ba nnafoa 90-120 a wode aba to mu no akyi wɔ aba no ahodoɔ so.

English Question: Harvest vegetables in the early morning when temperatures are cool. This helps produce stay fresh longer. Avoid harvesting in midday heat. For leafy vegetables, harvest with dew still present for crispness.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn wɔ da mu na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ sɛ wogye nnuan?
Twi Answer: Gye nnuan owia da ano bere a owia hye no ayɛ tirim. Eyi ma nnuan no tena pɛ sen ara. Bɔ hwɛ wɔ awia mu ahuhuro mu gye nnuan. Nhaban nnuan ho, gye won a nsuyiri da won so ara da no ho nkae.

English Question: Harvest tomatoes when they are fully colored but still firm. For selling to distant markets, harvest at the breaker stage when they begin to change color so they ripen during transport without getting damaged.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na megye m'ntomato?
Twi Answer: Gye ntomato bere a wɔanya wɔn rere na wɔda den ara. Sɛ wohwehwɛ tɔn wɔ akura a ɛwɔ akyiri a, gye wɔn bere a wɔredan wɔn rere na wɔrebɛware wɔ kwan so a wɔde kɔ efisɛ wontumi ntwam.

English Question: Cassava is usually harvested 9-18 months after planting. Cut the stem at 30-40 cm height then loosen the soil around the plant with a hoe and pull up the roots. Handle roots gently to avoid bruising.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye m'bankye yie?
Twi Answer: Bankye taa gye wɔ abosome 9-18 akyi a wode to mu. Twa tibo no wɔ sɛntimita 30-40 so, afei de akɔde fa asase a ɛhyia nnua no ho na twe ntini no sor. De ntini no pɛ efisɛ sɛ ehow a ɛma ɛsɛe ntɛm.

English Question: Harvest groundnuts when leaves start yellowing. Loosen the soil with a hoe first then pull the whole plant upward. Shake off excess soil and thresh on a clean tarpaulin. Dry pods in the sun for 3-5 days before storage.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye nkatie a aba bi nko?
Twi Answer: Gye nkatie bere a nhaban no redan sika. Fa akɔde fa asase no ho ansa, afei twe nnua no nyinaa sor. Woso asase a aka no afi na bu wɔ tarpaulin horo so. Yaw aba no wɔ owia mu nnafoa 3-5 ansa na waguina.

English Question: Palm fruits are ready when they turn reddish-orange and some fruits start falling naturally from the bunch. Use a long-handled chisel or harvesting sickle to cut the bunch from the tree. Collect fallen fruits from the ground too. Process within 24-48 hours of harvest to avoid free fatty acid buildup which reduces oil quality.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye abe aba yie?
Twi Answer: Abe aba wie ase bere a wɔdan kɔkɔɔ-ɛda na aba bi firi bɔ afi ne ho pɛ. Fa long-handled chisel anaa harvesting sickle twa bɔ no fi dua no ho. Gye aba a atu gu asase so nso. Yɛ adwuma wɔ dafe 24-48 akyi a wogye sɛ free fatty acid nbi dodo a ɛsua ngo ho pa.

English Question: Mangoes are ready to harvest when: the fruit changes color from green to yellow, orange, or red depending on variety; the fruit flesh near the seed turns yellow; the fruit gives slightly when gently pressed; and the fruit smells sweet near the stem. For commercial harvest, pick slightly before full ripeness so they ripen during transport.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na mangoro awie ase sɛ megye?
Twi Answer: Mangoro awie ase bere a: aba no resen rere fi akyen kɔ hoho, ɛda, anaa kɔkɔɔ wɔ aba no ahodoɔ so; aba no nnompe a ɛbɛn aba no dan hoho; aba no tumi pii kakra bere a wode fa so pɛ; na aba no nhwiren foforo pue fi tibo ho. Tɔn ho, gye ansa na ɛawi pɛpɛɛpɛ na ɛware wɔ kwan so.

English Question: Harvest pepper using scissors or a sharp knife to cut the fruit with a small piece of stem — never pull the pepper off by hand as it damages the plant. Harvest when fruits are fully developed and have changed to their final color. Regular harvesting every 3-5 days encourages the plant to produce more fruits throughout the season.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye mako a ɛnsɛe nnua no?
Twi Answer: Gye mako fa scissors anaa sekan tew twa aba no a tibo kakra ka ho — mfa wo nsa twe mako afi nnua no ho da efisɛ ɛsɛe nnua no. Gye bere a aba no awi yie na wɔadan wɔn rere. Gye pɛ mmere 3-5 biara ma nnua no sɛ ɛkɔ ma aba dodo wɔ bere mu nyinaa.

English Question: Collect fallen shea fruits from the ground during the harvest season (May to August). Remove the sweet pulp by soaking and washing. Dry the nuts for 1-2 weeks in the sun. Crack the dried shells to get the kernels. Dry kernels further before storing or processing into shea butter. Never dry shea nuts on bare soil or over fire as this reduces butter quality.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye ne yɛ adwuma wɔ nkuto aba?
Twi Answer: Gye nkuto aba a atu gu asase so wɔ gye bere mu (Ɔbɛnem kwan so Ɔsannaa). Yi asew a ɛda mu wɔ da wɔ nsuo mu na hohoro. Yaw aba no owia mu nnawotwe 1-2. Bubu nkuku a ayaw no sɛ wunya aba no mu ade. Yaw aba mu ade no bio ansa na waguina anaa yɛ nkuto ngo. Mfa nkuto aba yaw wɔ asase firi so anaa ogya so da efisɛ ɛsua ngo ho pa.

English Question: A pineapple is ready when: the skin changes from green to yellow starting at the base, the fruit gives a dull hollow sound when tapped, the fruit smells sweet and fragrant, the leaves at the top pull out easily, and the fruit is firm but gives slightly when pressed. Pineapples do not ripen further after harvest, so timing is critical.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'aborɔfo awie ase sɛ megye?
Twi Answer: Aborɔfo awie ase bere a: foforo no resen fi akyen kɔ hoho fi ase, aba no su sɛ kɔkɔ bere a wode bɔ so, aba no nhwiren foforo pue na ɛyɛ dɛ, nhaban a ɛwɔ so no twe ba yie, na aba no yɛ den nanso tumi pii kakra. Aborɔfo nware bio akyi a wogye, enti bere yɛ titiriw pa ara.

English Question: Dry maize properly to below 13% moisture before storage. Store in clean, dry, well-ventilated structures. Use hermetic bags to prevent insect infestation. Avoid mixing good grain with damaged grain.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meguina m'aburow na aflatoxin dze nka ho?
Twi Answer: Yaw aburow yie na ɛsua 13% nsuku ansa na waguina. Guina wɔ fie a ɛhoro, yera, na ɛwɔ mframa pa. Fa hermetic bags sɛ adwummakers nni mu. Bɔ hwɛ ka aburo pa ne aburo a ɛasɛe no bom.

English Question: Fresh cassava deteriorates within 24-72 hours after harvest. For longer storage, process into dried chips, gari, or flour. Waxing the roots can extend fresh storage to about a week. Keep in cool, shaded areas.
Twi Question: Bere ahe na metumi guina bankye a megye no akyi?
Twi Answer: Bankye foforo sɛe wɔ dafe 24-72 akyi a wogye no. Sɛ wohwehwɛ guina bere tenten a, yɛ no bankye chips a ayaw, gari, anaa mfurow. Waxing bankye no de tumi ma no tena pɛ bere koro nnawotwe mu. Wura no wɔ bae a ɛhuru na owia ntra mu.

English Question: Store yams in a cool, dark, well-ventilated area. Traditional yam barns work well. Avoid contact with soil and keep yams off the ground. Inspect regularly and remove any rotting tubers. Yams can last 4-6 months.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meguina m'bayerɛ yie?
Twi Answer: Guina bayerɛ wɔ bae a ɛhuru, ɛsum na mframa pue mu yie. Amammerɛ bayerɛ guina sukuu yɛ adwuma pa. Bɔ hwɛ asase nka wɔn na ma wɔn na wɔntena asase so. Hwɛ wɔn so pɛ na yi ɔbayerɛ a ɛresɛe. Bayerɛ tumi tena yie abosome 4-6.

English Question: Keep the storage area clean and free of food scraps. Seal all holes and cracks in walls. Use snap traps or approved rodenticides. Store bags on raised platforms away from walls. Cats are also effective.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekora m'aduan a maguina fi ɔkra ne okusie ho?
Twi Answer: Kora guina fie no horo na aduan asennua ntena mu. Popa tumtum ne ɛwɔwɔ nyinaa wɔ bɔ mu. Fa snap traps anaa dawuro a wɔagyei de kum ɔkra. Guina bags wɔ platform a ɛda sor tete akyi. Agyinamoa nso yɛ adwuma pa.

English Question: Store tomatoes at room temperature away from direct sunlight. Do not stack heavily. Keep them stem-side down. Tomatoes last 1-2 weeks this way. For longer preservation, dry, can, or make tomato paste. Never refrigerate unripe tomatoes.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meguina m'ntomato a menhyɛ wɔn fridge mu?
Twi Answer: Guina ntomato wɔ fie mu osu a ɛyɛ pɛ sɛ owia ntra wɔn so tɔtɔ. Mfa wɔn si so dodo. De wɔn si wɔn tibo fam. Ntomato tumi tena nnawotwe 1-2 eyi ho. Sɛ wohwehwɛ tena bere tenten a, yaw, kanta, anaa yɛ ntomato paste.

English Question: You can make low-cost hermetic storage using: triple-layer plastic bags where you place grain in an inner plastic bag, seal it, place in a second bag, seal it, then place in a third outer bag and seal. Or use metal drums with tight-fitting lids sealed with tape. Store off the ground on pallets. This method is very effective for 6-12 months of storage.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ hermetic guina a ɛboɔ yɛ ketewa?
Twi Answer: Wobetumi yɛ hermetic guina a ɛboɔ yɛ ketewa wɔ: plastik bags mmiɛnsa a wode aduan si plastik bag mu, po so, de si bag abien mu, po so, afei de si bag mmiɛnsa mu na po so. Anoa fa metal drums a wɔn soro yɛ den a wɔde tape po so. Guina wɔ pallet so afi asase so. Anammɔn no yɛ adwuma yie pa ara wɔ guina abosome 6-12 mu.

English Question: Dry fish or meat thoroughly until it is very hard and dry. Wrap tightly in cloth or paper, then in a plastic bag. Store in a cool, dry, ventilated area away from moisture and insects. You can smoke the meat or fish to extend shelf life. Inspect weekly and re-dry immediately if any moisture is detected. Properly dried fish or meat can last 2-3 months.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meguina nsuomnam anaa nam a ayaw wɔ afuo so a menwɔ fridge?
Twi Answer: Yaw nsuomnam anaa nam no yie kosi sɛ ɛyɛ den na yera. De ntama anaa krataa sɛɛ mu yie, na afei de plastik bag sɛɛ. Guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru, yera, na mframa pue mu fi nsuo ne adwummakers ho. Wobetumi bu nam anaa nsuomnam no ewi sɛ ɛma no tena yie. Hwɛ so nnawotwe biara na yaw ntɛm sɛ nsuo wɔ mu. Nam anaa nsuomnam a ayaw yie tena abosome 2-3.

English Question: Mold grows when moisture is present. Prevent it by: drying produce thoroughly before storage, storing in well-ventilated areas, using absorbent packaging like cloth or paper not plastic, checking stored goods regularly, removing any moldy produce immediately to prevent spread, keeping storage areas clean, and never mixing new produce with old.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mema fungus amma ɛnda sor wɔ m'aduan a maguina?
Twi Answer: Fungus da sor bere a nsuo wɔ hɔ. Kora ase wɔ: yaw aduan no yie ansa na waguina, guina wɔ beae a mframa pue mu yie, fa packaging a ɛsuo nsuo te sɛ ntama anaa krataa na mfa plastik, hwɛ aduan a waguina pɛ, yi aduan a fungus ato ho ntɛm sɛ anntete, kora guina beae no horo, na mmfa aduan foforo ka aduan kedee bom da.

English Question: Cold storage is refrigerated storage that keeps produce at low temperatures to extend shelf life. Small farmers can access it through: farmer cooperatives that own shared cold storage facilities, government-run cold storage centers, private cold storage services that charge per crate or kilogram, mobile cold storage trucks, and evaporative coolers which are low-cost non-electrical cooling structures.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ntwene-nkuma guina yɛ na okuafo ketewa tumi nya ase anaa?
Twi Answer: Ntwene-nkuma guina yɛ aduan guina a wɔde ntwene nkuma so ma aduan tena yie bere tenten. Okuafo ketewa tumi nya ase wɔ: okuafo cooperative a wɔwɔ ntwene-nkuma guina bom, ɔman ntwene-nkuma guina centres, onipa hɔ ntwene-nkuma guina nnwuma a wɔsua crate anaa kilogram biara, mobile ntwene-nkuma guina trucks, ne evaporative coolers a ɛboɔ yɛ ketewa a wɔhyɛ electricity mu.

English Question: Dry seeds thoroughly to less than 10% moisture. Sort and remove damaged, diseased, or small seeds. Place in airtight containers — glass jars, tins, or sealed plastic bags. Add a small packet of silica gel or a tablespoon of powdered milk wrapped in cloth to absorb moisture. Store in a cool, dark, dry place. Label with crop name, variety, and date. Test germination before planting season.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meguina m'aba yie ma bere a ɛto so?
Twi Answer: Yaw aba no yie na ɛsua nsukuro 10%. Si na yi aba a asɛe, a yadeɛ aka, anaa a wɔkum. De aba to nkuku a apo so — glass jar, tin, anaa sealed plastik bag. De silica gel kotoku ketewa anaa powdered milk tablespoon baako a wɔde ntama sɛɛ no ka ho sɛ ɛsuo nsukuro. Guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru, ɛsum, na yera. Kyerɛw nnuaba din, aba din, ne da. Hwɛ aba pue ansa na bere aba.

English Question: Sell directly at local markets, to aggregators or food processing companies, or form a cooperative with other farmers. Register with government programs like PFJ which helps connect farmers to buyers.
Twi Question: Ɛhe na metumi de m'afuo nnuaba tɔn na nya boɔ pa?
Twi Answer: Tɔn tɔtɔ wɔ aguabasa a ɛbɛn wo, anaa wɔ aduan yɛ adeɛ kuo, anaa si cooperative ne okuafo foforɔ. Kyerɛw wo din wɔ ɔman adwuma te sɛ PFJ a ɛboa okuafo ayɔnkofa ne adeɛtɔfo.

English Question: Access agricultural loans through GIRSAL, rural banks, microfinance institutions, and cooperatives. Have a farm business plan ready, register your farm officially, and consult your local MOFA office for guidance.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menya ka sɛ meyɛ okuafo adwuma?
Twi Answer: Nya okuafo adwuma ka wɔ GIRSAL, ɔmansin ban, microfinance kuro, ne cooperatives mu. Wɔ wo afuo adwuma dwumadie plan, kyerɛw wo afuo din wɔ ɔman hɔ yie, na bisa wo MOFA ofisi wɔ beae a ɛbɛn wo.

English Question: Profit equals Total Sales Revenue minus Total Costs. Track all expenses including seeds, fertilizer, labor, transport, and chemicals and all income from sales. Keep a simple notebook or use your phone to record daily expenses.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na melem m'afuo ho mfaaso?
Twi Answer: Mfaaso yɛ sika nyinaa a wogye fi tɔn no minus sika nyinaa a wode. Kora sika nyinaa a wode ka ho te sɛ aba, ferefere, dwumadie, kwan so sika, dawuro, ne sika nyinaa a wogye fi tɔn. Kora krataa ketewa anaa fa wo fɔn de kora da biara ho sika.

English Question: Yes, cooperatives offer many benefits including group purchasing of inputs at lower prices, collective selling for better prices, access to credit, shared equipment, training, and stronger negotiating power with buyers and government.
Twi Question: Ɛsɛ sɛ meba okuafo kuo mu anaa?
Twi Answer: Aane, cooperative de mfaaso bebree brɛ: kuo to adenneɛ ketewa mu, kuo tɔn sɛ wanya boɔ pa, nya ka, fa egyapade bom, nyansapɔ, na kuo tumi yɛ kɛse sen wɔ adeɛtɔfo ne ɔman ho nsɛm mu.

English Question: Process raw produce into higher-value products: dry and package grains, make tomato paste, gari from cassava, or palm oil from palm fruits. Value addition reduces post-harvest losses and increases income.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mede boɔ ka m'afuo nnuaba ho sɛ menya sika dodo?
Twi Answer: Yɛ aduan foforo no yɛ aduan a wɔtɔ boɔ kɛse: yaw na paka nnuaba a ayaw, yɛ ntomato paste, gari fi bankye, anaa ngo fi abe aba. Boɔ to so maa mpampa post-harvest mpoano ne ma sika dodo.

English Question: Use ventilated crates or baskets not plastic bags for vegetables and fruits. Harvest early morning and transport before midday heat. Avoid overloading to prevent bruising. Cover produce with wet sacks to keep cool. For grains use clean dry bags. Sell same day for perishables whenever possible.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mede m'nnuaba kɔ aguabasa a ɛnkɔ ase?
Twi Answer: Fa afidie a mframa pue mu anaa akete na mfa plastik bags nsɛ nnuan ne aba. Gye owia da ano na de kɔ ansa na awia mu ahuhuro aba. Bɔ hwɛ de dodo hye mu sɛ ɛnhow. De ntama nte sɛɛ nnuaba so sɛ ɛkora wɔn ase huru. Nnuaba a ayaw ho, fa bags horo ne kraen.

English Question: A market information system provides farmers with current prices of crops at different markets so they can decide where and when to sell for the best price. In Ghana, services like Esoko, the Ghana Commodity Exchange (GCX), and MOFA market information services provide this. Access via phone, radio, or internet. This prevents farmers from being cheated by middlemen who know prices but farmers don't.
Twi Question: Dɛn na aguabasa nsɛm system yɛ na ɛboa okuafo sɛn?
Twi Answer: Aguabasa Nsɛm system de nnuaba boɔ a ɛwɔ aguabasa ahodoɔ so ma okuafo sɛ wɔtumi paw beae ne bere a wɔbɛtɔn sɛ wanya boɔ pa. Wɔ Ghana, nnwuma te sɛ Esoko, Ghana Commodity Exchange (GCX), ne MOFA aguabasa nsɛm nnwuma de eyi brɛ. Nya ase wɔ fɔn, redio, anaa internet so. Eyi mma okuafo anko ase wɔ middlemen a wɔnim boɔ nanso okuafo nnim ntam.

English Question: Crop insurance protects farmers against losses from drought, floods, pests, or other disasters by paying compensation when crops fail. In Ghana, the Ghana Agricultural Insurance Pool (GAIP) offers index-based weather insurance for farmers. Premiums are affordable and payouts are based on weather data not individual farm assessment. Contact MOFA or your cooperative to learn how to enroll.
Twi Question: Dɛn na nnuaba ho nsirɛ yɛ na okuafo Ghana tumi nya ase anaa?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba ho nsirɛ kora okuafo fi nnuaba ko a ɛba fi nsuo pa, nsuo tenten, adwummakers, anaa ɔkɔm foforɔ ho wɔ de sika brɛ wɔn bere a nnuaba nwu. Wɔ Ghana, Ghana Agricultural Insurance Pool (GAIP) de index-based weather insurance ma okuafo. Premium no boɔ yɛ ketewa na wɔde ɛwim nsɛm mmu ka ne afuo biara nhwɛ. Ka kyerɛ MOFA anaa wo cooperative sɛ wuhu ɛdeɛn na wosi wo din.

English Question: To price fairly, calculate your total production cost per unit (cost of seeds, fertilizer, labor, transport, etc. divided by total harvest). Add a profit margin of at least 20-30%. Check current market prices for similar produce in your area. Your price should cover all costs plus give you profit. Never sell below your production cost even if market prices are low.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesiesie m'afuo nnuaba boɔ yie?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ siesie boɔ yie a, lem wo adwuma ho sika nyinaa wɔ nnuaba biara so (aba, ferefere, dwumadie, kwan so sika, ne deɛ aka no, kyɛ nyinaa wɔ nnuaba a wogye no nyinaa so). Ka mfaaso a ɛsua 20-30% ho. Hwɛ boɔ a wɔde tɔn nnuaba te sɛ wo de wɔ wo beae. Wo boɔ sɛ akata sika nyinaa a wode na ma wo mfaaso. Mto da wɔ wo adwuma ho sika ase bere a aguabasa boɔ ayɛ sua.

English Question: Key government programs for farmers in Ghana include: Planting for Food and Jobs (PFJ) which provides subsidized seeds and fertilizers; Rearing for Food and Jobs for livestock; Ghana Commercial Agriculture Project (GCAP) for commercial farmers; Youth in Agriculture Program; and the Agricultural Development Bank (ADB) loans. Contact your district MOFA office for current programs available in your area.
Twi Question: Ɔman boa adwuma bɛn na ɛwɔ ho ma okuafo wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Ɔman adwuma titiriw a ɛwɔ ho ma okuafo wɔ Ghana ne: Planting for Food and Jobs (PFJ) a ɛde aba ne ferefere a wɔatwa boɔ brɛ; Rearing for Food and Jobs ma mmoa; Ghana Commercial Agriculture Project (GCAP) ma tɔntɔn okuafo; Youth in Agriculture Program; ne Agricultural Development Bank (ADB) ka. Ka kyerɛ wo district MOFA ofisi ma adwuma a ɛwɔ hɔ wɔ wo beae saa ara.

English Question: The Ghana Commodity Exchange (GCX) is a formal marketplace where farmers can sell their produce at transparent, standardized prices. To use it: register as a member through an accredited warehouse operator, store your certified grain in a GCX-accredited warehouse, receive a warehouse receipt that you can sell at the exchange or use as collateral for a bank loan. It is especially good for maize, soya, and sorghum.
Twi Question: Dɛn na Ghana Commodity Exchange yɛ na ɛdeɛn na mefa di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Ghana Commodity Exchange (GCX) yɛ aguabasa a ɛwɔ ho yie a okuafo tumi tɔn wɔn nnuaba wɔ boɔ a wɔada adi ne a wɔasiesie. Sɛ wohwehwɛ fa di dwuma a, kyerɛw wo din wɔ accredited warehouse operator ho, guina wo nnuaba a wɔakyerɛw wɔ GCX-accredited warehouse mu, nya warehouse receipt a wobetumi tɔn wɔ exchange no mu anaa de kɔ ban ho sɛ collateral. Ɛyɛ adwuma yie pa ara ma aburow, soya, ne ɔtɛ.

English Question: During drought, mulch heavily to conserve soil moisture, irrigate if possible, choose drought-tolerant crop varieties, and avoid adding nitrogen fertilizer which increases water demand. Harvest early-maturing varieties before drought peaks.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ m'afuo so bere a nsuo pa?
Twi Answer: Bere a nsuo pa no, de mulch to asase so yiye sɛ nsukuro wo mu, de nsuo to nnua so sɛ wonya tumi, paw nnuaba aba a ɛtumi nsuo pa so, na bɔ hwɛ de nitrogen ferefere to sɛ ɛma nnuaba hia nsuo dodo. Gye nnuaba a wɔware ntɛm ansa na nsuo pa yɛ dodo.

English Question: After flooding, make drainage channels to remove excess water quickly. Allow soil to drain before entering with heavy machinery. Check plants for root rot and remove severely damaged ones. Apply potassium fertilizer to help plants recover. Be alert for increased fungal diseases after flooding.
Twi Question: Osu tenten ma nsuo hyɛɛ m'afuo mu. Dɛn na meyɛ?
Twi Answer: Nsuo tu akyi, yɛ mmɔnkyemmonkyem sɛ nsuo no pue ntɛm. Ma asase no ntena ansa na wode egyapade kɛse ba mu. Hwɛ nnuaba ntini ho sɛ wɔasɛe na yi a wɔasɛe kɛse. De potassium ferefere to so sɛ ɛboa nnuaba no sane aba.

English Question: Lodging from wind can be managed by carefully straightening and mounding soil around fallen plants within 24-48 hours. However if the stem is broken recovery is unlikely. To prevent lodging choose short-stalked varieties and avoid excessive nitrogen.
Twi Question: Mframa tumi buu m'aburow nnua. Wɔtumi sane aba anaa?
Twi Answer: Wobetumi hwɛ nnua a mframa ato wɔn ase no ase wɔ de asase de si wɔn ho pɛ wɔ dafe 24-48 mu. Nanso sɛ tibo no apae a, ɛnyɛ ɔkorɔ sɛ wɔsane ba. Sɛ wohwehwɛ kora ase a, paw aba a wɔn tiboo tia na kora nitrogen ferefere ase.

English Question: Watch for natural signs such as flowering of certain trees, behavior of birds, and increased humidity. Check Ghana Meteorological Agency forecasts on radio, TV, or their website. Local MOFA extension officers often share seasonal forecasts. Planting too early before rains establish risks seed loss.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim bere a osu reba?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ nhwiren foforo nsɛm te sɛ nnua bi abode, anomaa biribi, ne huhu a ɛresor. Hwɛ Ghana Meteorological Agency amanneɛ wɔ redio, TV, anaa wɔn website so. MOFA extension officers a ɛbɛn wo no taa kyɛ bere amanneɛ. To aba ntɛm dodo ansa na osu reba retwe aba no sɛe.

English Question: Control weeds by timely hand weeding in the first 3-4 weeks after planting, using mulch to suppress weeds, and applying pre-emergence herbicides at planting. The first weeding must be done within 2-3 weeks after crop emergence.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ nhaban a ɛntia asɛm yie a mennya sika koraa?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ nhaban foforo ase wɔ nnafoa 3-4 a aburow pue akyi no mu, fa mulch kora nhaban foforo ase, na de herbicide to ansa na nnuaba pue. Nhaban foforo tia a ɛdi ɛkan no yɛ wɔ nnafoa 2-3 mu a nnuaba pue akyi.

English Question: Intercropping means growing two or more crops together on the same land. For example, maize with cowpea. Benefits include better land use, the legume adds nitrogen to the soil, reduced pest pressure, and income from two crops.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛyɛ intercropping na ɛboa?
Twi Answer: Intercropping kyerɛ sɛ wokura nnuaba abien anaa dodo wɔ asase koro so. Nhwɛso so, aburow ne abɔdweɛ. Mfaaso ho ne: asase ho dwuma pa, abɔdweɛ de nitrogen ma asase, adwummakers hia sua, na nnuaba abien firi sika.

English Question: Weed at least twice per season — first weeding within 2-3 weeks of planting and second weeding 4-6 weeks after planting. After this, crop canopy usually shades out weeds. Maize is most sensitive to weeds in the first 30-40 days after planting.
Twi Question: Mmmere ahe na msɛ meyɛ nhaban foforo tia wɔ m'afuo mu?
Twi Answer: Tia nhaban foforo mmere abien pɛ wɔ bere biara — nhaban tia a ɛdi ɛkan wɔ nnawotwe 2-3 a wode aba to mu akyi na nhaban tia a ɛto so abien wɔ nnawotwe 4-6 akyi. Eyi akyi, nnuaba nhaban taa sɛɛ nhaban foforo ase.

English Question: Keep a simple farm diary or notebook. Record planting dates, inputs purchased and costs, labor hired and paid, crop activities, harvest quantities, and sales. Simple mobile apps or voice memos on your phone can help record activities easily.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekora m'afuo nsɛm?
Twi Answer: Kora afuo krataa anaa nsɛmpoma ketewa. Kora aba to da, adenneɛ a wotɔ ne won boɔ, dwumadie a wohwɛ ne sika a wode twaa, afuo adwuma, nnuaba a wogye, ne tɔn nsɛm. Mobile apps ketewa anaa kasa nkrataa wɔ wo fɔn no tumi boa wo kora nsɛm yie.

English Question: Measure your farm using a measuring tape, GPS app like Google Maps, or by counting paces where 100 paces by 100 paces is approximately 0.2 acres. Alternatively your local MOFA office can help measure your farm.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim m'afuo boɔ wɔ acres mu?
Twi Answer: Sus wo afuo wɔ susudua, GPS app te sɛ Google Maps anaa OsmAnd, anaa kan tɔntɔn a tɔntɔn 100 ne tɔntɔn 100 yɛ bɛn acres 0.2. Anoa, wo MOFA ofisi a ɛbɛn wo no tumi boa wo su wo afuo.

English Question: Manage farm labor by: planning activities in advance and knowing how many workers you need for each task, hiring skilled workers for technical tasks and using family labor for routine work, paying fair wages on time to retain good workers, organizing communal labor (nnoboa) with neighboring farmers to reduce costs, tracking time spent on each activity to identify inefficiencies, and using appropriate tools to reduce manual labor.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ afuo dwumadie yie?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ afuo dwumadie wɔ: dwumadie siesie ansa na ɛba na nim obi dodo a wohia ma adwuma biara, fa obi a onim adwuma ma adwuma a ɛhia nyansam na fa abusua adwuma ma adwuma a wɔtaa yɛ, tua dwumadie sika a ɛfata bere a ɛsɛ sɛ wokora adwumfo pa, si nnoboa ne okuafo a wɔbɛn wo sɛ mpampa sika, kora bere a wɔde yɛ adwuma biara so sɛ wuhu beae a enni adwuma pa, na fa adeɛ a ɛfata di dwuma sɛ mpampa nsa adwuma.

English Question: A farm map is a simple drawing or diagram showing your farm layout including field boundaries, crops in each area, water sources, access roads, trees, and infrastructure. It helps you: plan crop rotations, track what was planted where, plan irrigation and drainage, apply for land certificates, and communicate with extension officers and banks. You can draw it by hand or use free GPS apps on your phone.
Twi Question: Dɛn na afuo map yɛ na ɛsɛ sɛ meyɛ baako adɛn?
Twi Answer: Afuo map yɛ kyerɛwee anaa diagram ketewa a ɛkyerɛ wo afuo anammɔn a mu wɔ afuo nkyɛn, nnuaba a ɛwɔ beae biara mu, nsuo, kwan, nnua, ne adwumafie. Ɛboa wo sɛ: siesie nnuaba sesae, kora nsɛm a wode aba to mu wɔ beae bɛn, siesie nsuo to ne nsuo pue anammɔn, bisa asase krataa, na kasa ne extension officers ne ban. Wobetumi kyerɛw wo nsa so anaa fa GPS apps daa wɔ wo fɔn so.

English Question: Reduce transport losses by: harvesting at the right maturity, grading and sorting produce before transport, using appropriate packaging (ventilated crates for fresh produce, strong sacks for grains), loading carefully to prevent crushing, traveling during cool hours (early morning or night), using roads that avoid excessive vibration, and selling as close to the farm as possible to reduce transport distance.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi sua mpoano a ɛba fi kwan so anammɔn bɔne ho?
Twi Answer: Sua kwan so mpoano wɔ: gye nnuaba bere a ɛsɛ, si ne yi nnuaba ansa na wede kɔ, fa packaging a ɛfata (afidie a mframa pue mu ma nnuaba foforo, kotoku den ma nnuaba a ayaw), de adwuma yie sɛ ɛnhow, kɔ bere a ɛhuru (owia da ano anaa anadwo), fa kwan a wonyi nnuaba no dodo, na tɔn a ɛbɛn afuo so ara sɛ sua kwan asukyerɛ.

English Question: Precision farming means using data and technology to apply exactly the right amount of inputs at the right time and place. Smallholders can practice basic precision farming by: soil testing different parts of the field and applying fertilizer based on results, using mobile apps to track crop growth, monitoring pest and disease hotspots and targeting treatment, and keeping detailed farm records to identify what works best.
Twi Question: Dɛn na precision farming yɛ na okuafo ketewa tumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: Precision farming kyerɛ fa data ne technology di dwuma sɛ de adenneɛ a ɛfata to bere a ɛsɛ na beae a ɛsɛ. Okuafo ketewa tumi yɛ basic precision farming wɔ: hwɛ asase ahorow afuo mu na de ferefere to wɔ adwuma ho, fa mobile apps di dwuma sɛ kora nnuaba da sor, hwɛ adwumakers ne yadeɛ beae na hyɛ dawuro hɔ pɛ, na kora afuo nsɛm mu yiye sɛ wuhu dea yɛ adwuma pa.

English Question: Season planning should include: checking your budget and available resources, deciding which crops to grow based on market demand and land suitability, calculating input quantities needed and ordering in advance, arranging labor supply for peak periods, planning irrigation if needed, identifying buyers in advance, and reviewing what worked and what didn't in the previous season. Start planning at least 2 months before the season begins.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesiesie bere a ansa na ɛba?
Twi Answer: Bere siesie sɛ aka: hwɛ wo sika ne adenneɛ a wowɔ, paw nnuaba a wobɛkura wɔ aguabasa hia ne asase ho, lem adenneɛ dodo a wohia na tɔ ansa na bere aba, siesie obi a obɛyɛ adwuma wɔ bere a ɛhia dodo, siesie nsuo to sɛ ɛhia, hwehwɛ adeɛtɔfo ansa na bere aba, na hwɛ dea yɛ adwuma yie ne dea anyɛ yie wɔ bere a edi ɛkan. Fi siesie abosome 2 ansa na bere aba.

English Question: If your farm floods regularly, take these steps: dig drainage channels around and through the field to direct water away, create raised beds to keep plant roots above waterline, plant flood-tolerant crop varieties, install water pumps to remove standing water quickly, build earthen bunds around the field perimeter, and consider planting floating rice varieties if flooding is very severe and frequent.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ nsuo a ɛhyɛ m'afuo mu?
Twi Answer: Sɛ nsuo taa hye wo afuo mu a, yɛ eyi: hu mmɔnkyemmonkyem twa ne wɔ afuo mu de nsuo no kɔ, yɛ asase-sor afuo sɛ nnuaba ntini atena sor nsuo soronko, to aba a ɛtumi nsuo tenten ase hyɛ, si nsuo pumps sɛ yi nsuo a ɛda hɔ ntɛm, yɛ asase bɔ twa afuo no ho, na hwɛ fa floating rice aba sɛ nsuo tenten taa ba na ɛyɛ dodo.

English Question: Protect your farm by: building proper fencing with thorny hedges or wire fencing, using watchdogs especially at harvest time, forming community vigilance groups with neighboring farmers, harvesting promptly when crops are ready to minimize field time after ripening, installing basic alarm systems if affordable, registering your farm to establish legal ownership, and developing good relationships with neighboring community members.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekora m'afuo fi korɔmfo ho?
Twi Answer: Kora wo afuo wɔ: si fense yie wɔ nkyerɛ nhwiren anaa wire, fa ɔkraman kora titiriw bere a wogye nnuaba, si kuo ne okuafo a wɔbɛn wo sɛ wɔhwɛ so, gye nnuaba ntɛm bere a ɛawie ase sɛ afuo mu bere sua akyi a nnuaba awi, si basic alarm sɛ sika wɔ ho, kyerɛw wo afuo din sɛ wunya asase krataa yie, na yɛ abakɔsɛm yie ne oman mu nnipa a wɔbɛn wo.

English Question: Crush 500g of neem seeds, soak in 10 litres of water overnight, strain through cloth, and add a little soap. Spray on crops in early morning or evening. Neem controls aphids, whiteflies, and caterpillars. Reapply after rain.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ neem adwummakers dawuro wɔ fie?
Twi Answer: Tutu neem aba 500g, da wɔ nsuo litre 10 mu anadwo koro, hun wɔ ntama mu, na de sapo kakra ka ho. Guare nnuaba so owia da ano anaa anwummere. Neem kora aphid, fitaa abowa, ne aborɔnoma ase yie. De to so bio nsuo akyi.

English Question: Organic farming means growing crops without synthetic chemicals or fertilizers, using only natural inputs like compost, manure, neem, and biological pest controls. It improves soil health over time, is safer for consumers, and can command premium prices in some markets.
Twi Question: Dɛn na nhwiren foforo okuafo adwuma yɛ?
Twi Answer: Nhwiren Foforo Okuafo Adwuma kyerɛ sɛ wokura nnuaba a womfa chemical anaa ferefere ahemfie bi, na wode nhwiren foforo adenneɛ pɛ te sɛ compost, aguare, neem, ne nhwiren adwummakers kontrol. Ɛsiesie asase mu yiye bere akyi, ɛho tumi na adeɛtɔfo, na wobetumi tɔn boɔ kɛse wɔ aguabasa bi mu.

English Question: Mulching covers soil with dry grass, straw, leaves, or plastic and conserves soil moisture reducing watering by 50%, regulates soil temperature, suppresses weed growth, and adds organic matter as it decomposes. Apply 5-10cm thick around plants.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mulching boa m'afuo?
Twi Answer: Mulching sɛɛ asase wɔ atɛntɛnni kraen, tow, nhaban, anaa plastik na ɛkora nsukuro wɔ asase mu ma nsuo to sua 50%, siesie asase osu, kora nhaban foforo ase, na de nhwiren foforo ka ho bere a ɛadwo. De sɛntimita 5-10 to nnuaba ho.

English Question: Plant marigolds, basil, garlic, or neem trees around your farm or between crop rows. These release compounds that deter many insects. Pyrethrum is very effective. Push-pull farming uses Desmodium grass between crop rows to repel stemborers.
Twi Question: Nnuaba bɛn na metumi kura sɛ wɔkora adwummakers ase nhwiren ho?
Twi Answer: To marigold, basil, gyene kokoo, anaa neem nnua wo afuo ho anaa wɔ nnuaba ntam. Wɔn pue nhwiren a ɛtete adwummakers bebree. Pyrethrum yɛ adwuma pa ara. Push-pull farming de Desmodium atɛntɛnni to nnuaba ntam sɛ ɛkora stemborer ase yie pa ara.

English Question: Composting is turning organic waste into natural fertilizer. Mix green materials like grass and vegetable waste with brown materials like dry leaves and straw in a pile. Keep it moist and turn it every 2 weeks. After 2-3 months you will have rich compost ready for your farm.
Twi Question: Dɛn na composting yɛ na ɛdeɛn na meyɛ no?
Twi Answer: Composting yɛ dan nhwiren foforo asennua yɛ nhwiren ferefere. Ka nhwiren foforo adeɛ te sɛ atɛntɛnni ne nnuan asennua ka bom ne nhwiren ɛda adeɛ te sɛ nhaban kraen ne tow wɔ bɔ koro. Ma ɛnte na tware no nnawotwe 2 biara. Abosome 2-3 akyi wobɛnya compost pa.

English Question: Biochar is charcoal made from organic matter that improves soil when added. To make it: dig a pit or use a metal drum, fill with dry crop residues, wood chips, or husks, ignite and let it burn slowly with limited air (not fully exposed to oxygen), cover when partially charred to stop burning, let it cool, crush into small pieces, mix with compost before adding to soil. Biochar lasts in soil for hundreds of years and improves water and nutrient retention.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ biochar sɛ siesie asase?
Twi Answer: Biochar yɛ efi a wɔyɛ fi nhwiren foforo a ɛsiesie asase bere a wɔde ka ho. Yɛ no eyi: hu tumtum anaa fa metal drum, hye nnuaba nsennua a ayaw, dua bi anaa nkuto mu, hyew na ma ɛhye brɛ brɛ a mframa ketewa wɔ mu (amfa oxygen mu pɛpɛɛpɛ), sɛɛ bere a ɛrehye kakra sɛ ɛnhye bio, ma ɛhuru, tutu yɛ mmerɛ, ka compost ho ansa na wode ka asase ho. Biochar tena asase mu mfe ahabiri na ɛsiesie nsuo ne aduan guina.

English Question: Vermicomposting uses earthworms to break down organic waste into very high-quality compost called vermicompost or worm castings. To start: get a container or build a wooden box, add bedding of moist shredded newspaper or cardboard, add earthworms (red wigglers are best), feed with fruit and vegetable scraps, coffee grounds, and eggshells. Avoid meat, dairy, and oily food. Harvest the rich compost from the bottom every 2-3 months.
Twi Question: Dɛn na vermicomposting yɛ na ɛdeɛn na mesi ase?
Twi Answer: Vermicomposting fa asase nwirɛntwi di dwuma sɛ pɛ nhwiren foforo asennua yɛ compost a ɛwɔ aduan pa pa ara a wɔfre vermicompost anaa worm castings. Sɛ wohwehwɛ si ase: nya nkuku anaa yɛ dua box, de krataa anaa cardboard a wɔatwa twa na wɔapo mu de yɛ mpa, de asase nwirɛntwi hyɛ (red wiggler yɛ pa pa ara), de nnuan ne aba asennua, coffee, ne kosua nkuku hyɛ. Bɔ hwɛ nam, nkyene aduan, ne ngo aduan. Gye compost a ɛwɔ ase hɔ no abosome 2-3 biara.

English Question: Organic pest control methods for vegetables include: handpicking large insects and caterpillars, using physical barriers like row covers or netting, companion planting with pest-repelling plants, spraying with homemade neem oil, garlic, or chili solutions, attracting beneficial insects with flowering plants, using kaolin clay sprays to confuse insects, and maintaining healthy soil and plants as the best long-term defense.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora adwummakers ase nhwiren ho wɔ nnuan afuo mu?
Twi Answer: Nhwiren adwummakers kora anammɔn ma nnuan ne: twe adwummakers kɛse ne aborɔnoma wɔ nsa, fa akwantempon a wɔde nnuaba so te sɛ row covers anaa net, ka nnuaba a wɔkora adwummakers ase ho, guare fie neem dawuro, gyene, anaa mako a wɔayɛ, twe adwummakers pa wɔ abode nnuaba ho, fa kaolin clay guare sɛ ɛbue adwummakers no, na kora asase ne nnuaba aho yie sɛ anammɔn pa ara wɔ bere tenten mu.

English Question: Push-pull is a clever intercropping system developed in Africa that controls stemborers (the most destructive maize pest) without chemicals. Plant Desmodium grass between maize rows (it repels/pushes stemborers away) and Napier grass or Brachiaria around the field border (it attracts/pulls stemborers and traps them). Desmodium also fixes nitrogen and suppresses Striga weed. This system is free to maintain once established.
Twi Question: Dɛn na push-pull farming systɛm yɛ?
Twi Answer: Push-pull yɛ intercropping anammɔn ahorow a wɔyɛ wɔ Afrika a ɛkora stemborer (aburow adwummaker a ɛsɛe pa ara) ase a wɔmfa chemicals. To Desmodium atɛntɛnni wɔ aburow nnua ntam (ɛkora/push stemborer kɔ) na Napier atɛntɛnni anaa Brachiaria twa afuo no ho (ɛtwe/pull stemborer na gye wɔn). Desmodium nso fi nitrogen na kora Striga nhaban foforo ase. Anammɔn no yɛ daa akyi a wɔasi no yie.

English Question: Growing without any external inputs is very difficult and usually leads to low yields. However, you can minimize purchased inputs by: making your own compost and manure, saving your own open-pollinated seeds, making homemade organic pesticides, using crop rotation to naturally restore soil fertility, and relying on rainwater. This approach requires more knowledge and management but can be cost-effective for subsistence farming.
Twi Question: Metumi kura nnuaba a menhwɛ ho saa ara anaa?
Twi Answer: Kura a wonhwɛ ho adenneɛ biara yɛ den pa ara na taa ma nnuaba da sor sua. Nanso wobetumi sua adenneɛ a wotɔ wɔ: yɛ wo compost ne aguare ho, gye wo open-pollinated aba, yɛ fie nhwiren adwummakers dawuro, fa nnuaba sesae sɛ siesie asase ho nhwiren a enni sika, na fa osu nsuo. Anammɔn no hia nyansam ne hwɛ ase dodo nanso tumi yɛ adeɛ pa ma fie okuafo adwuma.

English Question: Harvest at the right time, handle produce gently to avoid bruising, dry grains properly, store in appropriate conditions, transport in ventilated containers, and sell quickly for perishables. Post-harvest losses in Ghana can reach 30-40%.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi yɛ na m'aduan a megye no akyi anko mpoano?
Twi Answer: Gye nnuaba bere a ɛsɛ, de nnuaba no a eye yie sɛ ɛnhow, yaw nnuaba a ayaw no yie, guina wɔ bae a ɛsɛ, de kɔ bae a mframa tumi pue mu, na tɔn ntɛm sɛ ɛyɛ aduan a ɛsɛe ntɛm. Ghana mu aduan a ɛko aseɛ wɔ gye akyi betumi kɔ 30-40%.

English Question: Spread grains on clean tarpaulins or raised drying platforms in the sun. Stir regularly for even drying. Avoid drying on bare soil which introduces dirt and moisture. Grains are dry enough when a handful feels cool not warm and hard seeds do not dent easily.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyaw m'nnuaba yie akyi a megye wɔn?
Twi Answer: To nnuaba wɔ tarpaulin horo anaa platform a ɛda sor wɔ owia mu. Sane wɔn pɛ sɛ wɔyaw pɛ. Bɔ hwɛ yaw wɔ asase firi so efisɛ ɛde fufuo ne nsuo ba mu. Nnuaba yaw yie bere a wo nsa a wode fa no yɛ huru na aba den nyi wɔ nsateaa ase ntɛm.

English Question: Avoid harvesting during wet conditions. Handle gently to prevent bruising. Store in cool shaded well-ventilated areas on raised surfaces. Remove and separate any rotting fruits immediately. Consider making tomato paste or drying to reduce losses. Transport in ventilated crates not plastic bags.
Twi Question: M'ntomato a megye wɔn resɛe ntɛm. Dɛn na metumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: Bɔ hwɛ gye bere a nsuo wɔ hɔ. De wɔn pɛ sɛ wɔnhow. Guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru, owia ntra mu, mframa pue mu na ɛda sor. Yi na twa ntomato a resɛe ntɛm ara. Fa tomato paste yɛ anaa yaw sɛ mpampa sika kɔ mpoano.

English Question: Harvest vegetables early in the morning when cool, handle gently, sort out damaged ones immediately, store in cool ventilated areas, and sell quickly. For leafy vegetables, wrap in damp cloth to extend freshness. Avoid long transport in hot conditions.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi sua nnuan a megye wɔn akyi mpoano?
