Twi Answer: Gye nnuan owia da ano bere a ɛhuru, de wɔn pɛ, yi a wɔasɛe ntɛm ara, guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru na mframa pue mu, na tɔn ntɛm. Nhaban nnuan ho, de ntama nte de sɛɛ wɔn sɛ ɛma wɔn tena pɛ.

English Question: Grading means sorting produce into quality categories based on size, color, shape, and freedom from defects. It is important because: buyers pay premium prices for Grade A produce, graded produce has longer shelf life when sorted, it builds trust with buyers and processors, it allows you to sell different grades to different markets, and it makes it easier to negotiate better prices. Grade A goes to supermarkets, Grade B to restaurants, Grade C to processors.
Twi Question: Dɛn na grading yɛ na ɛsɛ sɛ ɛyɛ papa sɛ wotɔn nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Grading kyerɛ yi nnuaba no mu wɔ aba ho pa ahodoɔ wɔ boɔ, rere, ahofã, ne mfomso a enni ho so. Ɛho hia efisɛ: adeɛtɔfo tua sika dodo ma Grade A nnuaba, nnuaba a wɔasi no mu tena yie bere tenten, ɛkyerɛ adeɛtɔfo ne adwuma kuo sɛ wobetumi de wɔn so, ɛma wo tumi tɔn Grade ahodoɔ wɔ aguabasa ahodoɔ, na ɛboa wo ne adeɛtɔfo siesie boɔ yie. Grade A kɔ supermarkets, Grade B kɔ adidibea, Grade C kɔ adwuma kuo.

English Question: Dry vegetables by: washing and slicing thinly, blanching (briefly boiling) leafy vegetables for 1-2 minutes before drying to preserve color and nutrients, spreading on clean raised drying racks in the sun, or using a solar dryer. Vegetables are dry when crisp and hard — usually 2-5 days in sun. Pack in sealed airtight bags and store in a cool dry place. Dried vegetables last 6-12 months and can be sold as a higher-value product.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ nnuan a ayaw sɛ wɔtena yie bere tenten?
Twi Answer: Yaw nnuan wɔ: hohoro na twa twa yie, blanch (hyew kakra) nhaban nnuan sɛntɔ 1-2 ansa na woyaw sɛ ɛkora wɔn rere ne aduan ho nhwiren, de to drying rack horo a ɛda sor wɔ owia mu, anaa fa solar dryer. Nnuan yaw wie bere a wɔyɛ den na wɔpae — taa nnafoa 2-5 wɔ owia mu. Paka wɔ bags a apo so na guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru ne yera. Nnuan a ayaw tena abosome 6-12 na wobetumi tɔn wɔ boɔ kɛse.

English Question: To make peanut butter: sort and remove damaged nuts, roast in a pan on low heat until golden brown (20-30 minutes), stir constantly to prevent burning, remove skins while warm, grind in a blender or milling machine until smooth, add salt to taste, and pack in clean sealed containers. Can add a little vegetable oil if too thick. Homemade peanut butter sells well and has a 2-3 month shelf life at room temperature.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ nkatie betere fi nkatie mu?
Twi Answer: Yɛ nkatie betere eyi: yi na si nnuaba a asɛe, hyew wɔ pan so ogya sua mu kosi sɛ ɛdan hoho bɔɔ (sɛntɔ 20-30), sane pɛ sɛ ɛnhyew, yi nkuto a ɛwɔ so bere a ɛhuru, blend wɔ blender anaa mill mu kosi sɛ ɛyɛ mmerɛ, de ɛwa ka ho sɛ dɛm, na paka wɔ nkuku horo a apo so. Tumi de vegetable dawuro kakra ka ho sɛ ɛhwa pa dodo. Fie nkatie betere tɔn yie na ɛtena abosome 2-3 wɔ fie osu mu.

English Question: To process palm oil at home: harvest fresh bunches and ferment for 3-5 days to loosen fruits, thresh fruits from the bunch, boil fruits for 30-60 minutes until soft, pound or press to separate oil from fiber, add water and boil the pulp again, skim oil from the surface, filter through cloth, boil the filtered oil to remove water (until bubbling stops), and cool before storing in sealed containers. Traditional palm press improves extraction efficiency.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ ngo wɔ fie?
Twi Answer: Yɛ ngo wɔ fie eyi: gye bɔ foforo na ma wɔn da nnafoa 3-5 sɛ aba no pae yie, gye aba fi bɔ no ho, hyew aba no sɛntɔ 30-60 kosi sɛ wɔyɛ mmerɛ, tutu anaa pɛm sɛ yi ngo fi nsennua mu, de nsuo ka aba no ka ho na hyew bio, yi ngo fi so, hun wɔ ntama mu, hyew ngo a wɔahun no sɛ yi nsuo (kosi sɛ bubble ahwie), na ma ɛhuru ansa na waguina wɔ nkuku a apo so. Traditional palm press boa sɛ wunya ngo dodo.

English Question: Cassava value-added products include: gari (fermented and roasted cassava), fufu flour, cassava flour for baking, cassava chips (dried slices), cassava starch for industrial use, kokonte (dried cassava), and high-quality fufu. Each step of processing adds value and income. Gari is especially popular and can double the income from fresh cassava. Consider forming a women's group to process together to reduce costs and increase volumes.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mede boɔ ka bankye ho sɛ menya sika dodo?
Twi Answer: Bankye ho adwuma a wɔde yɛ dodo ne: gari (bankye a wɔade na hyew), fufu mfurow, bankye mfurow ma bobe adwuma, bankye chips (slices a ayaw), bankye starch ma adwuma kuro, kokonte (bankye a ayaw), ne fufu a ɛwɔ aho pa. Adwuma biara a wɔde yɛ de boɔ ne sika ka ho. Gari pɛ pa ara na ɛtumi ma bankye foforo sika abien. Hwɛ si mmaa kuo sɛ wɔyɛ adwuma bom sɛ sua sika ne ma nnuaba dodo ba.

English Question: Pepper grows best in warm sunny conditions with well-drained fertile soil. Start seeds in a nursery then transplant 4-6 week old seedlings. Space 45-60 cm apart. Water regularly, stake tall plants, and apply balanced fertilizer.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura mako yie?
Twi Answer: Mako da sor pa wɔ owia mu na asase a nsuo pue mu yie na ɛwɔ aduan pa. Fi aba fi nursery, afei si nnuaba a wɔdin nnawotwe 4-6 wɔ wɔ beae foforɔ. Gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 45-60. De nsuo to so pɛ, si aduro nnua a wɔreden, na de ferefere pɛ to so.

English Question: Cowpea matures in 60-90 days depending on the variety. Harvest when pods turn yellow-brown and dry. For fresh green beans, harvest when pods are full but still green about 60 days after planting.
Twi Question: Bere ahe na ɛsɛ ma abɔdweɛ awie ase?
Twi Answer: Abɔdweɛ wie ase wɔ nnafoa 60-90 mu wɔ aba no ahodoɔ so. Gye bere a fidie no dan sika ɛda na ayera. Abɔdweɛ foforo ho, gye bere a fidie no ayɛ ma nanso ɛda koraa nnafoa 60 akyi a wode to mu.

English Question: Onions grow best in cool dry conditions. Plant sets or transplants in the dry season November to February in northern Ghana. Irrigate regularly. Harvest when tops fall over naturally. Dry in shade before storage.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura gyene wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu?
Twi Answer: Gyene da sor pa wɔ huru tirim na ɛyera. To sets anaa transplants wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu. De nsuo to so pɛ. Gye bere a wɔn tenten atu. Yaw wɔ owia sum ansa na waguina.

English Question: Watermelon needs well-drained sandy loam soil, warm temperatures, and plenty of sunlight. Space 1.5-2 m apart. Water deeply but infrequently. Apply potassium-rich fertilizer during fruiting. Harvest when the tendril near the fruit turns brown.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura watermelon yie?
Twi Answer: Watermelon hia asintiɛ asase a nsuo pue mu yie, owia mu, na owia hye pa. Gyae asukyerɛ mita 1.5-2. De nsuo to asase mu yiye nanso mmere pii bi. De potassium ferefere to so bere a aba reba. Gye bere a ntini a ɛbɛn aba no dan ɛda.

English Question: Prune cocoa trees regularly to remove dead wood and improve light. Apply recommended fertilizers. Control black pod disease by removing infected pods and spraying copper-based fungicides. Replace unproductive old trees with improved varieties.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi ma m'kookoo da sor dodo?
Twi Answer: Twa kookoo nnua so pɛ sɛ yi dua kum ne nnua a wɔawu fi mu na ma owia hyɛ mu. De ferefere a wɔaka to so. Kora black pod yadeɛ ase wɔ yi pods a wɔayarɛ na de copper fungicide guare so. Si nnua kedee a wonnya bi fi wɔn ho na de aba foforɔ a ɛda sor wɔ wɔn beae.

English Question: Black pod is caused by Phytophthora fungus and spreads in wet humid conditions. It turns pods black and destroys beans. Control by removing and burying infected pods, pruning trees for better air circulation, and spraying copper-based fungicides regularly during rainy season.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛma kookoo black pod yadeɛ na ɛdeɛn na metumi kora ase?
Twi Answer: Black pod fi Phytophthora fungus na ɛtete wɔ nsuo ne huhu mu. Ɛdan pods tuntum na ɛsɛe aba no. Kora ase wɔ yi ne sisie pods a wɔayarɛ, twa nnua so sɛ mframa pue mu yie, na de copper fungicide guare pɛ wɔ osu bere mu.

English Question: Ginger grows best in partially shaded humid conditions with rich well-drained soil. Plant rhizomes 5-7 cm deep spaced 20-30 cm apart. Keep soil moist and mulch heavily. Harvest after 8-10 months when leaves yellow and die back.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura kakaduro yie?
Twi Answer: Kakaduro da sor pa wɔ beae a owia tra mu kakra na ɛwɔ huhu, asase a ɛwɔ aduan pa na nsuo pue mu yie. De rhizomes to asase mu sɛntimita 5-7 na gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 20-30. Kora asase nte na de mulch to so papaapa. Gye abosome 8-10 akyi a nhaban no dan sika na awu.

English Question: Harvest sorghum when grain is hard, heads have turned their mature color, and moisture content is around 20-25%. Dry after harvest before storage. Harvest promptly to avoid bird damage.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na ɛsɛ sɛ megye ɔtɛ?
Twi Answer: Gye ɔtɛ bere a aba no ayɛ den, aba no dinn adan wɔn rere na nsukuro yɛ bɛn 20-25%. Yaw akyi a wogye ansa na waguina. Gye ntɛm sɛ anomaa mfomso anba.

English Question: Plantain responds well to organic matter such as manure and compost plus potassium-rich fertilizers. Apply NPK 15-15-15 at planting then top-dress with muriate of potash during bunch development. Potassium is critical for good bunch weight and disease resistance.
Twi Question: Ferefere bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ ma borɔdɔ?
Twi Answer: Borɔdɔ gye nhwiren foforo aduan pa te sɛ aguare ne compost a potassium ferefere ka ho yiye. De NPK 15-15-15 to mu bere a wode to mu afei de muriate of potash to so bere a aba reba. Potassium ho hia pa ara ma bɔ kɛse ne yadeɛ tumi.

English Question: Panama disease is a fatal fungal soil disease. Use certified disease-free planting material, avoid planting in previously infected soil, practice strict hygiene by cleaning tools before moving between farms, and plant resistant varieties like Cardaba or FHIA hybrids. There is no chemical cure.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora Panama yadeɛ ase wɔ borɔdɔ ne kwadu mu?
Twi Answer: Panama yadeɛ yɛ fungal asase yadeɛ a ɛkum. De aba a wɔakyerɛw wɔ ho a enni yadeɛ to mu, bɔ hwɛ to wɔ asase a yadeɛ aka ho ansa, yɛ ho tumi yie wɔ hohoro adeɛ ansa na wosesa afuo, na to aba a ɛtumi hyɛ ase te sɛ Cardaba anaa FHIA.

English Question: Plant plantain suckers from healthy mother plants. Choose planting material free from pests. Dig holes 60cm x 60cm x 60cm and fill with compost. Space plants 3m x 3m. Mulch heavily, water in dry periods, and apply potassium-rich fertilizer for good bunch development.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura borɔdɔ yie?
Twi Answer: To borɔdɔ aba fi nnua a wɔwɔ aho na wɔsom yie. Paw aba a enni adwummakers. Hu tumtum sɛntimita 60 x 60 x 60 na hye compost mu. Gyae asukyerɛ mita 3 x 3. De mulch to so papaapa, de nsuo to ɔpɛ bere mu, na de potassium ferefere to sɛ aba reba yie.

English Question: Popular rice varieties in Ghana include AGRA Rice, Jasmine 85, and NERICA varieties. NERICA varieties are resistant to drought and local pests. Contact your local MOFA extension officer for variety recommendations suited to your specific area.
Twi Question: Ɔmɔ aba bɛn na ɛda sor pa wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Ɔmɔ aba a wɔpɛ wɔ Ghana ho ne AGRA Rice, Jasmine 85, ne NERICA aba. NERICA aba tumi nsuo pa ne beae adwummakers ase hyɛ. Ka kyerɛ wo MOFA extension officer a ɛbɛn wo sɛ ɔka aba a ɛfata wo beae ho.

English Question: Cashew grows best in well-drained sandy or laterite soils in areas with a distinct dry season. Plant seeds directly 5 cm deep in the field or transplant seedlings. Space trees 8-10 meters apart. Apply fertilizer in the second year onward. Control collar rot disease, cashew stem and root borer insects, and anthracnose. Harvest nuts when the cashew apple turns yellow or red and the nut is dark grey. Cashew trees start producing at 3-5 years.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura cashew yie?
Twi Answer: Cashew da sor pa wɔ asase a nsuo pue mu yie a ɛyɛ asintiɛ anaa laterite wɔ beae a ɔpɛ bere wɔ hɔ. To aba tɔtɔ wɔ asase mu sɛntimita 5 anaa si nnuaba mfoforo ananmu. Gyae nnua asukyerɛ mita 8-10. De ferefere to mfe a ɛto so abien ananmu. Kora collar rot yadeɛ, cashew tibo ne ntini adwummakers, ne anthracnose ase. Gye aba bere a cashew apple no dan hoho anaa kɔkɔɔ na aba no dan tuntum-brɔdwa. Cashew nnua da sor fi mfe 3-5 akyi.

English Question: Soybeans are highly profitable legumes. Plant after rains are well established. Inoculate seeds with Bradyrhizobium bacteria before planting (this fixes nitrogen and can triple yields). Space 30-45 cm within rows and 60 cm between rows. Apply phosphorus fertilizer at planting. Weed once at 3 weeks. Harvest when 95% of pods have turned yellow-brown. Dry to 12% moisture before storage. Soybeans have strong demand from oil processors and animal feed manufacturers.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura soya yɛ adwuma sɛ menya sika?
Twi Answer: Soya yɛ abɔdweɛ a ɛde sika ba pa ara. To akyi a osu asi yie. De Bradyrhizobium bacteria ka aba ho ansa na woto (eyi fi nitrogen na ɛtumi ma nnuaba da sor mprɛ mmiɛnsa). Gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 30-45 wɔ ntam ne sɛntimita 60 wɔ nnua so ntam. De phosphorus ferefere to mu bere a wode to. Tia nhaban foforo bere a ɛto so mmiɛnsa no nnawotwe baako. Gye bere a 95% fidie no adan hoho bɔɔ. Yaw kosi 12% nsuku ansa na waguina. Soya hia yɛ kɛse wɔ ngo adwuma kuo ne mmoa aduan adwuma kuo ho.

English Question: Sweet potato grows best in well-drained sandy loam soil. Plant vine cuttings (30-40 cm long) not seeds, inserting 2/3 of the cutting into the soil. Space 30 cm apart on ridges 90 cm apart. Apply NPK at planting. Weed early. Harvest 3-5 months after planting when leaves begin to yellow. Sweet potato is drought-tolerant and can grow in poor soils — excellent for climate resilience. The leaves are also nutritious and can be eaten as vegetables.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura asikyire bankye yie?
Twi Answer: Asikyire bankye da sor pa wɔ asase a nsuo pue mu yie na ɛyɛ asintiɛ loam. To vine cuttings (sɛntimita 30-40 tenten) na mfa aba, de 2/3 wɔ cutting no to asase mu. Gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 30 wɔ ntwaho so a ɛgyae sɛntimita 90. De NPK to mu bere a wode to. Tia nhaban foforo ntɛm. Gye abosome 3-5 akyi a wode to mu bere a nhaban reredan hoho. Asikyire bankye tumi nsuo pa ase hyɛ na ɛtumi da sor wɔ asase a enni pa — ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ pa ara ma katawere mu sɛsae ho. Nhaban no nso wɔ aduan ho nhwiren ne wobetumi di sɛ nnuan.

English Question: Commercial pineapple production: plant suckers or crowns from healthy plants, space 60x30 cm on raised beds in rows, apply NPK fertilizer 3 times per year, force flowering by applying ethephon or acetylene solution at 12-14 months to synchronize harvest, control mealy bugs and heart rot disease, harvest 15-18 months after planting. MD2 and Smooth Cayenne are popular export varieties. Ghana exports significant volumes of pineapple to Europe.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura aborɔfo wɔ adwuma mu?
Twi Answer: Aborɔfo adwuma kura ho: to suckers anaa crowns fi nnua a wɔwɔ aho wɔ, gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 60x30 wɔ asase-sor afuo wɔ nnua so mu, de NPK ferefere to mprɛ mmiɛnsa bere biara, ma abode ba wɔ de ethephon anaa acetylene solution hyɛ wɔ bosome 12-14 akyi sɛ wogye bere koro, kora mealy bug ne heart rot yadeɛ ase, gye bosome 15-18 akyi a wode to mu. MD2 ne Smooth Cayenne yɛ export aba a wɔpɛ wɔn. Ghana de aborɔfo kɔ Yurop dodo.

English Question: Moringa is one of the most nutritious plants in the world and grows easily in Ghana. Plant seeds directly or use stem cuttings in well-drained soil. It tolerates drought and poor soils. Harvest leaves regularly to keep the tree short and productive. Moringa leaves can be eaten fresh, dried, and powdered. Benefits include: extremely high in iron, vitamins A and C, protein, and calcium. It is used medicinally and sold as a nutritional supplement at premium prices.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura moringa na mfaaso bɛn na ɛwɔ?
Twi Answer: Moringa yɛ nnua a ɛwɔ aduan ho nhwiren pa ara wɔ wiase mu na ɛda sor yie wɔ Ghana. To aba tɔtɔ anaa fa tibo cutting wɔ asase a nsuo pue mu yie. Ɛtumi nsuo pa ne asase a enni pa ase hyɛ. Gye nhaban pɛ sɛ ɛkora dua no tia ne adwuma mu. Moringa nhaban wobetumi di foforo, yaw na tutu. Mfaaso ho ne: iron, vitamins A ne C, protein, ne calcium ho yɛ dodo pa ara. Wɔde di dawuro adwuma na tɔn sɛ nutritional supplement wɔ boɔ kɛse.

English Question: Common cocoa nursery diseases include: collar rot (Phytophthora), damping off, and black pod. Control by: using sterilized potting mix, ensuring good drainage in nursery bags, avoiding overwatering, removing and destroying diseased seedlings immediately, maintaining good spacing for air circulation, spraying with copper-based fungicides preventatively, and ensuring nursery shade cloth allows 50% light penetration.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi kora yadeɛ ase wɔ m'kookoo nursery mu?
Twi Answer: Kookoo nursery yadeɛ a wɔtaa hu ne: collar rot (Phytophthora), nnuaba-mfoforo wu yadeɛ, ne black pod. Kora ase wɔ: fa potting mix a wɔasi amu, kora nsuo pue mu yie wɔ nursery bags, bɔ hwɛ nsuo dodo, yi ne seaa nnuaba mfoforo a wɔayarɛ ntɛm, kora asukyerɛ yie sɛ mframa pue mu, guare wɔ copper-based fungicide sɛ kora ase ansa na yadeɛ reba, na kora sɛ nursery shade cloth ma owia 50% pue mu.

English Question: Garden eggs grow best in warm conditions with well-drained fertile soil. Start seeds in a nursery and transplant 4-6 week old seedlings. Space 60x60 cm. Apply NPK at planting and top-dress with urea at 4 weeks. Stake plants when they get large. Watch for mites, aphids, and flea beetles. Harvest when fruits are still firm and glossy — over-ripe fruits become bitter. Garden eggs are popular in Ghanaian cuisine and have strong local market demand.
Twi Question: Anammɔn bɛn na ɛyɛ pa wɔ kura garden egg (Afrika ntrɔba)?
Twi Answer: Garden egg da sor pa wɔ ahuhuro mu na asase a nsuo pue mu yie ne aduan pa. Fi aba fi nursery na si nnuaba mfoforo a wɔdin nnawotwe 4-6 ananmu. Gyae asukyerɛ sɛntimita 60x60. De NPK to mu bere a wode to na de urea to so nnawotwe 4 akyi. Si aduro nnua no bere a wɔreyɛ kɛse. Hwɛ mite, aphid, ne flea beetle ho. Gye bere a aba no da den na hyerɛn — aba a ɛawi dodo yɛ dɛm den. Garden egg pɛ pa ara wɔ Ghana ɔman mu aduan ho na ɛwɔ aguabasa hia kɛse.

English Question: A simple farm business plan includes what you will grow and how much, land available, inputs needed and their costs, expected yield and selling price, total expected income, total costs, and expected profit. Also include risks and how you will manage them.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ afuo adwuma dwumadie plan ketewa?
Twi Answer: Afuo adwuma dwumadie plan ketewa mu wɔ: dea wobɛkura ne sɛn, asase a wowɔ, adenneɛ a hia ne wɔn boɔ, nnuaba a wobɛnya ne tɔn boɔ, sika nyinaa a wobɛnya, sika nyinaa a wode, ne mfaaso a wobɛnya. Ka nsɔhwɛ ne ɛdeɛn na wobɛyɛ sɛ wobɛhwɛ won ase.

English Question: Visit local markets to identify traders. Contact food processing companies and restaurants. Use phone or WhatsApp groups for farmers in your area. Signing contract farming agreements with companies before the season guarantees buyers and sometimes provides inputs on credit.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwehwɛ adeɛtɔfo ma m'afuo nnuaba ansa na megye wɔn?
Twi Answer: Kɔ aguabasa a ɛbɛn wo sɛ wuhu nnipa a wɔtɔn. Ka kyerɛ aduan yɛ adeɛ kuo ne adidibea. Fa fɔn anaa WhatsApp kuo ma okuafo wɔ wo beae. De contract farming agreement ka adeɛtɔ kuo bere a bere mfiase ansa na ɛma adeɛtɔfo yɛ dada.

English Question: Contract farming is an agreement between a farmer and a buyer before the season starts. The buyer agrees to purchase your produce at a fixed price after harvest. Benefits include guaranteed market, sometimes free inputs on credit, and technical support.
Twi Question: Dɛn na contract farming yɛ na ɛboa me sɛn?
Twi Answer: Contract farming yɛ apam a ɛda okuafo ne adeɛtɔ kuo ntam ansa na bere no aba. Adeɛtɔ kuo no ka ho sɛ wɔbɛtɔ wo nnuaba boɔ a wɔaka akyi a wogye. Mfaaso ho ne: aguabasa a wɔadaa ho, adenneɛ a wɔde brɛ wo ka mu mmere bi, ne nnwuma boa.

English Question: Start small and learn as you grow. Choose one or two crops you understand well for your first season. Keep records of everything. Seek advice from experienced farmers and extension officers. Join a farmer group or cooperative. Do not give up after one bad season. Farming is a dignified and profitable business when done well.
Twi Question: Adesua bɛn na wobɛma aberantemmaa a ɔresi okuafo adwuma ɛkan?
Twi Answer: Fi ketewa na sua bere a woda sor. Paw nnuaba baako anaa abien a wohu wɔn yie bere a ɛdi ɛkan. Kora nsɛm nyinaa. Hwehwɛ nnwuma boa fi okuafo a wɔnim adwuma no ne extension officers. Ba okuafo kuo mu. Mma bere koro a aannya yie no amma wo anhuri. Okuafo adwuma yɛ adwuma a ɛwɔ anuonyam na ɛde sika ba sɛ woyɛ no yie.

English Question: Registering your farm with MOFA gives you access to government subsidies, training, extension services, credit, and market linkages. Visit your local MOFA office or District Assembly with your ID and land documents. Registration is free and very beneficial.
Twi Question: Ɛsɛ sɛ mede m'afuo nkyerɛw?
Twi Answer: Wo afuo nkyerɛw wɔ MOFA de tumi ma wo sɛ wunya ɔman ho boa, nyansapɔ, extension nnwuma, ka, ne aguabasa ho kyɛfa. Kɔ wo MOFA ofisi anaa District Assembly a ɛbɛn wo wɔ wo nkyerɛwsɛm ne asase krataa. Nkyerɛw yɛ daa na ɛboa pa ara.

English Question: To sell as certified organic you need to farm organically for at least 3 years and pass inspection by an accredited certification body. In Ghana organizations like ENCOT and Control Union offer organic certification.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menya kratafa sɛ metɔn organic nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ tɔn organic nnuaba a wɔakyerɛw wɔn a, ɛsɛ sɛ woyɛ organic okuafo adwuma mfe 3 pɛ na wufa inspection a organic kuo yɛ. Wɔ Ghana, kuo te sɛ ENCOT ne Control Union de organic kratafa brɛ.

English Question: GlobalGAP (Good Agricultural Practices) is an international certification standard that verifies produce is grown safely and sustainably. It is required by most European supermarkets to import fresh produce. Getting certified opens doors to premium export markets. Requirements include: safe pesticide use with records, worker welfare, environmental protection, and food safety. In Ghana, groups like PFAG (Pesticide and Fertilizer Association of Ghana) can help farmers get certified.
Twi Question: Dɛn na GlobalGAP kratafa yɛ na ɛboa okuafo sɛ wɔde nnuaba kɔ amanaman?
Twi Answer: GlobalGAP (Good Agricultural Practices) yɛ amanaman kratafa nhyɛso a ɛkyerɛ sɛ nnuaba kura yie na ɛho tumi. Yurop supermarkets bebree hia sɛ na wɔde nnuaba foforo ba. Nya kratafa no bue aguabasa kɛse a wɔtɔn wɔn boɔ kɛse. Nhyɛso ho ne: adwummakers dawuro fa a ɛho tumi ne nsɛm kora, adwumafo ho hwɛ, ɛwim ho hwɛ, ne aduan ho tumi. Wɔ Ghana, kuo te sɛ PFAG (Pesticide and Fertilizer Association of Ghana) tumi boa okuafo nya kratafa.

English Question: To register your farm as a business in Ghana: register with the Registrar General's Department as a sole proprietorship or partnership (costs GHS 150-300), get a Tax Identification Number (TIN) from the Ghana Revenue Authority, register with MOFA for agricultural activities, open a business bank account, and get all required operating permits from your local assembly. A formally registered farm business is more credible to banks, buyers, and government programs.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mede m'afuo kyerɛw sɛ adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ kyerɛw wo afuo sɛ adwuma wɔ Ghana a: kyerɛw wɔ Registrar General's Department sɛ sole proprietorship anaa partnership (sika GHS 150-300), nya Tax Identification Number (TIN) fi Ghana Revenue Authority hɔ, kyerɛw wɔ MOFA ho ma okuafo adwuma, bue adwuma ban account, na nya kratafa biara a wohia fi wo local assembly. Afuo adwuma a wɔakyerɛw no yɛ pa ara wɔ ban, adeɛtɔfo, ne ɔman adwuma ho.

English Question: Fairtrade certification guarantees farmers a minimum price for their produce that covers production costs plus a social premium that is invested in community development. Benefits include: stable income even when world prices drop, Fairtrade premium funds for schools, health, and infrastructure, access to pre-financing before harvest, better trading relationships, and marketing support. Fairtrade is common in Ghana for cocoa, coffee, and fresh fruit. Contact Fairtrade Africa for information.
Twi Question: Dɛn na Fairtrade kratafa yɛ na mfaaso bɛn na ɛwɔ ho ma okuafo?
Twi Answer: Fairtrade kratafa hɔ kura sɛ okuafo nya boɔ a ɛdata wɔn nnuaba a ɛkata adwuma ho sika ne social premium a wɔde fa oman nkosuo mu. Mfaaso ho ne: sika a ɛda pɛ bere a amanaman boɔ tow, Fairtrade premium sika ma sukuu, yadeɛ, ne nkosuo adwuma, nya sika ansa na wogye nnuaba, adwuma ho apam a ɛyɛ pa, ne adwuma ho boa. Fairtrade pɛ wɔ Ghana ho ma kookoo, kɔfi, ne aba foforo. Ka kyerɛ Fairtrade Africa sɛ wunya nsɛm.

English Question: To sell agricultural chemicals (pesticides, fertilizers) in Ghana, you need: a license from the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), which requires completing a training course on pesticide handling, passing an examination, paying the licensing fee, having appropriate storage facilities, and renewing the license annually. Selling agricultural chemicals without a license is illegal and carries penalties. Contact the EPA Pesticides Control and Management Centre for the application process.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menya kratafa sɛ metɔn okuafo adwuma chemicals wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ tɔn okuafo adwuma chemicals (adwumakers dawuro, ferefere) wɔ Ghana a, wohia: kratafa fi Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), a ɛhia sɛ wo siesie adwummakers dawuro hwɛ suahu, fa exam mu, tua kratafa sika, wɔ guina fie a ɛfata, na sane kratafa mfe biara. Tɔn okuafo adwuma chemicals a wonni kratafa yɛ illegal na ɛwɔ akyinnye. Ka kyerɛ EPA Pesticides Control and Management Centre sɛ wuhu bisa anammɔn.

English Question: To qualify for agricultural loans, banks and microfinance institutions typically require: farm records showing area farmed and crops grown, sales records for at least one season, input purchase receipts, a farm business plan, MOFA registration certificate, land ownership or lease documents, a valid ID, and sometimes a guarantor. Start keeping records now even if you are not currently seeking a loan — it takes time to build a credible financial history that banks trust.
Twi Question: Nsɛm bɛn na ɛsɛ mekora sɛ menya okuafo adwuma ka?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ nya okuafo adwuma ka a, ban ne microfinance institutions taa hia: afuo nsɛm a ɛkyerɛ asase asukyerɛ ne nnuaba a wokura, tɔn nsɛm ma bere baako pɛ pɛ, adenneɛ tɔn krataa, afuo adwuma dwumadie plan, MOFA kyerɛwsɛm kratafa, asase wura anaa asɛ krataa, ID a ɛtia, na mmere bi obi a ɔbɛka ho. Fi kora nsɛm saa ara bere a wonhwehwɛ ka da — ɛhia bere sɛ si sika ho nsɛm a wɔgye di a ban tumi gye di.

English Question: Simple water harvesting includes digging half-moon catchments to collect rainwater, constructing check dams as small barriers across drainage channels, and building farm ponds lined with clay or plastic. Contact your local Water Resources Commission for technical support.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesi dam ketewa anaa nsuo gye sistɛm?
Twi Answer: Nsuo gye anammɔn ketewa ho ne: hu osu nsuo gye mmɔnkyemmonkyem, si check dams te sɛ akwantempon ketewa wɔ nsuo ntwaho nkyɛn, na tu afuo pond a wɔde amane anaa plastik si faako mu. Ka kyerɛ wo Water Resources Commission sɛ wunya nnwuma boa.

English Question: Construct a farm pond or dig a larger deeper well. Install a rainwater harvesting system collecting from rooftops into tanks during rainy season. Use water-efficient irrigation methods. Alternatively identify permanent water sources like rivers and use pumps.
Twi Question: M'esre yera wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu. Ɛdeɛn na metumi guina nsuo dodo?
Twi Answer: Tu afuo pond anaa hu esre kɛse ne tenten. Si osu nsuo gye sistɛm a wɔde fi ato so gye wɔ tank mu wɔ osu bere mu. Fa nsuo ho anammɔn a ɛfa nsuo nkyɛn. Anoa, hwehwɛ nsuo a ɛda hɔ pɛ te sɛ ɔsubɔnten na de pump fa di dwuma.

English Question: Conserve water by mulching heavily around plants to reduce evaporation, watering early morning or evening only, using drip irrigation which reduces water use by up to 60%, growing drought-tolerant crops, making windbreaks to reduce drying winds, and collecting and storing rainwater during wet season.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekora nsuo wɔ m'afuo mu wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu?
Twi Answer: Kora nsuo wɔ de mulch to nnuaba ho papaapa sɛ nsukyerɛ ba sua, de nsuo to owia da ano anaa anwummere pɛ, fa nsuo tete-tete kyɛ a ɛsua nsuo kɔ 60%, kura nnuaba a ɛtumi nsuo pa ase, si windbreaks sɛ mframa a ɛma asase yera nkɔ, na gye ne guina osu nsuo wɔ osu bere mu.

English Question: Essential tools for smallholder farming include a hoe and cutlass for land preparation and weeding, a watering can for irrigation, a knapsack sprayer for pesticide application, a measuring tape, storage bags including hermetic bags for grain, and a simple scale.
Twi Question: Adeɛ bɛn na mehia sɛ mesi afuo ketewa?
Twi Answer: Adeɛ a ɛhia wɔ afuo ketewa mu ne akɔde ne sekan ma asase siesie ne nhaban tia, nsuo kyɛ ma nsuo to, knapsack sprayer ma dawuro guare, susudua, guina bags a hermetic bags ka ho ma nnuaba, ne scale ketewa ma nnuaba sus.

English Question: After each use, rinse the tank three times with clean water and spray the wash water away from crops. Check and replace worn nozzles regularly. Lubricate the pump piston periodically. Store empty and clean in a cool dry area. Regularly inspect hoses and connections for leaks.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ m'knapsack sprayer so?
Twi Answer: Wodi dwuma biara akyi, hohoro nkuku no mprɛ mmiɛnsa wɔ nsuo horo na guare nsuo a wode hohoro no ho afi nnuaba ho. Hwɛ na sesa nozzle a asɛe pɛ. De ngo hyɛ pump no mu bere bi. Guina a ɛhoro wɔ bae a ɛhuru na yera. Hwɛ hose ne nnɔɔmu pɛ.

English Question: Agricultural extension officers from MOFA provide free advice and training to farmers. They can visit your farm to diagnose crop problems, recommend solutions, inform you about new varieties and technologies, connect you to government programs, and help you access subsidized inputs.
Twi Question: Dɛn na agricultural extension officer yɛ?
Twi Answer: Agricultural extension officers fi MOFA de boa ne nyansapɔ brɛ okuafo akyɛ. Wɔbetumi ba wo afuo so sɛ wuhwɛ nnuaba nsɛm, ka boa kyerɛ, kaa wo tia aba ne technology foforɔ ho, kyerɛ wo ɔman adwuma, na boa wo nya adenneɛ a wɔatwa wɔn boɔ.

English Question: Register with your local MOFA office and stay in contact with your extension officer. Subsidies like subsidized fertilizer and seeds under PFJ are distributed through MOFA-registered channels. Have your Ghana Card or voter ID ready and register early as subsidies are often limited.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menya ɔman okuafo adwuma boa?
Twi Answer: Kyerɛw wo din wɔ wo MOFA ofisi a ɛbɛn wo na tena wo extension officer ho. Boa te sɛ ferefere ne aba a wɔatwa boɔ wɔ PFJ ase no pue wɔ MOFA mu. Wura wo Ghana Card anaa ɔman nkyerɛwsɛm na kyerɛw wo din ntɛm efisɛ boa no taa yɛ ketewa.

English Question: Hybrid seeds are bred from two parent lines to produce vigorous high-yielding crops. However seeds saved from hybrids do not perform well in the next season — you must buy fresh seeds each time. Open-pollinated varieties allow you to save seeds for replanting.
Twi Question: Hybrid aba ne open-pollinated aba ntam yɛ dɛn?
Twi Answer: Wɔde aba abien ntam bɔ hybrid aba sɛ ɛma nnuaba a wɔwɔ ahoɔden na wɔda sor dodo. Nanso aba a wogye fi hybrid no nnua mu nti adwuma yie bere a ɛto so abien — ɛsɛ sɛ wotɔ aba foforo bere biara. Open-pollinated aba de tumi gye aba sɛ wode to mu bio.

English Question: For open-pollinated varieties select the best-performing plants and allow their fruits to fully mature on the plant. Harvest seeds, clean and dry them thoroughly in shade. Store in airtight containers with silica gel sachets to absorb moisture. Label with crop name, variety, and date.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na megye m'aba sɛ mede to mu wɔ bere a ɛto so?
Twi Answer: Open-pollinated aba ho, paw nnua a wɔda sor pa na ma wɔn aba no wie ase yie wɔ nnua so. Gye aba no, hohoro na yaw wɔ owia sum mu yie. Guina wɔ nkuku a apo so ne silica gel sachets a ɛsuo nsukuro. Kyerɛw nnuaba din, aba din ne da so.

English Question: Practice climate-smart farming by planting trees on your farm through agroforestry, using compost and manure instead of chemical fertilizers, practicing minimum tillage to protect soil carbon, using water-efficient irrigation, growing diverse crops, and avoiding burning crop residues.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ okuafo adwuma a ɛboa katawere mu sɛsae so?
Twi Answer: Yɛ climate-smart farming wɔ to nnua wɔ wo afuo so wɔ agroforestry ho, de compost ne aguare fa ahemfie ferefere ananmu, yɛ minimum tillage sɛ ɛkora asase carbon, fa nsuo-efficient irrigation, kura nnuaba ahorow, na bɔ hwɛ hyew nnuaba nsennua.

English Question: Drought-tolerant crops for Ghana's changing climate include improved NERICA rice, drought-tolerant maize varieties like Obatanpa and Omankwa, cowpea, sorghum, millet, and cassava. Contact CSIR-SARI or MOFA for the latest recommended varieties in your region.
Twi Question: Nnuaba bɛn na ɛtumi wiase tebea sɛsae ase hyɛ yie wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba a ɛtumi nsuo pa ase hyɛ wɔ Ghana tebea sɛsae mu ne NERICA ɔmɔ a wɔayɛ no foforo, aburow a ɛtumi nsuo pa ase te sɛ Obatanpa ne Omankwa, abɔdweɛ, ɔtɛ, ɔtɛ pa, ne bankye. Ka kyerɛ CSIR-SARI anaa MOFA sɛ wunya aba a wɔaka.

English Question: Agroforestry is growing trees alongside crops or livestock on the same land. Benefits include: trees provide shade that reduces water stress, tree roots hold soil and prevent erosion, fallen leaves add organic matter, some trees fix nitrogen improving soil fertility, trees provide fruit or timber as additional income, and trees help store carbon reducing climate change impact. Recommended trees include Moringa, Leucaena, and Acacia.
Twi Question: Dɛn na agroforestry yɛ na ɛboa m'afuo sɛn?
Twi Answer: Agroforestry yɛ kura nnua wɔ nnuaba anaa mmoa ho wɔ asase koro so. Mfaaso ho ne: nnua de ewim brɛ ma ɛma nsuo hia nkɔm, nnua ntini kora asase na ɛmma asase nhuru, nhaban a atu de nhwiren foforo ka ho, nnua bi fi nitrogen ma asase ho nhwiren da sor, nnua de aba anaa dua bi ka ho sɛ sika foforɔ, na nnua boa guina carbon na ɛsua katawere mu sɛsae ho ɔkɔm. Nnua a wɔka wɔn ho ne Moringa, Leucaena, ne Acacia.

English Question: To prepare for unpredictable weather: grow more than one crop to spread risk, keep records of past planting dates and yields to understand your local patterns, store enough food and seed reserves, install or improve water harvesting systems, use drought and flood-tolerant varieties, maintain healthy soil with high organic matter which buffers both drought and flooding, and join farmer groups that share weather information.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesiesie m'afuo ama ɛwim tebea a ɛntumi nnim?
Twi Answer: Siesie ama ɛwim tebea a ɛntumi nnim: kura nnuaba dodo sɛ mfomso antete, kora aba to bere ne nnuaba a wogye ho nsɛm sɛ wuhu wo beae tebea, guina aduan ne aba ahwɛso, si anaa siesie nsuo guina systɛm, fa aba a ɛtumi nsuo pa ne nsuo tenten ase hyɛ, kora asase a enni aho yie ne nhwiren foforo dodo a ɛboa wɔ nsuo pa ne nsuo tenten bere, na ba okuafo kuo a wɔkyɛ ɛwim amanneɛ.

English Question: Minimum tillage (also called conservation tillage) means disturbing the soil as little as possible when preparing for planting — using just enough tillage to create a seedbed. Benefits include: preserves soil structure, reduces erosion, maintains soil moisture, protects soil organisms, reduces fuel and labor costs, and helps store carbon in the soil. Use a jab planter or hand hoe to plant directly into the soil with minimal disturbance.
Twi Question: Dɛn na minimum tillage yɛ na ɛdeɛn na ɛyɛ asase pa?
Twi Answer: Minimum tillage (a wɔfre no conservation tillage nso) kyerɛ haw asase ketewa ketewa bere a wosiesie aba to mu ansa — fa tillage a ɛdodo pɛ sɛ woyi asase aba to mu ansa. Mfaaso ho ne: kora asase mu siesie, sua erosion, kora nsukuro wɔ asase mu, kora asase mu nkwa, sua fuel ne dwumadie ho sika, na boa guina carbon wɔ asase mu. Fa jab planter anaa nsa akɔde to aba tɔtɔ wɔ asase mu na wonhaw dodo.

English Question: Trees absorb carbon dioxide from the atmosphere and store it in their wood and roots — this is called carbon sequestration. A single large tree can absorb 22 kg of carbon dioxide per year. Trees also reduce local temperatures, increase rainfall through transpiration, protect water catchments, and reduce erosion. Planting trees on your farm is one of the most powerful climate actions a farmer can take.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na to nnua wɔ m'afuo so boa katawere mu sɛsae so?
Twi Answer: Nnua gye carbon dioxide fi ɛwim mu na guina mu wɔ wɔn dua ne ntini mu — wɔfre eyi carbon sequestration. Dua kɛse baako tumi gye carbon dioxide kilogram 22 wɔ afe biara. Nnua nso sua beae ahuhuro, boa osu ba wɔ transpiration mu, kora nsuo gye beae, na sua erosion. To nnua wɔ wo afuo so yɛ katawere mu sɛsae dwuma titiriw a okuafo tumi yɛ.

English Question: Solar powered irrigation uses solar panels to generate electricity that powers water pumps for irrigating crops. Benefits include: no fuel costs, low maintenance, reliable operation, and environmental friendliness. Small farmers can access it through: government subsidy programs, cooperative ownership of shared solar pumps, microfinance loans for solar pump purchase, and NGO programs. The initial cost is high but long-term savings are significant.
Twi Question: Dɛn na solar powered irrigation yɛ na okuafo ketewa tumi di?
Twi Answer: Solar powered irrigation fa solar panels di dwuma sɛ ɛyɛ electricity a ɛma nsuo pumps a wɔde to nnuaba so adwuma. Mfaaso ho ne: fuel ho sika nni, hwɛ ase yɛ mmerɛ, adwuma yɛ pɛ, na ɛma ɛwim no da yie. Okuafo ketewa tumi nya ase wɔ: ɔman boa adwuma, cooperative bom fa solar pumps, microfinance ka ma solar pump tɔn, ne NGO adwuma. Sika a wode fi no yɛ den nanso bere tenten ho mfaaso yɛ kɛse.

English Question: Integrate livestock by using their manure as organic fertilizer for crops. Chickens can help control insects and weeds. After harvest allow animals to graze on crop residues which also helps clear the field. This integrated farming approach reduces costs and improves productivity.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mefa m'mmoa di dwuma ma m'afuo nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Ka mmoa ho wɔ de wɔn aguare yɛ nhwiren foforo ferefere ma nnuaba. Akrɔma tumi boa kora adwummakers ne nhaban foforo ase. Nnuaba gye akyi, ma mmoa nom nnuaba nsennua a aka no a ɛnso boa hohoro afuo no. Eyi farming anammɔn sua sika na ɛma afuo no nyinaa da sor yie.

English Question: Sudden chicken deaths could be from Newcastle Disease, Gumboro disease, or poisoning. Vaccinate chickens against common diseases at the right ages. Consult a veterinary officer immediately for diagnosis. Quarantine sick birds to prevent spread to healthy ones.
Twi Question: M'akrɔma rewu ntɛm. Dɛn na betumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: Akrɔma wu a ɛba ntɛm betumi fi Newcastle Yadeɛ, Gumboro yadeɛ, anaa dawuro. De akrɔma kɔ yadeɛ dawuro bere a ɛfata wɔn mfeɛ so. Ka veterinary officer ho ntɛm sɛ ɔhwɛ yadeɛ no. Yi akrɔma a wɔayarɛ no fi wɔn a wɔwɔ aho no mu.

English Question: Vaccinate all animals on schedule, quarantine new animals for 2 weeks before mixing with your herd, isolate sick animals immediately, maintain clean housing with good ventilation, dispose of dead animals properly, and consult a veterinary officer regularly. Good hygiene is the most important disease prevention tool.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mema yadeɛ antete wɔ m'mmoa ntam?
Twi Answer: De mmoa nyinaa kɔ yadeɛ dawuro bere a ɛsɛ, yi mmoa foforo na wɔntena nnawotwe 2 ansa na woka wɔn ne mmoa a wɔwɔ hɔ bom, yi mmoa a wɔayarɛ ntɛm ara, kora wɔn fie a ɛhoro ne mframa pue mu yie, yi mmoa a awu yie, na ka veterinary officer ho pɛ.

English Question: Useful apps for Ghanaian farmers include: Esoko for market prices, Farmerline for agricultural advice and services, Hello Tractor for renting tractors, AgroFresh for produce quality management, Google Translate for translating agricultural content, YouTube for farming tutorials, Ghana Met Agency app for weather forecasts, and WhatsApp for connecting with other farmers and extension officers. Most are free or low-cost.
Twi Question: Farming apps bɛn na ɛboa okuafo wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Apps a ɛboa okuafo Ghana mu ne: Esoko ma aguabasa boɔ, Farmerline ma okuafo adwuma boa ne nnwuma, Hello Tractor ma tractor asɛ, AgroFresh ma nnuaba ho pa hwɛ, Google Translate ma okuafo nsɛm dan, YouTube ma okuafo adwuma nhyehyɛe, Ghana Met Agency app ma ɛwim amanneɛ, ne WhatsApp ma kasa ne okuafo ne extension officers foforɔ. Wɔn bebree yɛ daa anaa boɔ yɛ ketewa.

English Question: YouTube has thousands of free farming tutorials. Search for: specific crop names plus 'farming Ghana', pest or disease names plus 'how to control', fertilizer application techniques, irrigation setup guides, and post-harvest handling. Subscribe to channels like IITA, CTA Agriculture, and local Ghanaian farming channels. Download videos on WiFi to watch offline when you are at the farm without internet access.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mefa YouTube di dwuma sɛ sua okuafo adwuma anammɔn?
Twi Answer: YouTube wɔ okuafo adwuma nhyehyɛe ahorow a ɛyɛ daa. Hwehwɛ: nnuaba din ne 'farming Ghana', adwumakers anaa yadeɛ din ne 'how to control', ferefere to anammɔn, nsuo to nhyehyɛe, ne gye akyi hwɛ ase anammɔn. Kyerɛw wo din wɔ channels te sɛ IITA, CTA Agriculture, ne Ghana okuafo channels. Sii videos wɔ WiFi so sɛ wuhwɛ wɔn bere a wowɔ afuo so na internet nni hɔ.

English Question: A soil testing kit is a set of chemicals and test strips or color charts that let you test your soil's pH, nitrogen, phosphorus, and potassium levels at home. To use: collect soil from several spots in your field and mix together, take a small sample, follow the kit instructions to mix with testing chemicals, compare the color change to the chart provided, and use results to decide what fertilizer to apply. Kits are available at agricultural supply stores.
Twi Question: Dɛn na asase hwɛ kit yɛ na ɛdeɛn na mefa di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Asase hwɛ kit yɛ chemicals ne test strips anaa color charts a ɛma wo tumi hwɛ wo asase pH, nitrogen, phosphorus, ne potassium wɔ fie. Di dwuma eyi: gye asase fi beae ahodoɔ wɔ afuo mu na ka bom, fa sample ketewa, bu kit nhyɛso so sɛ de chemicals ka ho, twe rere sɛsae na ka ho ne chart a wɔde brɛ, na fa adwuma ho sɛ paw ferefere a wohia. Kits wɔ hɔ wɔ agricultural supply adeɛtɔ hɔ.

English Question: Women play a critical role in Ghanaian agriculture — they make up about 52% of the agricultural workforce. Women are primarily responsible for food crop production, post-harvest processing, and marketing. They often face challenges accessing land, credit, and inputs. Programs that specifically support women farmers include Women in Agricultural Development (WIAD) under MOFA, and many NGOs focusing on women's empowerment in agriculture.
Twi Question: Dɛn na mmaa gyina wɔ okuafo adwuma mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Mmaa gyina titiriw pa ara wɔ Ghana okuafo adwuma mu — wɔyɛ bɛn 52% wɔ okuafo adwumafo mu. Mmaa hia aduan nnuaba kura, gye akyi yɛ adwuma, ne tɔn. Wɔtaa hia asase, ka, ne adenneɛ ho nsɛm. Adwuma a ɛhwɛ mmaa okuafo ho pɛ ne Women in Agricultural Development (WIAD) wɔ MOFA ase, ne NGOs bebree a wɔhwɛ mmaa ho wɔ okuafo adwuma mu.

English Question: Take clear close-up photos of affected plant parts — leaves, stems, fruits, or roots. Include a coin for scale. Send photos to: your extension officer via WhatsApp, post in farmer WhatsApp or Facebook groups for advice, use apps like Plantix or PlantVillage that use AI to diagnose diseases from photos, or email to your nearest CSIR research station. Clear photos from multiple angles help get the most accurate diagnosis.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mefa smartphone camera di dwuma sɛ hunu m'nnuaba nsɛm?
Twi Answer: Fa foto fitafita wɔ nnuaba a wɔayarɛ no ho — nhaban, tibo, aba, anaa ntini. Ka sika de hwɛ boɔ. De foto kɔ: wo extension officer ho wɔ WhatsApp, de si wɔ okuafo WhatsApp anaa Facebook kuo mu sɛ wunya boa, fa apps te sɛ Plantix anaa PlantVillage a wɔde AI di dwuma sɛ hunu yadeɛ fi foto mu, anaa email kɔ CSIR research station a ɛbɛn wo. Foto fitafita fi afã ahodoɔ boa sɛ wuhu yadeɛ no pa ara.

English Question: To start a small home poultry farm: decide on type (layers for eggs or broilers for meat), build or buy a simple wooden or wire coop with shade and good ventilation, start with 10-20 birds, provide clean water and commercial feed, vaccinate birds at the recommended ages, keep the coop clean, and record feeds, deaths, and egg production. Start small and scale as you learn.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesi akrɔma afuo ketewa wɔ fie?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ si akrɔma afuo ketewa wɔ fie: paw ahodoɔ (layers ma kosua anaa broilers ma nam), si anaa tɔ dua anaa wire fie a ewim brɛ ne mframa pue mu yie, fi akrɔma 10-20, de nsuo horo ne aduan a wɔtɔ ma wɔn, de akrɔma kɔ yadeɛ dawuro bere a ɛsɛ, kora fie no horo, na kora aduan, wuu, ne kosua ho nsɛm. Fi ketewa na fa dodo so bere a wosua.

English Question: Improve cow milk quality and quantity by: feeding balanced rations including good pasture, silage, hay, and concentrate feed; providing clean water always; milking at the same time every day; maintaining good hygiene during milking; treating and preventing mastitis (udder inflammation) promptly; providing shade and reducing stress; and selecting productive dairy breeds or crossing local cattle with improved breeds.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi ma m'boo nufuo pa ara?
Twi Answer: Siesie boo nufuo ho pa ne kɛse wɔ: ma aduan a ɛpɛ wɔn ho yie a mu wɔ atɛntɛnni pa, silage, hay, ne concentrate aduan; de nsuo horo ma wɔn daa; nom wɔn nufuo bere koro da biara; kora ho tumi bere a wonuom nufuo; yɛ dawuro ma na kora mastitis (nufuo mu yadeɛ) ntɛm; ma ewim brɛ wɔn na mma wɔn nhaw; na paw boo a wɔn nufuo yɛ pa anaa ka beae boo ne boo foforɔ a ɛda sor bom.

English Question: Reduce feed costs using local ingredients: for poultry, use maize germ, rice bran, palm kernel cake, fishmeal, and dried moringa leaves as protein; for pigs, use cassava peels, plantain peels, vegetable waste, and kitchen leftovers (no meat or salt); for cattle, plant improved pasture grasses like Brachiaria and Stylosanthes, use crop residues like maize stover and rice straw, and supplement with salt blocks.
Twi Question: Aduan bɛn a ɛwɔ fie na ɛyɛ pa wɔ m'mmoa ho sɛ mpampa sika?
Twi Answer: Sua aduan sika wɔ fa beae adenneɛ: akrɔma ho, fa aburow germ, ɔmɔ nkutupan, abe nkuto cake, nsuomnam dust, ne moringa nhaban a ayaw sɛ aduan protein; prako ho, fa bankye nkutupan, borɔdɔ nkutupan, nnuan asennua, ne fie aduan a aka (mfa nam anaa ɛwa); boo ho, to Brachiaria ne Stylosanthes atɛntɛnni a wɔayɛ wɔn foforo, fa nnuaba nsennua te sɛ aburow nsennua ne ɔmɔ tow, na ka salt blocks ho.

English Question: When handling sick animals: wear gloves and wash hands thoroughly after contact, isolate sick animals from healthy ones immediately, do not move sick animals to other farms, contact a veterinary officer for diagnosis before administering treatment, follow withdrawal periods for medicines before slaughter or selling milk, keep records of all treatments given, and dispose of dead animals by deep burial away from water sources.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ mmoa a wɔayarɛ ho yie?
Twi Answer: Bere a wuhwɛ mmoa a wɔayarɛ ho: fa nsatea nhoma na hohoro wo nsa yie akyi a woka wɔn, yi mmoa a wɔayarɛ fi wɔn a wɔwɔ aho no mu ntɛm, mfa mmoa a wɔayarɛ kɔ afuo foforɔ, ka veterinary officer ho sɛ ɔhunu yadeɛ no ansa na wode dawuro to, bu dawuro withdrawal bere ansa na wokum anaa tɔn nufuo, kora nsɛm a yɛ dawuro nyinaa ho, na de mmoa a awu sisie wɔ asase mu tenten fi nsuo ho.

English Question: Signs of goat pregnancy include: no return to heat after mating, enlarged abdomen especially from month 3, enlarged udder especially in the last month, behavioral changes like becoming calmer, and weight gain. Care during pregnancy: provide extra feed especially in the last 6 weeks, ensure access to clean water always, avoid rough handling, vaccinate against clostridial diseases, deworm at least 3 weeks before kidding, and prepare a clean kidding area.
Twi Question: Ahohyenam bɛn na ɛkyerɛ sɛ m'abirekyi wɔ nyinsɛn na ɛdeɛn na meyɛ?
Twi Answer: Abirekyi nyinsɛn ahohyenam ho ne: onsan nba bio akyi a watwa, yafunu kɛse titiriw fi bosome 3, nufuo kɛse titiriw wɔ bosome ɔkyena, ɔtenabea sɛsae te sɛ yɛ abotare, na boɔ sor. Hwɛ bere nyinsɛn mu: ma aduan dodo titiriw wɔ nnawotwe 6 a atwam ansa na omba, kora nsuo horo wɔ hɔ daa, mhaw no, de kɔ clostridial yadeɛ dawuro, hwɛ adwummakers ase wiemu 3 ansa na oba mba, na siesie beae horo sɛ oba mba.

English Question: Key food safety practices for farmers include: washing hands before handling produce, using clean water for irrigation especially on leafy vegetables, applying pesticides according to label instructions and respecting pre-harvest intervals, not using human waste as fertilizer, keeping animals away from vegetable gardens, using clean equipment and containers, and training farm workers on hygiene practices.
Twi Question: Aduan ho tumi anammɔn bɛn na okuafo sɛ bu wɔn so?
Twi Answer: Aduan ho tumi anammɔn a ɛhia ma okuafo ne: hohoro wo nsa ansa na wohwɛ nnuaba ho, fa nsuo horo sɛ to nnuaba so titiriw nhaban nnuan so, de adwummakers dawuro to wɔ krataa nhyɛso so na bu pre-harvest bere so, mfa onipa aguare yɛ ferefere, mma mmoa nnuaba afuo mu, fa egyapade ne nkuku horo, na kyerɛ afuo adwumafo aduan ho tumi anammɔn.

English Question: The waiting time between pesticide application and harvest is called the Pre-Harvest Interval (PHI) and varies by chemical. Always check the pesticide label for the specific PHI. Common examples: Emamectin benzoate (3-7 days), Cypermethrin (7-14 days), Mancozeb fungicide (7 days), Glyphosate herbicide (14 days). If the label is lost, wait at least 14 days as a safe default. Never harvest before the PHI has passed.
Twi Question: Bere ahe na ɛsɛ me twɛn akyi a mede adwummakers dawuro guare ansa na megye nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Bere a ɛda adwummakers dawuro to ne nnuaba gye ntam sɛ Pre-Harvest Interval (PHI) na ɛsesa wɔ chemical biara so. Hwɛ adwummakers dawuro krataa so bere a ɛhia pɛ. Nhwɛso a wɔtaa hu: Emamectin benzoate (nnafoa 3-7), Cypermethrin (nnafoa 7-14), Mancozeb fungicide (nnafoa 7), Glyphosate herbicide (nnafoa 14). Sɛ krataa no ahu a, twɛn nnafoa 14 pɛ sɛ beae a ɛho tumi. Mye nnuaba ansa na PHI no awi da.

English Question: Wash vegetables safely by: using clean potable water, soaking for 1-2 minutes in a solution of 1 tablespoon of vinegar per litre of water or approved food-grade chlorine solution, then rinsing thoroughly with clean water. For leafy vegetables, separate leaves and wash each leaf individually. Dry before packaging. Never wash with river, pond, or canal water as these may contain pathogens.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehohoro nnuan yie ansa na midi anaa tɔn?
Twi Answer: Hohoro nnuan yie wɔ: fa nsuo horo a wɔtumi nom, da wɔ vinegar tablespoon baako wɔ nsuo litre biara mu anaa food-grade chlorine a wɔagyei mu sɛntɔ 1-2, afei hohoro yie wɔ nsuo horo. Nhaban nnuan ho, twa nhaban mu na hohoro nhaban biara biara ho. Yaw ansa na wopaka. Mhohoro wɔ ɔsubɔnten, asranom, anaa kɔtɔ nsuo mu da efisɛ wɔn mu tumi wɔ yadeɛ.

English Question: Using raw (untreated) waste carries serious risks: human and animal waste contains pathogens like E.coli, Salmonella, and parasites that can contaminate crops and cause disease in people who eat them. The WHO recommends composting waste for at least 6-12 months or treating with ash or lime before applying to crops. Only apply to soil, never to the edible parts of plants. Always wash hands and produce thoroughly.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɔkɔm wɔ ho wɔ fa onipa anaa mmoa aguare foforo yɛ ferefere?
Twi Answer: Fa aguare foforo (a wonsi amu) di dwuma wɔ ɔkɔm kɛse: onipa ne mmoa aguare wɔ yadeɛ mu te sɛ E.coli, Salmonella, ne adwumakers a ɛtumi haw nnuaba na yɛ nnipa a wɔdi wɔn yadee. WHO ka sɛ compost aguare wiemu 6-12 anaa siesie wɔ nkamfo anaa lime ho ansa na wode to nnuaba so. De to asase pɛ, mde to nnuaba a wɔdi ho da. Hohoro wo nsa ne nnuaba yie daa.

English Question: If pesticide poisoning occurs: call the Ghana Poisons Information Centre or the nearest hospital immediately, remove the victim from the exposure area, if ingested do not induce vomiting unless directed by medical professionals, if on skin remove contaminated clothing and wash with soap and water, if in eyes flush with clean water for 15-20 minutes, bring the pesticide container or label to the hospital. Prevention: always wear protective equipment when using pesticides.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mede adwummakers dawuro ɔkɔm hwe krataa kɔ?
Twi Answer: Sɛ adwummakers dawuro ɔkɔm ba a: frɛ Ghana Poisons Information Centre anaa sikabea a ɛbɛn wo ntɛm, yi obi a ɔkɔm aba no fi beae no, sɛ ɔnom a mma onyi no mua ansa na onyini ɔkɔm ne mu, sɛ firi wo ho skin so a yi ntama a dawuro ato so na hohoro wɔ sabɔ ne nsuo mu, sɛ wɔ ani mu a fa nsuo horo mu sɛntɔ 15-20, de adwummakers dawuro nkuku anaa krataa kɔ sikabea. Kora ase: taa hye ntoma a ɛkora wo ho bere a wode adwummakers dawuro di dwuma.

English Question: Buy certified seeds from: MOFA-approved agro-input dealers, agricultural supply stores in district capitals, certified seed companies like SeedCo, Pioneer, and Yara, cooperative input stores, and CSIR research stations which sometimes sell breeder or foundation seeds. Always look for the official seed certification label on the bag. Avoid buying seeds from roadsides or markets where quality cannot be guaranteed.
Twi Question: Ɛhe na metumi tɔ aba a wɔakyerɛw wɔn wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Tɔ aba a wɔakyerɛw wɔn fi: agro-input adeɛtɔfo a MOFA agyei, agricultural supply adeɛtɔ wɔ district titirimpon mu, aba kuo a wɔakyerɛw wɔn te sɛ SeedCo, Pioneer, ne Yara, cooperative input adeɛtɔ, ne CSIR research stations a wɔtaa tɔn breeder anaa foundation aba. Hwɛ daa aba kyerɛwsɛm krataa a ɛwɔ bag so no. Bɔ hwɛ tɔ aba fi kwan ho anaa aguabasa a wɔntumi nkyerɛ aho hɔ.

English Question: Seed priming is soaking seeds in water or a special solution for a specific time before planting to improve germination rate, speed, and uniformity. Methods include: hydropriming (soaking in plain water for 6-12 hours then drying before planting), and salt priming (soaking in dilute salt solution). Primed seeds germinate faster and more uniformly, which helps crops establish better especially in marginal soils or unpredictable rainfall.
Twi Question: Dɛn na seed priming yɛ na ɛboa aba pue sɛn?
Twi Answer: Seed priming kyerɛ da aba wɔ nsuo anaa aduru a wɔakyerɛ ho bere mu ansa na woto mu sɛ ɛsiesie aba pue rate, ntɛm, ne pɛ. Anammɔn ho ne: hydropriming (da wɔ nsuo foforo mu dapɛn 6-12 na yaw ansa na woto), ne salt priming (da wɔ ɛwa a wɔasusu mu). Aba a wɔaprime no pue ntɛm ne pɛ, eyi boa nnuaba si yie titiriw wɔ asase a enni pa anaa osu a ɛntumi nnim bere mu.

English Question: Test seed viability by: placing 10 seeds on a damp paper towel, fold and keep in a warm place, check after 7-10 days. Count how many germinated — if 8-10 germinated (80-100%) seeds are excellent; 6-7 (60-70%) are acceptable; below 5 (50%) plant more seeds per hole. Old or poorly stored seeds lose viability — check the production date on the bag and do not use seeds more than 2 years old.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ aba no da sor na ɛfata sɛ mede to mu?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ aba ho pa wɔ: de aba 10 si krataa nte so, fa bo mu na guina wɔ bae a ɛhuru, hwɛ nnafoa 7-10 akyi. Kan a pue — sɛ 8-10 apue (80-100%) a aba no yɛ pa pa ara; 6-7 (60-70%) akyɛ; ɛsua 5 (50%) a to aba dodo wɔ tumtum biara mu. Aba kedee anaa a wonguina wɔn yie sua wɔn tumi — hwɛ yɛ da a ɛwɔ bag so na mfa aba a wɔadin mfe abien kenkan.

English Question: Young people can make farming profitable by: treating farming as a business not a subsistence activity, specializing in high-value crops or livestock products, using technology and innovation, accessing youth-specific agricultural finance programs, connecting to urban markets through digital platforms, forming youth cooperatives for scale and bargaining power, adding value through processing, and combining farming with agribusiness services like input supply or transportation.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mmofra tumi ma okuafo adwuma brɛ sika?
Twi Answer: Mmofra tumi ma okuafo adwuma brɛ sika wɔ: hwɛ okuafo adwuma sɛ adwuma na mfa sɛ fie aduan adwuma, paw nnuaba anaa mmoa nnuaba ho adwuma a wɔtɔ boɔ kɛse, fa technology ne nnorimde di dwuma, nya mmofra ho okuafo adwuma ka adwuma, ka kɔ akura aguabasa wɔ digital platforms ho, si mmofra cooperative sɛ fa ɔman ne tumi kɛse, de boɔ ka ho wɔ yɛ adwuma mu, na ka okuafo adwuma ho nnwuma te sɛ adenneɛ tɔn anaa kwan so nnwuma.

English Question: A Farmer Field School (FFS) is a learning program where groups of 25-30 farmers meet regularly in a field to observe, experiment, and learn about agriculture together under a trained facilitator. They learn practical skills by doing rather than just listening. FFS programs in Ghana are run by MOFA, NGOs, and development organizations. Contact your local MOFA extension office or agricultural NGOs in your area to find and join one.
Twi Question: Dɛn na farmer field school yɛ na ɛdeɛn na meba mu?
Twi Answer: Farmer Field School (FFS) yɛ suahu adwuma a okuafo 25-30 kuo hyia pɛ wɔ afuo mu sɛ wɔhwɛ, dwiri, ne sua okuafo adwuma bom wɔ obi a wɔakyerɛ ase. Wɔsua adwuma ho nyansam wɔ di dwuma na mfa tie pɛ. FFS adwuma wɔ Ghana ne MOFA, NGOs, ne nkosuo kuo di. Ka kyerɛ wo MOFA extension ofisi anaa agricultural NGOs wɔ wo beae sɛ wuhu ne ba mu.

English Question: Options for accessing land include: renting from landowners (common in Ghana, negotiate fair terms), sharecropping where you farm and share produce with the landowner, borrowing land from family or community leaders, government allocation programs for young farmers, and cooperative land pooling. Always get written agreements when renting or sharecropping to protect your investment. Contact the Lands Commission or MOFA for guidance on formal land access.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menya asase ma okuafo adwuma sɛ menni?
Twi Answer: Asase nya anammɔn ho ne: asɛ fi asase wura (taa yɛ wɔ Ghana, siesie nhyɛso yie), sharecropping a woyɛ okuafo adwuma na fa nnuaba bi brɛ asase wura no, de asase fi abusua anaa oman hene ho, ɔman asase brɛ adwuma ma mmofra okuafo, ne cooperative asase ka bom. Kora nhyɛso krataa bere a wasɛ anaa sharecrop sɛ ɛkora wo sika. Ka kyerɛ Lands Commission anaa MOFA sɛ wunya mmoa wɔ asase nya anammɔn mu.

English Question: Benefits of farmer cooperatives include: collective bargaining power for better input prices and higher selling prices, shared access to expensive equipment like tractors and storage facilities, group loans that may be easier to access than individual loans, collective learning and knowledge sharing, risk pooling among members, access to bulk markets that individual farmers cannot reach, and stronger political voice when advocating for farmer interests with government.
Twi Question: Mfaaso bɛn na ɛwɔ ho wɔ si okuafo cooperative?
Twi Answer: Okuafo cooperative mfaaso ho ne: kuo tumi kɛse ma adenneɛ boɔ sua ne tɔn boɔ kɛse, ka egyapade a wɔboɔ yɛ den te sɛ tractor ne guina fie ho bom, kuo ka a ɛtumi yɛ mmerɛ sɛ nya sen onipa ho ka, kuo suahu ne nyansam kyɛ, mfomso sesae wɔ kuo mu, nya aguabasa kɛse a okuafo baako nntumi nkɔ hɔ, ne kuo mu tumi kɛse bere a wɔka okuafo ho nsɛm kyerɛ ɔman.

English Question: To access export markets: ensure your produce meets international quality and food safety standards, get certified (organic, GlobalGAP, or Fairtrade if possible), register with Ghana Export Promotion Authority (GEPA), contact exporters and trading companies, join export-focused farmer cooperatives, attend agricultural trade fairs, and use online platforms like TradeAfrica or Alibaba. High-value export crops from Ghana include cocoa, cashew, shea, pineapple, and chili pepper.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meka kɔ amanaman aguabasa ma m'afuo nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wohwehwɛ nya amanaman aguabasa a, kora sɛ wo nnuaba kɔ amanaman aho ne aduan ho tumi nhyɛso, nya kratafa (organic, GlobalGAP, anaa Fairtrade sɛ wonya tumi), kyerɛw wo din wɔ Ghana Export Promotion Authority (GEPA) hɔ, ka exporters ne adwuma kuo ho, ba export okuafo cooperative mu, kɔ okuafo adwuma aguabasa, na fa online platforms te sɛ TradeAfrica anaa Alibaba di dwuma. Nnuaba a wɔtaa export fi Ghana ne kookoo, cashew, nkuto, aborɔfo, ne mako hye.

English Question: Good farming soil is dark, crumbly, and has a pleasant earthy smell. Push your finger 5cm into the soil — if it holds shape but breaks apart easily, it is good. You can also send a sample to an agricultural office for a proper soil test.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na ɛkyerɛ sɛ m'asase yɛ yɛ papa ma okuafo adwuma?
Twi Answer: Asase pa wɔ okuafo adwuma mu yɛ ɛda, na ɛpepee yie, na ɛwɔ asase hua. Fa wo nsateaa wura asase no mu sɛntimita 5 — sɛ ɛkura ne ho nanso ɛpae yie a, ɛyɛ asase pa. Wobetumi de asase bi kɔ okuafo ofisi sɛ wɔhwɛ so yie.

English Question: For maize, use NPK fertilizer (15-15-15) at planting, then top-dress with urea about 4-6 weeks after planting. Apply 2 bags of NPK per acre at planting and 1 bag of urea per acre when top-dressing.
Twi Question: Ferefere bɛn na ɛyɛ papa ma aburo?
Twi Answer: Aburo ho, fa NPK ferefere (15-15-15) de to asase mu bere a wode aburow to mu no. Afei fa urea gu so sɛntɔ 4-6 akyi a wode aburow to mu no. Fa NPK bɔtɔ 2 gu acre baako biara mu bere a wode aburow no gu fam, na fa urea bɔtɔ 1 gu acre baako biara mu bere a wode to so.

English Question: Yes, animal manure from cows, goats, or chickens is an excellent organic fertilizer. Apply well-composted manure 2-3 weeks before planting. It improves soil structure and provides slow-release nutrients.
Twi Question: Metumi de mmoa dɔteɛ adi dwuma mmom sen nnuru ferefere?
Twi Answer: Aane, mmoa aguare fi boo, abirekyi, anaa akrɔma yɛ ferefere papa pa ara. De aguare a ɛawie wo yie no to asase so wiemu 2-3 ansa na wobede aba to mu. Ɛsiesie asase mu na ɛma aduan ho nhwiren ba bebree.

English Question: Mix green materials like grass and vegetable waste with brown materials like dry leaves and straw in a pile. Keep it moist and turn it every 2 weeks. After 2-3 months, you will have rich compost ready for your farm.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na meyɛ compost wɔ fie?
Twi Answer: Fa Nneɛma a ɛyɛ ahabammono te sɛ sare ne nnuaba funu fra nneɛma a ɛyɛ bruu te sɛ nhaban a ɛwo ne sarew. Ma ɛnnyɛ nwini na dane no dapɛn abien biara. Abosome 2-3 akyi, wobɛnya compost pa a ɛawie wo yie wɔ wo afuo ho.

English Question: Add organic matter like compost, animal manure, or crop residues to sandy soil. This helps retain moisture and nutrients. Mulching the soil surface also reduces water evaporation. Consider drip irrigation for better water management.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi yɛ asintiɛ asase a ɛwo ntɛm no yiye?
Twi Answer: De nhwiren foforo te sɛ compost, mmoa aguare, anaa nnuaba ho nsennua ka asintiɛ asase no ho. Eyi boa ma nsu ne nnuaba mu nnuane nka mu yie. Sɛ wode mulch kata asase no so a, ɛma nsuo nwo ntɛm. Fa drip irrigation di dwuma sɛ wuhwɛ nsuo so yiye.

English Question: Plant cover crops or grass along slopes, practice contour farming, build terraces on steep land, and mulch bare soil. Avoid leaving soil uncovered during heavy rain seasons.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mema asase amma ɛnhuru wɔ m'afuo mu?
Twi Answer: To nnuaba anaa atɛntɛnni wɔ kwantempon ho, yɛ contour farming, si terrace wɔ asase a ɛkwan so, na de mulch sɛɛ asase a ɛda. Bɔ hwɛ asase da ho akyɛ wɔ nsuo tenten bere mu.

English Question: Apply agricultural lime (calcium carbonate) to raise the pH of acidic soil. Typically apply 1-2 tonnes per hectare. Apply lime at least 3-4 weeks before planting and mix it well into the soil.
Twi Question: M'asase yɛ acidic dodo. Dɛn na metumi yɛ?
Twi Answer: De agricultural lime (calcium carbonate) to asase acidic no so sɛ ɛma pH no sor. Taa de tonne 1-2 to hectare biara so. De lime to asase so wiemu 3-4 ansa na wode aba to mu na ka ho yie wɔ asase mu.

English Question: Most vegetables grow best in soil with a pH between 6.0 and 7.0. Below 6.0 is too acidic and above 7.5 is too alkaline. You can test your soil pH using a simple pH testing kit from an agro-input shop or send a sample to your nearest agricultural laboratory.
Twi Question: Asase pH bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ ma nnuan?
Twi Answer: Nnuan bebree da sor pa wɔ asase a pH yɛ 6.0 ne 7.0 ntam. Ɛsua 6.0 a ɛyɛ acidic dodo na ɛboro 7.5 a ɛyɛ alkaline dodo. Wobetumi hwɛ wo asase pH wɔ pH testing kit fi agro-input adeɛtɔ hɔ anaa de asase bi kɔ agricultural laboratory a ɛbɛn wo.

English Question: Green manure means growing specific crops like legumes or grasses and then plowing them back into the soil while still green. This adds organic matter and nitrogen to the soil. Common green manure crops include cowpea, mucuna, and lablab. Plow them in at least 3 weeks before planting your main crop.
Twi Question: Dɛn na green manure yɛ na ɛdeɛn na mefa di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Green manure kyerɛ kura nnuaba bi te sɛ abɔdweɛ anaa atɛntɛnni na afei boro wɔn gu asase mu bere a wɔda koraa. Eyi de nhwiren foforo ne nitrogen ka asase ho. Green manure nnuaba a wɔtaa di dwuma ne abɔdweɛ, mucuna, ne lablab. Boro wɔn gu asase mu wiemu 3 ansa na wokura wo nnuaba titiriw.

English Question: Signs that fertilizer is working include: darker green leaves, faster plant growth, larger leaves, and higher yield compared to unfertilized plots. If plants remain yellowish and grow slowly after 2-3 weeks of fertilizer application, the fertilizer may not have been applied correctly or the soil may have other problems.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'ferefere yɛ adwuma?
Twi Answer: Ahohyenam sɛ ferefere yɛ adwuma ne: nhaban a wɔyɛ tuntum-akyen pa ara, nnuaba a wɔda sor ntɛm, nhaban kɛse, ne nnuaba a wɔda sor dodo sen beae a wɔanto ferefere. Sɛ nnuaba da hoho na wɔda sor brɛ akyi a ferefere to so wiemu 2-3 a, ferefere no beɛ to so yie anaa asase no wɔ nsɛm foforɔ.

English Question: Yes, over-fertilizing can burn plant roots and leaves, cause excessive leafy growth with poor fruiting, pollute water sources, and waste money. Always follow the recommended rates on fertilizer bags or advice from your extension officer. Start with less and increase gradually based on crop response.
Twi Question: Ferefere dodo tumi sɛe m'nnuaba anaa?
Twi Answer: Aane, ferefere dodo tumi hyew nnuaba ntini ne nhaban, ma nnuaba nhaban da sor dodo na aba ba sua, ha nsuo mu, na seaa sika. Bue ferefere bag so krataa nhyɛso anaa fa wo extension officer nsɛm di. Fi ferefere sua na fa dodo so kakra kakra wɔ nnuaba tebea so.

English Question: NPK stands for Nitrogen (N), Phosphorus (P), and Potassium (K) — the three main nutrients plants need. Nitrogen helps leafy growth, Phosphorus supports root development and flowering, and Potassium strengthens stems and improves fruit quality. The numbers like 15-15-15 show the percentage of each nutrient in the bag.
Twi Question: Dɛn na NPK kyerɛ wɔ ferefere bag so?
Twi Answer: NPK kyerɛ Nitrogen (N), Phosphorus (P), ne Potassium (K) — aduan titiriw mmiɛnsa a nnuaba hia. Nitrogen boa nhaban da sor, Phosphorus boa ntini ne abode, na Potassium ma tibo yɛ den na aba yɛ pa. Nɔma te sɛ 15-15-15 no kyerɛ kɛse a aduan biara wɔ bag mu.

English Question: Do not apply fertilizer when: heavy rain is forecast as it will wash away the fertilizer, the soil is very dry as it can burn roots, plants are severely stressed from pests or disease, soil is waterlogged, or crops are very close to harvest. Always apply when soil has some moisture and weather is stable.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na nsɛ meto ferefere?
Twi Answer: Mto ferefere bere a: osu tenten rebɛba efisɛ ɛbɛhoro ferefere no kɔ, asase yera pa ara efisɛ betumi hyew ntini, nnuaba hia adwummakers anaa yadeɛ kɛse, nsuo hyɛ asase mu, anaa nnuaba rebɛwie ase ntɛm. To ferefere bere a asase wɔ nsuo kakra na ɛwim tebea yɛ pɛ.

English Question: Simple home tests: for pH, mix soil with vinegar — if it fizzes the soil is alkaline. Mix soil with baking soda and water — if it fizzes the soil is acidic. For texture, squeeze moist soil — clay soil holds shape, sandy soil crumbles, and loam soil holds shape then crumbles. For organic matter, dark soil has more organic matter than pale soil.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mehwɛ m'asase wɔ fie a menwɔ kit?
Twi Answer: Fie hwɛ anammɔn ketewa: pH ho, ka asase ne vinegar — sɛ ɛpɔ a asase no yɛ alkaline. Ka asase ne baking soda ne nsuo — sɛ ɛpɔ a asase no yɛ acidic. Nsusuw ho, hia asase nte — amane asase kura ne ho, asintiɛ asase pae, na loam asase kura ne ho na afei pae. Nhwiren foforo ho, asase ɛda wɔ nhwiren foforo dodo sen asase hoho.

English Question: Soil becomes hard from: overuse of heavy machinery which compacts the soil, lack of organic matter, repeatedly plowing at the same depth creating a hardpan layer, frequent flooding followed by drying, and low biological activity. To fix it, add organic matter, practice deep tillage occasionally, and use cover crops.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛma asase yɛ den na ɛhia yiye?
Twi Answer: Asase yɛ den fi: egyapade kɛse ho di dwuma dodo a ɛhia asase, nhwiren foforo aduan ho hia, bere biara boro asase sukyerɛ koro so a ɛyɛ hardpan, nsuo tenten a ɛto akyi na asase yera, ne nkwa a ɛdi asase mu hia. Sɛ wohwehwɛ siesie no a, de nhwiren foforo ka ho, bere bi boro asase mu tenten, na kura cover crops.

English Question: In Ghana, the best time to plant maize is at the beginning of the rainy season — March to April in the south, and May to June in the north. Plant when you have received at least 2-3 good rains so the soil is well moistened.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na ɛyɛ ɔkorɔ sɛ wode aburow to mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Wɔ Ghana, bere pa ara sɛ wode aburow to mu ne nsuo bere mfiase — Ɛbɔ kwan so Oforisuo wɔ apuei fam, na Ayɛwohomumo kwan so Mumu wɔ atifi fam. To aba mu bere a wanya nsu mmɛn 2-3 yie na asase no atenante yie.

English Question: Plant maize seeds 3-5 cm deep. If the soil is dry, plant slightly deeper to reach moisture. Space seeds 25-30 cm apart within rows and 75-90 cm between rows.
Twi Question: Ɛsukyerɛ bɛn na mede aburow aba to asase mu?
Twi Answer: De aburow aba to asase mu sɛntimita 3-5. Sɛ asase no yera a, to mu kakra dodo na wo nsa adu nsukuro ho. Gyae asukyerɛ 25-30 sɛntimita wɔ aba biara ntam na 75-90 sɛntimita wɔ nnua so ntam.

English Question: Crop rotation means growing different crops on the same land each season. For example, grow maize in season 1, then cowpea in season 2. This breaks pest cycles, improves soil fertility, and increases yields.
Twi Question: Dea ɛyɛ sɛ wosesa nnuaba gu asase mu na adɛn na ɛyɛ papa?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba sesae kyerɛ sɛ wokura ahorow nnuaba wɔ asase koro so bere biara. Nhwɛso so, kura aburow bere 1 mu, afei kura abɔdweɛ wɔ bere 2 mu. Eyi bubu adwummakers ntam, yɛ asase mu aduan ho nhwiren na ɛma nnuaba da sor dodo.

English Question: Choose certified seeds from reputable agro-input dealers. Good seeds are uniform in size, free from damage, and have a high germination rate of at least 85%. Avoid using seeds from the previous harvest for hybrid varieties.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mepaw aba pa sɛ mede to mu?
Twi Answer: Paw aba a wɔakyerɛw won fi agro-input atɔfo a wɔn din ayɛ pa. Aba pa yɛ pɛ wɔ boɔ mu, wɔ mfomso, na wɔn nyini yɛ kɛse sen 85%. Bɔ hwɛ de aba a wogye fi dɛm nnuaba meto aba hybrid aba no ase.

English Question: Clear the land of weeds and old crop residues. Plow or dig to loosen the soil to about 20-30 cm deep. Break up large clods and remove stones. Level the surface and apply basal fertilizer or compost before planting.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mesiesie asase aba to mu ansa?
Twi Answer: Yi sare ne nnua funu fi asase no so. Twa anaa hwe asase no mu kɔ sɛntimita 20- 30 mu. Bubu asase akɛse no na yi abo. Siesie fam no yiye na fa basal ferefere anaa compost gu so ansa na wode aba no agu fam.

English Question: Yes, you can grow vegetables in the dry season with irrigation. Crops like tomatoes, pepper, onions, leafy vegetables, and cucumbers grow well in dry season with proper watering.
Twi Question: Metumi adua nnɔbae wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu?
Twi Answer: Aane, wobetumi kura nnuan wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu sɛ wode nsuo gu so. Nnɔbae te sɛ ntomate, mako, gyeene, nhaban nnɔbae, ne cucumber nyini yiye wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu sɛ wode nsuo gu so yiye a.

English Question: Water seedlings well the day before transplanting. Transplant in the late afternoon or on a cloudy day to reduce heat stress. Dig the hole bigger than the root ball. Remove seedling from container carefully without disturbing roots. Firm soil around roots and water immediately. Provide shade for 2-3 days if needed.
Twi Question: Kwan bɛn na ɛyɛ papa a yɛfa so si nnua nketewa baabi foforo a ɛrenwu?
Twi Answer: Gu nnua nketewa no nsuo pii da a ɛdi kan ansa na wosi wɔn baabi foforo. Si wɔn baabi foforo anwummere anaa da a ewim yɛ nwunu na ama owia nhyew wɔn. Tu amoa a ɛsɛ kɛse sen ntini no. Yi nnua nketewa no fi nkuku mu brɛoo a wunhaw ntini no. Fa asase kata ntini no ho yiye na gu nsuo ntɛm ara. Fa sunsuma brɛ wɔn nna 2-3 sɛ ɛhia2.

English Question: Check germination 5-10 days after planting depending on the crop. Good germination means at least 80% of planted seeds have sprouted uniformly. If germination is poor, check if seeds were planted too deep, soil was too dry or waterlogged, temperature was too extreme, or seeds were old. Replant gaps with fresh seeds immediately.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na menim sɛ m'aba apue yie?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ sɛ aba no afifi nna 5-10 akyi a wode agu fam5. Sɛ aba no fifi yiye a, ɛkyerɛ sɛ aba a wode agu fam no 80% pɛ afifi pɛpɛɛpɛ80. Sɛ aba no mfifi yiye a, hwɛ sɛ wode agu fam dodo, asase no yɛ kusuu anaa nsuo dɔɔso wɔ mu, ewim yɛ hye anaa nwunu dodo, anaa aba no dedaw. Fa aba foforo gu mmeae a ɛda hɔ no ntɛm ara.

English Question: A nursery is a protected area where seeds are germinated and young plants are raised before transplanting to the main field. Use a nursery for: small expensive seeds like tomato, pepper, and onion; crops that need a head start before rains; and crops where seedling survival in the field is uncertain. Nurseries save seeds and improve stand establishment.
Twi Question: Nursery yɛ dɛn na bere bɛn na ɛsɛ sɛ yɛde di dwuma?
Twi Answer: Nursery yɛ beae a wɔbɔ ho ban a wɔde aba gu mu na wɔtete nnua nketewa ansa na wɔde akɔdua wɔ afuo kɛse no mu. Fa nursery di dwuma ma: aba nketewa a ne boɔ yɛ den te sɛ ntomate, mako, ne gyeene; nnɔbae a ɛhia sɛ wofi ase ntɛm ansa na osuo aba; ne nnɔbae a ɛnyɛ awiegye sɛ ɛbɛtena ase wɔ afuo no mu. Nursery boa ma aba no yɛ yiye na ɛma nnua no nyini yiye.

English Question: Yes, mixing vegetables is called companion planting and can be very beneficial. Good combinations include tomatoes with basil (basil repels tomato pests), maize with beans and squash (the Three Sisters method), onions with carrots (they repel each other's pests), and marigolds with any vegetable (repels many insects). Avoid planting crops from the same family together as they share pests.
Twi Question: Metumi adua nnɔbae ahorow pii wɔ afuo koro mu anaa?
Twi Answer: Aane, nnɔbae a wudua no bom yɛ companion planting na ɛboa pii. Nnuaba a wɔyɛ adwuma yie wɔ bom ne ntomato ne basil (basil kora ntomato adwummakers ase), aburow ne abɔdweɛ ne squash (Three Sisters anammɔn), gyene ne carrot (wɔkora wɔn ho adwummakers ase), na marigold ne nnuan biara (ɛkora adwummakers bebree ase). Hwɛ yiye na woannua nnɔbae a ɛwɔ abusua koro mu wɔ beae koro efisɛ wɔtaa nya yare koro.

English Question: On slopes, always plant across the slope (contour planting) rather than up and down. Make ridges along contour lines to hold water. Plant cover crops or grasses on the steepest parts. Use tied ridges (ridges with cross-ties every few meters) to capture rainwater. Mulch heavily to protect soil between plants.
Twi Question: Kwan bɛn na ɛsɛ sɛ mefa so dua nnɔbae wɔ mmepɔw so na ama nsuo anntu kɔ?
Twi Answer: Wɔ kwantempon so, to aba twa kwantempon so daa (contour planting) na mmom kɔ sor na gu ase. Yɛ ntwaho wɔ contour lines no ho na ama nsuo akora. To cover crops anaa atɛntɛnni wɔ beae a ɛkwan pa ara. Fa tied ridges (ntwaho a wɔne kyɛ ɛtɔ so baako biara) sɛ ɛgye osu nsuo. De mulch to so papaapa sɛ ɛkora asase nnuaba ntam.

English Question: Transplant tomato seedlings when they are 4-6 weeks old, have 4-6 true leaves, are 15-20 cm tall, and have a sturdy stem. Seedlings that are too young may not survive transplanting shock. Seedlings that are too old (over 8 weeks) become root-bound and may not establish well in the field.
Twi Question: Mfeɛ bɛn na ɛfata sɛ mesi ntomato nnuaba mfoforo ananmu?
Twi Answer: Si ntomato nnuaba mfoforo ananmu bere a wɔdin nnawotwe 4-6, wɔwɔ nhaban 4-6, wɔn soroɔ yɛ sɛntimita 15-20, na wɔwɔ tibo den. Nnuaba mfoforo a wɔkum dodo betumi ankyɛ si ananmu no ɔkɔm. Nnuaba mfoforo a wɔadin dodo (nnawotwe 8 kenkan) yɛ root-bound na betumi ansi yie wɔ afuo mu.

English Question: Raised bed farming means growing crops on elevated soil mounds or frames above the ground level. Benefits include better drainage, improved soil structure, easier weeding and harvesting, higher yield per square meter, better pest management, and ability to farm in poor soil areas. It is ideal for small spaces and home gardens.
Twi Question: Dɛn na raised bed farming yɛ na mfaaso bɛn na ɛwɔ?
Twi Answer: Raised bed farming kyerɛ kura nnuaba wɔ asase mounts anaa frame a ɛda sor sen asase soronko. Mfaaso ho ne: nsuo pue mu yie, asase mu siesie pa, nhaban tia ne nnuaba gye yɛ mmerɛ, nnuaba da sor dodo wɔ square meter biara mu, adwummakers hwɛ ase yie, na tumi kura wɔ asase a enni pa mu. Ɛfata afuo ketewa ne fie afuo.

English Question: Growing in containers is called container gardening. Use large buckets, old tires, plastic bags, or purpose-made pots. Fill with a mix of soil, compost, and sand for good drainage. Good container crops include tomatoes, peppers, leafy vegetables, herbs, and onions. Place in a sunny spot and water frequently as containers dry out faster than ground soil.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na mekura nnuaba wɔ nkuku anaa pots mu sɛ menni asase?
Twi Answer: Kura wɔ nkuku mu sɛ container gardening. Fa bucket kɛse, tayɛ kedee, plastik bags, anaa nkuku a wɔyɛ wɔn ho. Hye asase, compost, ne asintiɛ bom mu sɛ nsuo pue mu yie. Nnuaba a wɔda sor yie wɔ nkuku mu ne ntomato, mako, nhaban nnuan, nduaba aduan, ne gyene. Si wɔn wɔ beae a owia hye na de nsuo to pɛ efisɛ nkuku yera ntɛm sen asase.

English Question: This is likely the Fall Armyworm. Look inside the whorl for worms. Apply insecticides like emamectin benzoate early morning or late evening. Sand mixed with ash applied into the whorl also helps as an organic option.
Twi Question: M'aburow nhaban wɔ tumtum na wɔredidi won. Dɛn na meyɛ?
Twi Answer: Eyi tumi yɛ Fall Armyworm adwummaker. Hwɛ nhaban mu sɛ wɔhwehwɛ adwummakers anaa wɔ ho ntama. De adwummakers dawuro te sɛ emamectin benzoate guare owia da ano anaa nnɔnhwerew mu. Asintiɛ a waka nkamfo ka ho no tumi de gu nhaban mu sɛ nhwiren dawuro.

English Question: Dry the grain properly before storage to below 13% moisture. Use hermetic airtight bags which suffocate insects. You can also mix grain with diatomite dust or apply approved grain protectant chemicals.
Twi Question: Ɛdeɛn na metumi de weevils hyɛ ase wɔ m'aduan a maguina mu?
Twi Answer: Yaw aduan no yie ansa na waguina mu na ɛsua 13% nsuku. Fa hermetic bags a wɔapo so yie a ɛkum adwummakers wɔ mu. Wobetumi de aduan ka diatomite tukutuku ho anaa de aduan adwummakers dawuro a wɔagyei no to so.
