Yadeɛ a ɛtaa ba apataa ho ne ich (white spot), gill yadeɛ ne bacterial infections a wubetumi ahu wɔn ho de salt baths ne nkuru a wɔagyae so.

English Question: Starting a small commercial fish farm in Ghana with two earthen ponds of 500 square metres each costs approximately GHS 15,000 to 25,000 including pond construction, fingerlings, feed for one cycle, and basic equipment. A plastic tank fish farm can be started for GHS 8,000 to 15,000. The main ongoing costs are fish feed which accounts for 60 to 70 percent of total production cost. With good management you can make a profit from the first cycle.
Twi Question: Sika ahe na ɛyɛ papa sɛ mefi ase apataa adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Apataa adwuma ketewa kɛse fi ase wɔ Ghana de earthen ponds mmienu a square metres 500 biara wɔ mu ho teetee GHS 15,000 kɔ 25,000 a pond yɛ, fingerlings, aduan wɔ cycle baako mu, ne nneɛma a ɛyɛ papa. Plastic tank apataa adwuma wobetumi de GHS 8,000 kɔ 15,000 fi ase. Nneɛma a ɛkyere daadaa a ɛkɔ so pii ne apataa aduan a ɛyɛ adwuma agyapade 60 kɔ 70 percent. Sɛ woyɛ adwuma pa a, wobetumi anya mfaso wɔ cycle a ɛdi kan mu.

English Question: Harvest tilapia when they reach market size of 300 to 500 grams which typically takes 5 to 6 months from fingerling stage. Monitor growth by sampling fish monthly using a net. Harvest in the early morning when water temperature is cool to reduce fish stress. Partial harvesting at 4 months removes larger fish and allows smaller ones to grow. Sell fresh fish immediately or ice them for transport to market.
Twi Question: Bere bɛn na meyiyɛ me tilapia apataa?
Twi Answer: Yi tilapia bere a wɔkɔ si dwa kɛse a nnɔho 300 kɔ 500 gram a ɛtaa kyɛ mfee 5 kɔ 6 fi fingerling mu. Hwɛ sɛ apataa rebɛbo yie de sample apataa bere biara de net. Yi anɔpa bere a nsuo berɛ dɛ sɛ apataa nhunu. Partial yi wɔ mfee nnan mu yi apataa kɛse na ma nketewa bo sɔ. Tɔ apataa fofor ntɛm anaa de ice ka ho ma akɔ dwa.

English Question: Tilapia is easier to manage, tolerates lower water quality, feeds on plankton and algae as well as pellets, and is cheaper to produce. Catfish grows faster, commands a higher market price, tolerates very low oxygen levels but needs more protein in feed. Catfish farming gives higher profit per fish but requires more management. Many farmers in Ghana combine both species for diversified income.
Twi Question: Nte sɛn bɛn na ɛwɔ tilapia ne catfish adwuma ntam?
Twi Answer: Tilapia yɛ mmerɛw sɛ wohwɛ so, ɛtumi gyina nsuo a ɛnni yie, ɛdi plankton ne algae ne pellets nso, na bo wɔ to a ɛsua. Catfish bo sɔ ntɛm, dwa bo yɛ so sen, ɛtumi gyina oxygen nketewa a wɔ nsuo mu nanso ɛhia protein pii wɔ aduan mu. Catfish adwuma de mfaso kɛse ba ma apataa baako baako nanso ɛhia adwuma pii. Akuafo pii wɔ Ghana de nhyiamu mmienu kaa bom sɛ wɔnya owuo-teetee foforo.

English Question: Decide whether to raise broilers for meat or layers for eggs. Build or rent a poultry house that is well ventilated, predator-proof and has adequate space of 0.1 square metres per broiler or 0.2 square metres per layer. Source day-old chicks from reputable hatcheries. Provide feed, clean water, light and warmth from a brooder for the first 2 weeks. Vaccinate against Newcastle disease and Gumboro disease. Broilers are ready in 6 to 7 weeks and layers start laying at 18 to 20 weeks.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mefi ase akoko adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Siesie wo tiri ma broilers wɔ nam ho anaa layers wɔ tamma ho. Tu anaa sowa akoko fie a mframa fa mu yie, adwummaker ntumi nkɔ mu, na ahorow teetee wɔ hɔ sɛ 0.1 square metres biara broiler anaa 0.2 square metres biara layer. Gye day-old chicks fi hatcheries a wɔni gyinae. De aduan, nsuo pa, kanea ne berɛhyɛ fi brooder ma nnansa mmienu a ɛdi kan. Hware wɔ so ma Newcastle yadeɛ ne Gumboro yadeɛ. Broilers atwa so nnansas nsia kɔ nson akyi na layers fi ase gu tamma nnansas duodu nwɔtwe kɔ aduonu.

English Question: Newcastle disease is the most serious threat to poultry in Ghana. Prevent it through strict vaccination using Lasota vaccine at day 7, day 21 and every 2 months thereafter. Keep visitors away from your poultry house, disinfect equipment and footwear before entering, quarantine new birds for 2 weeks, buy birds from certified sources only, and cull sick birds immediately. There is no treatment for Newcastle disease once birds are infected.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ Newcastle yadeɛ annya me akoko?
Twi Answer: Newcastle yadeɛ ne akoko tia a ɛtaa yɛ den paa wɔ Ghana. Gye wo ho fi mu de Lasota hware aba ahyɛ so mu da 7, da 21 na mprɛn mmienu biara wɔ saa akyi. Ma ahofipa anyɛ kwan kɔ wo akoko fie, hware nneɛma ne nan so ansa na wukɔ mu, kora nnomaa foforɔ wɔ baabi foforo nnansas mmienu, gye nnomaa fi hɔ a wɔakyerɛw so pɛ, na kum nnomaa a wayarɛ ntɛm. Newcastle yadeɛ nni dawuro bere a nnomaa no anya mu.

English Question: Feed broilers starter crumbles for the first 2 weeks with 22 to 24 percent protein, then grower pellets with 18 to 20 percent protein from week 3 to 5, and finisher pellets with 16 to 18 percent protein in the final weeks. Provide fresh clean water at all times. Popular feed brands in Ghana include Darko Farms, Akate Wura and Ghana Feedmill feeds. Feed represents 70 percent of your production cost so buying quality feed is critical.
Twi Question: Aduan bɛn na mede ma me broiler akoko?
Twi Answer: De starter crumbles a protein 22 kɔ 24 percent wɔ mu ma broilers nnansas mmienu a ɛdi kan, afei grower pellets a protein 18 kɔ 20 percent wɔ mu wɔ nnansa mmiɛnsa kɔ num, na finisher pellets a protein 16 kɔ 18 percent wɔ mu wɔ nnansas a etwa to. De nsuo fofor pa to mu bere nyinaa. Feed brands a wɔpɛ wɔ Ghana ne Darko Farms, Akate Wura na Ghana Feedmill feeds. Aduan yɛ wo adwuma agyapade 70 percent enti gye aduan pa hia.

English Question: Heat stress is common in Ghana and reduces growth rate and egg production. Manage it by ensuring good ventilation in the poultry house, providing cool fresh water frequently, installing foggers or sprinklers on the roof, feeding in the cooler parts of the day morning and evening, reducing stocking density during hot seasons, adding vitamin C and electrolytes to water during extreme heat, and considering open-sided housing designs.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ berɛhyɛ den a ɛba me akoko ho?
Twi Answer: Berɛhyɛ den taa ba wɔ Ghana na ɛhia boɛ a aba nhia na tamma nhia. Boa ho de hwɛ sɛ mframa fa akoko fie mu yie, de nsuo dɛ foforɔ to mu bere biara, si foggers anaa sprinklers wɔ fie no atifi so, didi wɔ berɛ dɛ mu anɔpa ne anwumere, sua akoko a wɔwɔ mu wɔ berɛhyɛ bere, de vitamin C ne electrolytes ka nsuo mu wɔ hyehyɛ den bere, na twe wo adwene ho open-sided housing nhyiamu.

English Question: A good commercial layer hen like Lohmann Brown or Hy-Line can produce 280 to 320 eggs per year under good management. In Ghana with challenges of heat and disease, expect 200 to 260 eggs per year under average management. Egg production starts declining after 72 weeks of age. After this point, evaluate whether to cull the flock and start with new chicks or continue with the declining layers.
Twi Question: Tamma ahe na layer akoko gu wɔ afe baako mu?
Twi Answer: Layer kɛse pa te sɛ Lohmann Brown anaa Hy-Line tumi gu tamma 280 kɔ 320 afe baako mu sɛ wohwɛ so yie. Wɔ Ghana a berɛhyɛ ne yadeɛ yɛ den a, gyina tamma 200 kɔ 260 afe baako mu sɛ wohwɛ so yie kakra. Tamma gu a ɛkɔ so huna wɔ nnansas 72 akyi. Wɔ saa bere no, twe wo adwene ho sɛ kum flock no na fi ase de chicks foforɔ anaa gyina so de layers a ɛhuna no.

English Question: Start with 5 to 10 does and 1 buck. Common breeds in Ghana include the West African Dwarf goat which is hardy and disease-resistant, and the Sahelian goat which is larger. Construct a simple raised pen with wooden or wire sides that is dry, well ventilated and predator-proof. Feed on grass, crop residues, groundnut hay and supplement with salt licks. Vaccinate against PPR (Peste des Petits Ruminants) which is the most serious goat disease.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mefi ase birekyie adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Fi ase de mmirikyi 5 kɔ 10 ne ɔbarima baako. Breeds a wɔpɛ wɔ Ghana ne West African Dwarf birekyie a ɛyɛ den na yadeɛ ntumi nhu, na Sahelian birekyie a ɛso sen. Tu pen a ɛtele ne dua anaa waya ho a ɛyɛ dɛ, mframa fa mu yie na adwummaker ntumi nkɔ mu. Didi nhawan, nnuaba a ato fɛw, groundnut hay na de salt licks ka ho. Hware so ma PPR (Peste des Petits Ruminants) yadeɛ a ɛyɛ birekyie yadeɛ den pa ara.

English Question: Vaccinate goats against PPR (Peste des Petits Ruminants) annually as this is the most deadly goat disease in Ghana. Also vaccinate against CCPP (Contagious Caprine Pleuropneumonia), foot and mouth disease if in high-risk areas, and enterotoxaemia. Deworm every 3 months using ivermectin or albendazole. Control external parasites like ticks and lice with acaricide dipping or spraying. Consult your nearest MOFA veterinary officer for a vaccination schedule.
Twi Question: Yadeɛ bɛn na mahware me birekyie so?
Twi Answer: Hware birekyie so ma PPR (Peste des Petits Ruminants) afe biara efisɛ yadeɛ yi ne birekyie yadeɛ a ɛkum paa wɔ Ghana. Hware nso ma CCPP (Contagious Caprine Pleuropneumonia), nan ne anom yadeɛ sɛ wɔ hɔ a ɛyɛ den ho, na enterotoxaemia. Wia adwummaker wɔ ho mprɛnsa mmiɛnsa de ivermectin anaa albendazole. Boa external parasites te sɛ ticks ne lice ho de acaricide dipping anaa hware. Bisa wo MOFA vet offisa a ɛbɛn wo ho ma vaccination schedule.

English Question: Goats are browsers that prefer leaves, shrubs and crop by-products over grass. Feed them a mixture of fresh grass and leaves, crop residues like maize stalks and groundnut haulms, hay, and concentrate feeds for pregnant or lactating does. Always provide clean water and mineral salt licks. Never feed moldy or rotten feed. Goats can also browse freely in managed areas to supplement their feeding.
Twi Question: Dɛn na birekyie di na dɛn na mede ma wɔn yie?
Twi Answer: Birekyie yɛ browsers a wɔpɛ nhaban, nhaban ketewa ne nnuaba a ato fɛw sen nhawan. Ma wɔn nhawan foforɔ ne nhaban ahohiana, nnuaba a ato fɛw te sɛ aburoɔ abɔ ne groundnut saa, hay, na concentrate feeds ma mmirikyi a ɛwɔ aninso anaa a wɔwɔ nsuo mu. De nsuo pa ne mineral salt licks to mu bere nyinaa. Mma aduan a mold aba ho anaa a asɛe amma wɔn. Birekyie nso betumi abrowse wɔ baabi a wɔhwɛ so sɛ wɔkaa wɔn didi ho.

English Question: Common sheep breeds in Ghana include the West African Dwarf Sheep and the Djallonke. Start with 5 to 10 ewes and 1 ram. House them in a raised pen that protects from rain, predators and parasites. Sheep are good grazers and can be kept on crop residues, grass and hay. Vaccinate against PPR annually. Sheep reach maturity and can be sold for meat at 6 to 12 months. Sheep are highly profitable during festive seasons like Eid and Christmas.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mefi ase oguan adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Oguan breeds a wɔpɛ wɔ Ghana ne West African Dwarf Sheep ne Djallonke. Fi ase de mmirikyi 5 kɔ 10 ne ɔbarima baako. Sie wɔn wɔ pen a ɛtele a ɛhwɛ wɔn so fi nsuo, adwummaker ne parasites. Oguan taa didi nhawan yie na wobetumi akora wɔn wɔ nnuaba a ato fɛw, nhawan ne hay so. Hware so ma PPR afe biara. Oguan twa so na wubetumi atɔ wɔn ma nam sɛ mfee nsia kɔ duodu akyi. Oguan bo tɔ sen paa bere a afenhyia ba te sɛ Eid ne Bosome Dɔ.

English Question: Sheep are grazers that prefer grass while goats are browsers that eat leaves and shrubs. Sheep are generally more docile and easier to manage in groups. Goats are more curious and tend to escape from enclosures. Goat meat commands a slightly higher price in Ghanaian markets. Sheep wool is not commercially harvested in Ghana as local breeds have hair not wool. Both require similar health management including PPR vaccination.
Twi Question: Nte sɛn kɛse a ɛwɔ oguan ne birekyie adwuma ntam?
Twi Answer: Oguan di nhawan na birekyie di nhaban ne nhahan foforo. Oguan yɛ abodwo na ɛyɛ mmerɛw sɛ wohwɛ so kuo mu. Birekyie hunu ho ho na ɛtaa fi pen mu. Birekyie nam dwa bo yɛ so kakra sen wɔ Ghana dwa mu. Oguan len nni adwuma kɛse wɔ Ghana efisɛ local breeds wɔ nhwirɛ a ɛte sɛ afohyɛ na len. Wɔn mmienu hia health hwɛ koro a PPR vaccination ka ho.

English Question: Cattle farming requires significant capital and land. Common breeds in Ghana include the West African Shorthorn, White Fulani and Red Fulani. Start with 5 to 10 cows and 1 bull. Secure adequate grazing land of at least 1 hectare per animal or have a crop and fodder production plan. Vaccinate against CBPP, FMDV and rinderpest. Deworm quarterly. Keep records of breeding, feeding and health. Consider joining the National Cattle Farmers Association for market access and support.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mefi ase nnwan adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Nnwan adwuma hia sika kɛse ne asase. Breeds a wɔpɛ wɔ Ghana ne West African Shorthorn, White Fulani ne Red Fulani. Fi ase de nnwankow 5 kɔ 10 ne ɔbarima baako. Hwɛ sɛ nhawan asase ho hia sɛ hectare baako biara nnwan anaa wɔ nnuaba ne fodder to mu plan. Hware so ma CBPP, FMDV ne rinderpest. Wia adwummaker mprɛnsa nnan. Kora nsɛm ho sɛ bɔhyɛ, aduan ne health. Twe wo adwene ho fi ase wɔ National Cattle Farmers Association ho ma dwa kɔ ho ne mmoa.

English Question: Essential vaccines for cattle in Ghana include CBPP (Contagious Bovine Pleuropneumonia) vaccine given annually, FMD (Foot and Mouth Disease) vaccine twice yearly in endemic areas, blackleg vaccine for calves and Lumpy Skin Disease vaccine. Contact your nearest Veterinary Services Directorate office under MOFA for the current vaccination programme and schedule. Government vaccination campaigns also take place periodically and are subsidized.
Twi Question: Vaccines bɛn na nnwan hia wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Vaccines a nnwan hia wɔ Ghana ne CBPP (Contagious Bovine Pleuropneumonia) vaccine a wɔde to ho afe biara, FMD (Foot and Mouth Disease) vaccine mprɛn mmienu afe biara wɔ hɔ a yadeɛ wɔ, blackleg vaccine ma calves ne Lumpy Skin Disease vaccine. Ka Veterinary Services Directorate ofisi a ɛbɛn wo wɔ MOFA ase sɛ wɔde vaccination programme foforɔ ne schedule no bɛkyerɛ wo. Aban vaccination campaigns nso wɔ bere biara na wɔde nsua.

English Question: Trypanosomiasis also called nagana or sleeping sickness in cattle is transmitted by the tsetse fly and is common in the forest and transition zones of Ghana. Affected cattle show weight loss, anaemia, enlarged lymph nodes, fever and eventually death. Control by treating affected animals with diminazene aceturate, managing tsetse fly through bush clearing and insecticide-treated traps, and keeping cattle in areas with low tsetse fly populations. N'Dama and West African Shorthorn breeds have natural tolerance.
Twi Question: Trypanosomiasis yɛ dɛn na ɛyɛ nnwan den te sɛn wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Trypanosomiasis a wɔfre no nagana anaa sleeping sickness wɔ nnwan mu ne yadeɛ a tsetse fly de tete na ɛtaa ba wɔ Ghana kwaeɛ ne ntam zones. Nnwan a yadeɛ aba ho hunu nnɔho, wɔ mogya wɔn mu, lymph nodes a ɛso, oniwa ne owu awiei pɛ. Boa ho de hu nnwan a yadeɛ aba ho de diminazene aceturate, tsetse fly hwɛ de kuro tokuru ne insecticide-treated traps, na kora nnwan wɔ hɔ a tsetse fly nni so pii. N'Dama ne West African Shorthorn breeds wɔ tumi a ɛfa wɔn ankasa.

English Question: Start small with crops that need minimal investment like vegetables, maize or cassava. Begin with what land you have access to. Use family labour initially to reduce costs. Join a farmer-based organisation for access to group inputs and credit. Apply for the government Planting for Food and Jobs programme which provides subsidized seeds and fertilizer. Reinvest your profits to gradually expand your farm each season.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mefi ase okuafo adwuma wɔ Ghana a sika ketewa wɔ me nkyɛn?
Twi Answer: Fi ase ketewa de nnuaba a sika ketewa na ɛhia te sɛ nnuaba, aburoɔ anaa bankye. Fi ase wɔ asase a wowɔ ho. De wo fie ho adwuma ansa na ɛhia sika. Ka okuafo kuo ho sɛ wɔde group inputs ne credit nya. Bisa aban Planting for Food and Jobs programme a wɔde subsidized aba ne ferefere to. De wo mfaso no to wo afuom no so bere biara ma ɛkɔ so kɛse tenten tenten.

English Question: To register a farm business in Ghana, you need a Ghana Card or valid national ID, a business name, your address, and a business plan. Register your business name with the Registrar General's Department. For tax purposes, register with the Ghana Revenue Authority to get a TIN. If you want to access formal credit, you may also need to open a business bank account and join a recognised farmer group.
Twi Question: Krataa bɛn na mɛhia sɛ meregyina me afuom adwuma ho wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wobɛsi wo afuom adwuma ho wɔ Ghana a, wo hia Ghana Card anaa national ID a ɛwɔ mu, adwuma din, wo address, na business plan. Si wo adwuma din ho wɔ Registrar General's Department. Ma tax ho, si ho wɔ Ghana Revenue Authority ma wo nya TIN. Sɛ wohia credit a, wobetumi nso hia sɛ wubue adwuma bank account na ka okuafo kuo a wɔakyerɛw ho.

English Question: A simple farm business plan should include your farm description and location, the crops or animals you plan to produce, how much land you have, your production costs for inputs seeds fertilizer labour and equipment, expected yields and prices, how you plan to sell your produce, and your profit projection. Keep it simple and realistic. You can get a template from MOFA extension offices or agricultural NGOs like GSMA or Agric-Ahaban.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ meyɛ me afuom adwuma plan ketewa?
Twi Answer: Afuom adwuma plan ketewa nni yie sɛ ɛwɔ wo afuom ho nsɛm ne ɛhɔ a ɛwɔ, nnuaba anaa mmoa a wopɛ sɛ woto mu, asase a wowɔ, wo adwuma agyapade ho sika sɛ inputs, aba, ferefere, adwuma ne nneɛma, nnoa a wohwia ne bo a wohwia, ɛkwan a wopɛ sɛ wode wo nnuaba tɔ, na sika a wohwia sɛ wobɛnya. Ma no yɛ mmerɛw na ɛteɛ. Wobetumi anya template fi MOFA extension offices anaa NGOs te sɛ GSMA anaa Agric-Ahaban.

English Question: Agricultural loans in Ghana are available from Agricultural Development Bank (ADB) which specializes in farming loans, Rural and Community Banks in your area, the ARB Apex Bank, microfinance institutions, and through government schemes like the Planting for Food and Jobs credit component. The Ghana Incentive-Based Risk Sharing System for Agricultural Lending (GIRSAL) provides guarantees to encourage banks to lend to farmers. Always compare interest rates and repayment terms before borrowing.
Twi Question: Ɛhɔ na metumi anya okuafo mfɛdomhyɛw wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Okuafo mfɛdomhyɛw wɔ Ghana wɔ Agricultural Development Bank (ADB) a ɛtaa ma okuafo mfɛdomhyɛw, Rural ne Community Banks a ɛbɛn wo, ARB Apex Bank, microfinance institutions, na aban schemes te sɛ Planting for Food and Jobs credit component. Ghana Incentive-Based Risk Sharing System for Agricultural Lending (GIRSAL) de hyɛ banks so sɛ wɔma okuafo mfɛdomhyɛw. Fa interest rates ne repayment ho nsɛm twe ntam ansa na wobɔ mfɛdomhyɛw.

English Question: To get better prices for your farm produce, time your sales to avoid market gluts by selling when supply is low, join a farmer cooperative to negotiate collectively, add value through processing before selling, sell directly to restaurants, schools or supermarkets, use aggregator platforms and apps like Farmerline Esoko and Ghana Agricultural Market Information System, build relationships with reliable buyers, and diversify to multiple buyers.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ metɔ me afuom nnuaba wɔ bo a ɛso sen?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wobɛnya wo afuom nnuaba bo a ɛso sen a, siesie wo tɔ bere sɛ wo bɛtɔ bere a nnuaba nni ho pii, ka okuafo kuo ho sɛ wobɔ bo kaa bom, de wo nnuaba yɛ aduan ansa na wotɔ, tɔ straight kɔ adidibea, sukuu anaa supermarkets, de aggregator platforms ne apps te sɛ Farmerline Esoko ne Ghana Agricultural Market Information System, kora wo adwene ho buyers a wɔ gyinae, na tɔ kuo mmerantee ho.

English Question: Profitability depends on scale, management and market access. High profit crops include vegetables especially tomatoes, pepper and onion under irrigation, mushroom farming which gives quick returns, snail farming with low inputs, broiler poultry with fast turnover, fish farming especially catfish, and cashew farming for export. The key is to choose something you understand well, have a reliable market for, and can manage consistently. Start with one enterprise before diversifying.
Twi Question: Okuafo adwuma bɛn na ɛde mfaso ba sen wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Mfaso no kyɛ sɛ kɛse bɛn na woyɛ, dɛn na woyɛ na dwa kɔ ho. Nnuaba a ɛde mfaso ba sen ne nnuaba ahorow a ɛhia pii te sɛ tomatoes, pepper ne abɔnkɔ wɔ quench ase, mushroom adwuma a ɛde sika ntɛm, snail adwuma a sika ketewa na ɛhia, broiler poultry a ɛde sika ntɛm, apataa adwuma a ɛhia pii ne catfish, na cashew adwuma ma export. Asɛde a ɛyɛ papa ne: yi biribi a wohu mu yie, wowɔ dwa gyinae, na wobetumi ahwɛ so bere biara. Fi ase de adwuma baako ansa na woyɛ pii.

English Question: To apply for the Planting for Food and Jobs programme, visit your nearest District Department of Agriculture office under the Ministry of Food and Agriculture. Bring your Ghana Card, proof of land ownership or land use agreement, and your farm location. Register as a beneficiary farmer. Subsidized inputs including seeds and fertilizers are then distributed through licensed agro-dealers in your district. The programme covers maize, rice, soybean, sorghum, vegetables and other crops.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mebisa Planting for Food and Jobs programme?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wobɛbisa Planting for Food and Jobs programme a, kɔ wo District Department of Agriculture ofisi a ɛbɛn wo wɔ Ministry of Food and Agriculture ase. De wo Ghana Card, asase ho evidence anaa asase de adi nhyiamu krataa, na wo afuom hɔ. Si ho sɛ beneficiary okuafo. Inputs a wɔde asua te sɛ aba ne ferefere na wɔde kyɛ wɔ licensed agro-dealers mu wɔ wo district mu. Programme no fa aburoɔ, ɔmo, soybean, sorghum, nnuaba ne nnuaba foforɔ ho.

English Question: A good crop rotation for Ghana is to plant legumes like cowpea or groundnut after cereals like maize or sorghum. Legumes fix nitrogen into the soil improving fertility naturally. A 3-year rotation could be maize in year one, cowpea in year two, and cassava or vegetables in year three. Avoid planting the same crop family in the same field two seasons in a row as this builds up pests and diseases specific to that crop.
Twi Question: Adekuo nhyiamu bɛn na ɛhia pa ara wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Adekuo nhyiamu pa wɔ Ghana ne de legumes te sɛ bɔde anaa groundnut to mu akyi cereals te sɛ aburoɔ anaa sorghum. Legumes de nitrogen ka asase mu a ɛboa asase aduan pa. Mfe mmiɛnsa rotation bɛtumi ayɛ: aburoɔ mfe a ɛdi kan mu, bɔde mfe mmienu mu, na bankye anaa nnuaba mfe mmiɛnsa mu. Gye wo ho fi de nnuaba nhyiamu koro to mu wɔ afuom koro mfe mmienu so kwa efisɛ eyi ma adwummaker ne yadeɛ a ɛfa nhyiamu no ho kɔ so.

English Question: Post-harvest losses in Ghana can be up to 40 percent of the harvest. Reduce losses by harvesting at the right maturity stage, handling produce gently to avoid bruising, drying produce properly before storage, using improved hermetic storage bags like GrainPro or metal silos for grains, building ventilated storage for roots and tubers, processing excess produce into value-added products, and connecting to buyers before harvest to reduce time between field and market.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ ho sɛ me nnuaba nhunu yi akyi?
Twi Answer: Nnuaba ahunu akyi yi Ghana bɛtumi akosi 40 percent. Sua ahunu de yi bere a ɛyɛ papa pa, dii wo nnuaba no yie sɛ ɛnsɔre, ma nnuaba no tew yie ansa na woguina mu, de improved hermetic storage bags te sɛ GrainPro anaa metal silos ma aba, tu ventilated storage ma nnɔho biara, de nnuaba a ɛboro so yɛ aduan a bo kɔ so, na ka buyers ho ansa na wuyi sɛ ɛhia bere ketewa wɔ afuom ne dwa ntam.

English Question: Record keeping is essential for farm business success. Keep records of all inputs purchased with costs, planting dates and quantities, labour costs, yields from each plot, sales amounts and buyer details, and animal health records. Good records help you calculate real profit, identify what is working and what is not, qualify for bank loans, plan better for the next season, and comply with certification requirements if you want to sell to premium markets.
Twi Question: Ɛho hia sɛn ara sɛ wɔkora nsɛm wɔ afuom adwuma mu?
Twi Answer: Nsɛm kora ho hia pa ara ma afuom adwuma bo so. Kora nsɛm ho sɛ inputs nyinaa a wagye ne sika, to aba bere ne dodoɔ, adwuma sika, nnoa a afuom biara fi, tɔ sika ne buyer ho nsɛm, na mmoa health ho nsɛm. Nsɛm a wɔakora yie boa wo sɛ wobɛbu real mfaso, hunu biribi a ɛyɛ yie ne a ɛnyɛ yie, twerɛ bo sɛ bank loans hia, siesie wo adwuma yie ma bere a ɛdi hɔ, na tia certification ho nhia sɛ wopɛ sɛ wotɔ kɔ premium markets.

English Question: Maize streak virus causes yellow streaks running along the leaf veins giving leaves a striped appearance. It is transmitted by the leafhopper insect. There is no cure once a plant is infected. Control by planting resistant varieties like Obatanpa and Mamaba from CSIR, destroying infected plants early, and controlling leafhoppers with appropriate insecticides. Avoid late planting as late-planted fields suffer more leafhopper attacks.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛkyerɛ maize streak virus na dɛn na menyɛ ho?
Twi Answer: Maize streak virus ma nhaban ho yɛ yellow streaks a ɛkɔ wɔ nhaban abɔ ho na ɛma nhaban no yɛ stripes. Leafhopper adwummaker de tete. Yadeɛ no nni dawuro bere a nnuaba nya mu. Boa ho de resistant varieties te sɛ Obatanpa ne Mamaba fi CSIR to mu, yi nnuaba a yadeɛ aba ho ntɛm, na de insecticides hware leafhoppers so. Gye wo ho fi late to mu efisɛ afuom a wɔde to mu akyi sen no nya leafhopper atia sen.

English Question: Aflatoxin is a deadly poison produced by Aspergillus fungi that grows on improperly dried or stored maize. It causes liver cancer and can kill animals and humans. Prevent aflatoxin by drying maize properly to below 13 percent moisture before storage, using hermetic storage bags or metal silos, inspecting stored grain regularly and discarding mouldy grain, using aflasafe biocontrol product, and never feeding visibly mouldy grain to animals.
Twi Question: Aflatoxin yɛ dɛn wɔ aburoɔ mu na dɛn na menyɛ sɛ ɛnnya?
Twi Answer: Aflatoxin yɛ poisons a ɛyɛ den a Aspergillus fungi a ɛso wɔ aburoɔ a wonma no tew yie anaa a wonguina yie ho de ba. Ɛma akokoaa yareɛ na etumi kum mmoa ne nnipa. Gye aflatoxin fi ho de ma aburoɔ no tew yie kɔ 13 percent nsuo ase ansa na woguina, de hermetic storage bags anaa metal silos, hwɛ aba a woguina bere biara na yi aba a mold aba ho, de aflasafe biocontrol de, na mma aba a mold aba ho amma mmoa.

English Question: Yes you can grow maize in the dry season but you need irrigation. Dry season maize in Ghana is most common in the Volta Basin, Afram Plains and parts of northern Ghana where irrigation schemes exist. Use short-duration varieties that mature in 75 to 90 days. Drip or furrow irrigation works well. Dry season maize often fetches higher prices because supply is low. The main challenge is the higher cost of water and risk of heat stress.
Twi Question: Metumi ato aburoɔ wɔ bone berɛ wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Aane wobetumi ato aburoɔ wɔ bone berɛ nanso wohia quench. Bone berɛ aburoɔ wɔ Ghana taa ba wɔ Volta Basin, Afram Plains ne Ghana atifi ho bi a quench schemes wɔ hɔ. De short-duration varieties a ɛtwa so adays 75 kɔ 90 mu. Drip anaa furrow quench yɛ yie. Bone berɛ aburoɔ dwa bo tɔ sen paa bere biara efisɛ nnuaba nni so pii. Aho yɛ den ne nsuo sika a ɛboro so ne berɛhyɛ den yɛ haw.

English Question: Choose your maize variety based on the rainfall pattern of your area, the soil type, and your market. For the forest zone with high rainfall, use medium to late maturing varieties like Abontem or Mamaba. For the savanna and transition zones, use drought-tolerant varieties like Obatanpa, Wari or Aburohemaa. For household consumption, choose floury white varieties. For animal feed, yellow varieties like Dobidi have higher energy content. Buy certified seed from licensed dealers.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mepick aburoɔ aba variety pa wɔ me ɛhɔ ho?
Twi Answer: Yi wo aburoɔ variety sɛ nsuo a ɛtɔ bere wɔ wo hɔ, asase nhyiamu, na wo dwa so. Ma kwaeɛ zone a nsuo tɔ pii ho, de medium kɔ late maturing varieties te sɛ Abontem anaa Mamaba. Ma savanna ne ntam zones ho, de drought-tolerant varieties te sɛ Obatanpa, Wari anaa Aburohemaa. Ma efie didi, yi floury white varieties. Ma mmoa aduan, yellow varieties te sɛ Dobidi wɔ energy pii mu. Gye certified seed fi licensed dealers.

English Question: Minimum tillage means disturbing the soil as little as possible when preparing for planting. Instead of full ploughing, you make only planting holes or shallow furrows. Benefits include reduced soil erosion, preserved soil structure, lower fuel and labour costs, and better moisture retention. For maize minimum tillage works well especially when combined with mulching of crop residues. However it requires good weed management as weeds can be a bigger problem without full land preparation.
Twi Question: Minimum tillage yɛ dɛn na ɛtumi yɛ adwuma wɔ aburoɔ afuom?
Twi Answer: Minimum tillage kyerɛ sɛ wohaw asase ketewa ketewa bere a wosiesie sɛ wode aba to mu. Nti na wonfɛn asase pɛpɛɛpɛ, woyɛ awia pɛ anaa furrows ketewa pɛ. Mfaaso ne: asase erosion nsen, asase nhyiamu aguina, fuel ne adwuma sika sua, na nsuo aguina yie. Ma aburoɔ minimum tillage yɛ adwuma yie a ɛhia pii bere a wode nnuaba a ato fɛw mulch ka ho. Nanso ɛhia nhaban foforo hwɛ pa efisɛ nhaban foforo tumi yɛ den wɔ asase a wonhaw yie mu.

English Question: The best cassava varieties for fufu in Ghana are Afisiafi and Bankye Hemaa because they have high starch content, good texture when pounded, and stretch well. Dente and Abasafitaa are also good for fufu. Avoid watery or low-starch varieties as they produce poor-quality fufu. The cassava should be fresh and not overripe for best fufu quality.
Twi Question: Bankye variety bɛn na ɛhia pa ara ma fufu yɛ?
Twi Answer: Bankye varieties a ɛhia pa ara ma fufu yɛ wɔ Ghana ne Afisiafi ne Bankye Hemaa efisɛ wɔwɔ starch pii, texture pa bere a wode dome, na ɛtete yie. Dente ne Abasafitaa nso yɛ yie ma fufu. Gye wo ho fi watery anaa low-starch varieties efisɛ wɔde fufu a ɛnni yie yɛ. Bankye no nni yie sɛ ɛyɛ foforɔ na ɛantwa so akyi pa ara ma fufu pa.

English Question: Peel and wash fresh cassava. Grate or chip the cassava into small pieces. Dry the pieces on clean raised platforms in the sun for 2 to 3 days until completely dry. Alternatively use a mechanical dryer. Mill the dried chips into flour using a hammer mill. Sieve to get uniform flour. Store in sealed bags in a dry place. Cassava flour can be used for bread, pastries, banku and as a thickener. It has a shelf life of 6 to 12 months when properly stored.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ bankye flour fi bankye foforɔ?
Twi Answer: Yi bankye no ho na hohoro. Grate anaa twa bankye no yɛ chips ketewa. Ma chips no tew wɔ platforms a ɛtele na ɛpaa owia so adays mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa kosi sɛ ɛtew pɛpɛɛpɛ. Anaa de mechanical dryer. Fɛn chips a ɛatew no yɛ flour de hammer mill. Sie fi mu sɛ flour a ɛte so yie. Guina wɔ bags a wɔato mu wɔ baabi a ɛdɛ. Bankye flour bɛtumi de yɛ paanoo, pastries, banku na sɛ thickener. Ɛtumi gyina agyapade 6 kɔ 12 mfe mu sɛ wode guina yie.

English Question: To make meaningful profit from cassava you need at least 2 to 5 acres. With improved varieties and good management, 5 acres can yield 40 to 75 tonnes of fresh cassava. At current market rates this translates to GHS 24,000 to 45,000 in revenue. After deducting costs of GHS 6,000 to 10,000 for a 5-acre farm, profit can be GHS 14,000 to 35,000 per season. Processing into gari or starch doubles or triples this profit.
Twi Question: Asase ahe na mɛhia sɛ bankye adwuma ade sika ba?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wobɛnya mfaso pa fi bankye mu a, wohia sɛ eka mmienu kɔ num pɛ. De improved varieties ne adwuma pa, eka num tumi de bankye foforɔ nnɔho 40 kɔ 75 tonne. Wɔ dwa bo a wɔwɔ saa ara, eyi bɛyɛ GHS 24,000 kɔ 45,000. Nnuaha wo costs GHS 6,000 kɔ 10,000 ma eka num afuom akyi, mfaso bɛtumi ayɛ GHS 14,000 kɔ 35,000 bere biara. De yɛ gari anaa starch a ɛde mfaso mmienu anaa mmiɛnsa ba.

English Question: Under traditional smallholder management, palm oil yield is 1 to 2 tonnes per hectare per year. With improved Tenera varieties and proper management including fertilization and pest control, yield increases to 4 to 6 tonnes of palm oil per hectare. A mature well-managed plantation of 10 hectares can produce 40 to 60 tonnes of palm oil annually worth GHS 200,000 to 300,000. Palm oil prices are relatively stable making it a reliable long-term investment.
Twi Question: Abɛ ɔman ahe na ɛfiri hectare baako mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Wɔ traditional smallholder adwuma mu, abɛ ɔman aba yɛ tonnes baako kɔ mmienu biara hectare biara afe biara. De improved Tenera varieties ne adwuma pa a ferefere ne adwummaker hwɛ ka ho, nnoa kɔ tonnes 4 kɔ 6 abɛ ɔman biara hectare. Plantation a ɛatwa so na wohwɛ so yie a ɛtelɛ hectares 10 tumi de abɛ ɔman tonnes 40 kɔ 60 ba afe biara a ɛbɛyɛ GHS 200,000 kɔ 300,000. Abɛ ɔman bo yɛ so paa a ɛma ɛyɛ investment pa ma akyi.

English Question: Sudden death syndrome in broilers is common and caused by metabolic disorders due to fast growth rates. Other causes include Gumboro disease which destroys the immune system, Newcastle disease, infectious bronchitis, ammonia poisoning from dirty litter, water deprivation, heat stress and cardiac arrest. Maintain good ventilation, provide clean water always, vaccinate regularly, manage litter properly and avoid pushing birds to extreme growth rates through excessive feeding.
Twi Question: Dɛn ma broiler akoko wu ntɛm?
Twi Answer: Broilers wu ntɛm yɛ adwuma a ɛtaa yɛ na ɛba fi metabolic disorders a ɛba efisɛ wɔbo sɔ ntɛm. Aho akyirikyiri ne Gumboro yadeɛ a ɛsɛe immune system, Newcastle yadeɛ, infectious bronchitis, ammonia poisons fi litter fi, nsuo ahia, berɛhyɛ den ne akoko akyikyide. Hwɛ mframa yie, de nsuo pa to mu bere nyinaa, hware so bere biara, hwɛ litter yie na mma nnomaa nbo sɔ akyi sen wɔ aduan a ɛboro so de.

English Question: For maximum egg production ensure 16 hours of light daily using artificial lighting, maintain temperature between 18 and 24 degrees Celsius, provide layer mash with 16 to 17 percent protein and added calcium for strong shells, ensure clean water always, control parasites and disease through regular vaccination and deworming, collect eggs three times daily, keep stress low by avoiding sudden disturbances, and cull poor layers that consistently produce below average.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ tamma gu akoko sɛ wɔagu pii?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wopɛ sɛ akoko gu tamma pii a, hwɛ sɛ kanea da wɔ mu dɔn 16 de artificial light, kora berɛ wɔ degrees 18 ne 24 Celsius ntam, de layer mash a protein 16 kɔ 17 percent ne calcium a ɛhia ma tamma ho den na ka ho, de nsuo pa to mu bere nyinaa, boa parasites ne yadeɛ ho de hware ne wia adwummaker bere biara, pam tamma mprɛnsa mmiɛnsa biara da, ma anigyidie sua de gye wo ho fi nka kɔkɔɔkɔ, na kum layers a wɔgu nketewa bere nyinaa.

English Question: A brooder provides warmth for day-old chicks in the first 2 to 3 weeks. Use a heat lamp or electric bulb hung 45 cm above the floor in a circular guard made from cardboard or wire. Maintain temperature at 35 degrees Celsius in week one reducing by 3 degrees each week. Spread wood shavings as litter 5 to 7 cm deep. Provide water in chick-sized drinkers and starter feed in shallow trays. Watch chick behaviour to adjust temperature correctly.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ brooder ketewa ma day-old chicks?
Twi Answer: Brooder de berɛhyɛ ma day-old chicks wɔ nnansas mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa a ɛdi kan mu. De heat lamp anaa electric bulb a wɔde a so sɛntimita 45 fi asase so wɔ circular guard a wɔde cardboard anaa waya yɛ mu. Kora berɛ wɔ degrees 35 Celsius nnansa baako mu a ɛkɔ sua degrees mmiɛnsa bere biara. Terɛ wood shavings yɛ litter sɛntimita 5 kɔ 7 tia. De nsuo wɔ chick-sized drinkers na starter feed wɔ trays tete. Hwɛ chicks ahyɛso sɛ wobɛtua berɛ no ho yie.

English Question: The best housing for layers in Ghana's climate is the open-sided or naturally ventilated house. Use wire mesh or wooden slats on the sides for maximum airflow. Orient the house east to west so the long side faces north and south to reduce direct sunlight. Provide a sloped roof with good overhang. Install battery cages at 3 tiers for commercial production or deep litter floor for smaller flocks. Ensure 0.2 square metres per bird for floor housing and 450 square cm per bird for cages.
Twi Question: Housing nhyiamu bɛn na ɛhia pa ara ma layers wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Housing a ɛhia pa ara ma layers wɔ Ghana berɛ a ɛwɔ ne open-sided anaa naturally ventilated fie. De wire mesh anaa wooden slats to ho mframa nsa sɛ mframa fa mu yie. De fie no sie east kɔ west sɛ ho tenten so hyɛ north ne south anim sɛ owia ankasa annhyɛ mu. De roof a ɛtɔ yie ne overhang pa si. Si battery cages a tiers mmiɛnsa wɔ mu ma adwuma kɛse anaa deep litter floor ma flocks nketewa. Hwɛ sɛ square metres 0.2 wɔ nnomaa baako ho ma floor housing ne square cm 450 biara nnomaa ho ma cages.

English Question: Goats have a gestation period of 145 to 155 days about 5 months. Does can kid twice a year. They commonly have twins but singles and triplets also occur. The West African Dwarf goat commonly has twins and occasionally triplets. Provide extra feed to pregnant does in the last 6 weeks of pregnancy. Separate does close to kidding from the main herd. Assist if a doe is in labour for more than 30 minutes without progress.
Twi Question: Bere ahe na birekyie wo mma na mma ahe na ɛwo mmere baako?
Twi Answer: Birekyie mmirikyi si mu wɔ adays 145 kɔ 155 bɛyɛ sɛ mfee 5. Mmirikyi bɛtumi awo mfe mmienu mu. Wɔtaa wo mma mmienu nanso baako ne mmiɛnsa nso ba. West African Dwarf birekyie taa wo mmienu na bere biara mmiɛnsa. De aduan a ɛboro to ma mmirikyi a ɛwɔ aninso wɔ nnansas nsia a etwa to mu. Di mmirikyi a ɛbɛwo no fi herd kɛse ho. Boa sɛ mmirikyi wɔ abɔ so akyiri simma 30 a ɛnni so.

English Question: Goats need salt, calcium, phosphorus, selenium, copper and zinc for healthy growth and reproduction. The simplest way to provide minerals is to hang a mineral salt lick block in the pen which goats can lick freely. You can also add loose mineral mix to their feed. Selenium and copper deficiencies are common in Ghana causing poor growth, infertility and weak kids. Get your soil tested to know what minerals are deficient in your area and supplement accordingly.
Twi Question: Mineral bɛn na birekyie hia na dɛn na mede ma wɔn?
Twi Answer: Birekyie hia salt, calcium, phosphorus, selenium, copper ne zinc ma wɔn ho pa ne woo mma. Ɛkwan mmerɛw pa sɛ de minerals to wɔn nkyɛn ne de mineral salt lick block si pen mu a birekyie bɛtumi alick bere biara. Wobetumi nso de loose mineral mix ka wɔn aduan ho. Selenium ne copper hia taa ba wɔ Ghana a ɛma nnoa hiana, mma antwa anya, na mma hunu. Gye wo asase hwɛ ma wohunu minerals bɛn a hia wɔ wo hɔ na de ka ho saa.

English Question: Improve local cattle productivity by crossbreeding with improved exotic bulls like Friesian, Brown Swiss or Sahiwal through artificial insemination services available from CSIR-Animal Research Institute. Improve nutrition through fodder production of improved grasses like Panicum maximum and Stylosanthes, supplement with concentrate feed for breeding cows and calves, deworm and vaccinate regularly, and provide mineral supplements. Better management alone can increase productivity by 30 to 50 percent.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ me local nnwan nnoa bo kɔ so?
Twi Answer: Boa local nnwan nnoa ho de crossbreeding ne improved exotic bulls te sɛ Friesian, Brown Swiss anaa Sahiwal wɔ artificial insemination services a CSIR-Animal Research Institute de. Boa aduan ho de fodder to mu a improved grasses te sɛ Panicum maximum ne Stylosanthes, de concentrate feed ka ho ma breeding cows ne calves, wia adwummaker ne hware bere biara, na de mineral supplements ka ho. Adwuma pa pɛ tumi ma nnoa kɔ so 30 kɔ 50 percent.

English Question: Common signs of illness in cattle include loss of appetite and reduced feed intake, unusual posture or difficulty standing, nasal or eye discharge, diarrhoea, bloating, weight loss, reduced milk production, laboured breathing, lameness, and isolation from the herd. Any cattle showing these signs should be separated from healthy animals immediately and examined by a veterinary officer. Early detection and treatment saves lives and prevents spread to other animals.
Twi Question: Nsono bɛn na ɛkyerɛ sɛ nnwan wayarɛ?
Twi Answer: Nsono a ɛkyerɛ sɛ nnwan wayarɛ ne: aduan nhia, gyinae mfa ho anaa ahohia de gyina, hwam fi afi anaa ani, ayamtuo, ahonfuo, nnoa hun, nsuo sua, brɛath a ɛyɛ den, nan ahia, na afi herd no ho. Nnwan biara a ɛkyerɛ nsono yi nni yie sɛ woyiye fi mmoa pa ho ntɛm na vet offisa nhwɛ so. Hunu ntɛm na hu yɛ agyirae anom ne tete nsɛm mmoa foforɔ ho.

English Question: Good water quality is the foundation of successful fish farming. Test water weekly for pH which should be 6.5 to 8.5, dissolved oxygen above 5 mg per litre, ammonia below 0.02 mg per litre, and temperature between 25 and 30 degrees Celsius. Maintain quality by avoiding overfeeding which causes ammonia buildup, not overstocking, doing partial water changes of 20 to 30 percent weekly, growing aquatic plants to absorb excess nutrients, and aeration using paddle wheels or air pumps.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ nsuo pa wɔ me apataa pond mu?
Twi Answer: Nsuo pa yɛ fapem a apataa adwuma pa si so. Hwɛ nsuo biara nnansa de pH a ɛnni yie sɛ 6.5 kɔ 8.5, dissolved oxygen a ɛboro 5 mg biara litre, ammonia a ɛsian 0.02 mg biara litre ase, na berɛ wɔ degrees 25 ne 30 Celsius ntam. Kora mmerɛ de gye wo ho fi aduan a ɛboro so a ɛma ammonia adɔ so, to apataa a ɛboro so, sesa nsuo 20 kɔ 30 percent biara nnansas, to aquatic nnuaba sɛ wɔgye nutrients a ɛboro so, na de paddle wheels anaa air pumps ma nsuo nya oxygen.

English Question: The best harvesting method depends on whether you are doing partial or complete harvest. For partial harvest use a seine net to selectively remove larger fish leaving smaller ones to grow. For complete harvest drain the pond partially then use nets to remove all fish. Harvest early morning when water is cool. Have containers ready with clean water or ice to keep fish alive or fresh. Weigh and record your harvest for business records. Never use chemicals or electricity to harvest as these are illegal and harmful.
Twi Question: Ɛkwan bɛn na ɛhia pa ara sɛ meyiyɛ apataa fi pond mu?
Twi Answer: Ɛkwan a ɛhia pa ara sɛ wuyiyɛ no kyɛ sɛ partial anaa complete harvest na woyɛ. Ma partial harvest de seine net yi apataa kɛse a wɔbɛ na ma nketewa tena so bo sɔ. Ma complete harvest sua nsuo ketewa fi pond mu afei de nets yi apataa nyinaa. Yi anɔpa bere a nsuo dɛ. Ma containers a nsuo foforɔ anaa ice wɔ mu sɛ apataa aguina anaa tena foforɔ. Bu na kora wo harvest ho sɛ adwuma nsɛm. Mma wo mpo de chemicals anaa electricity yiyɛ efisɛ ɛnyɛ nea mmara gyina so na ɛyɛ bɔne.

English Question: To control tilapia breeding which causes overpopulation and stunted growth, use monosex culture by stocking only male tilapia. Males are identified by having one genital opening while females have two. Obtain male-only fingerlings from certified hatcheries that produce hormonally sex-reversed males. Alternatively introduce a predator species like Nile perch in small numbers to control fry, or use hapas to separate brood stock and collect fry for removal.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ tilapia apataa kyerɛ wɔn phula sɛ wobɔ wɔn bɔhyɛ so?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wopɛ sɛ wobɔ tilapia bɔhyɛ so a ɛma nnipa pii ne nnoa hiana no so, de monosex culture to mu de mmarima tilapia pɛ si. Wɔahu mmarima no sɛ wɔwɔ genital ho baako na mmirikyi wɔ mmienu. Gye male-only fingerlings fi certified hatcheries a wɔyɛ hormonally sex-reversed males. Anaa de predator nhyiamu te sɛ Nile perch ketewa to mu sɛ wɔhwɛ fry so, anaa de hapas sɛ wɔkyerɛ brood stock ne pam fry ma wɔyi wɔn.

English Question: Match your crop to your soil type for best results. Sandy soils drain quickly and suit groundnut, cowpea, sweet potato and watermelon. Clay soils retain water and suit rice, taro cocoyam and some vegetables. Loam soils are the most versatile and suit almost all crops including maize, cassava, tomatoes and most vegetables. Get a simple soil test done at your nearest MOFA office or agricultural laboratory to know your soil pH and nutrient levels before choosing your crop.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mepick nnuaba pa ma me asase nhyiamu?
Twi Answer: De wo nnuaba hyɛ wo asase nhyiamu mu ma nnoa pa. Sandy asase sua nsuo ntɛm na ɛbɛn groundnut, bɔde, sweet potato ne watermelon. Clay asase kora nsuo na ɛbɛn ɔmo, taro cocoyam ne nnuaba bi. Loam asase ne asase a ɛbɛn nnuaba bebree a aburoɔ, bankye, tomatoes ne nnuaba bebree ka ho. Gye wo asase hwɛ fi wo MOFA ofisi a ɛbɛn anaa agricultural laboratory ma wohunu wo asase pH ne ferefere levels ansa na wopick wo nnuaba.

English Question: Government support for young farmers in Ghana includes the Planting for Food and Jobs programme providing subsidized seeds and fertilizer, the Young Entrepreneurs and Agricultural Development (YEAD) programme, the Ghana Youth Employment and Entrepreneurial Development Agency (GYEEDA) agricultural modules, scholarships for agricultural education from MOFA, and the Agricultural Development Bank youth loans. Some districts also have youth in agriculture programmes. Visit your nearest MOFA district office or the Ministry of Food and Agriculture website for current programmes.
Twi Question: Aban mmoa bɛn na ɛwɔ ma mmerante okuafo wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Aban mmoa ma mmerante okuafo wɔ Ghana ne Planting for Food and Jobs programme a de subsidized aba ne ferefere to, Young Entrepreneurs ne Agricultural Development (YEAD) programme, Ghana Youth Employment ne Entrepreneurial Development Agency (GYEEDA) agricultural modules, scholarships ma okuafo education fi MOFA, na Agricultural Development Bank youth loans. Districts bi nso wɔ youth in agriculture programmes. Kɔ wo MOFA district ofisi a ɛbɛn anaa Ministry of Food and Agriculture website ma programmes a wɔwɔ saa ara.

English Question: Protect your farm from flooding and waterlogging by planting on raised beds or ridges especially for vegetables and root crops, digging drainage channels around the field perimeter to direct excess water away, avoiding farming in flood-prone low-lying areas during heavy rain seasons, choosing flood-tolerant varieties where possible, using cover crops and mulching to reduce runoff, and planting trees or grass strips along slopes to slow water flow and reduce erosion.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ me afuom annya nsuo tia?
Twi Answer: Gye wo afuom fi nsuo ho de to mu wɔ beds a ɛtele anaa ridges a ɛhia pii ma nnuaba ne nnɔho, boro drainage channels fa afuom no ho nyinaa sɛ ɛde nsuo a ɛboro so kɔ ho, gye wo ho fi okuafo adwuma wɔ hɔ a nsuo taa tia wɔ nsuo berɛ kɛse mu, yi flood-tolerant varieties wɔ hɔ a wɔwɔ, de cover crops ne mulching sua runoff, na to nnuaba anaa nhawan strips wɔ mmepɔ ho sɛ ɛhia nsuo kwan na sua erosion.

English Question: Several useful apps are available for Ghanaian farmers. The Farmerline Mergdata app provides market prices, weather forecasts and agricultural advice. The ESOKO platform sends SMS alerts about market prices. Plantix app helps diagnose crop diseases using photos. The One Acre Fund app assists with input planning. WhatsApp farmer groups share timely information. Soil Doctor provides soil testing and fertilizer recommendations. Use these apps to make better decisions on planting time, fertilizer application and market timing.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mede phone apps boa me okuafo adwuma?
Twi Answer: Apps a ɛboa wɔ Ghana okuafo wɔ hɔ ne: Farmerline Mergdata app a de dwa bo, berɛ nkra ne okuafo nkyerɛkyerɛ to. ESOKO platform de SMS alerts hyɛ dwa bo ho. Plantix app boa sɛ wohunu nnuaba yadeɛ de foto. One Acre Fund app boa inputs siesie. WhatsApp okuafo kuo kyɛ nsɛm a ɛyɛ papa ntɛm. Soil Doctor de asase hwɛ ne ferefere ho nkyerɛkyerɛ. De apps yi ma wo yɛ adwuma pa wɔ to aba bere, ferefere to ne dwa bere ho.

English Question: Contract farming is an agreement between a farmer and a buyer where the buyer agrees to purchase your produce at a pre-agreed price before you plant. In Ghana, companies like Masara N'Arziki for maize, Biase Plantations for sugarcane, various cocoa buying companies and export vegetable companies offer contract farming arrangements. Benefits include guaranteed market, access to inputs on credit, technical support and stable income. The main risk is being locked into a price that may be lower than the open market if prices rise.
Twi Question: Contract farming yɛ dɛn na ɛbɛtumi aboa me wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Contract farming ne nhyiam a ɛwɔ okuafo ne buyer ntam a buyer gyina so sɛ ɔbɛgye wo nnuaba bo a wɔako ka ansa na wode aba to mu. Wɔ Ghana, companies te sɛ Masara N'Arziki ma aburoɔ, Biase Plantations ma sugarcane, cocoa gye companies bebree ne export vegetable companies de contract farming nhyiam to. Mfaaso ne: dwa gyinae, access kɔ inputs wɔ credit so, technical mmoa ne owuo-teetee foforo so. Aho yɛ den kɛse ne sɛ wobɔ bo a ɛtumi yɛ sua sen open market sɛ bo kɔ so.

English Question: Manage irrigation efficiently by irrigating in the early morning or evening to reduce evaporation losses, using drip irrigation which delivers water directly to the root zone reducing waste by up to 50 percent compared to overhead sprinkler systems, mulching to retain soil moisture, monitoring soil moisture before irrigating rather than watering on a fixed schedule, levelling fields to ensure even water distribution, and fixing leaks in pipes and channels promptly.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mede quench pa yie sɛ me nsa nsuo?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ quench yie de quench wɔ anɔpa anaana anaa awia ansanaan sɛ ɛhia evaporation suas, de drip quench a ɛde nsuo kɔ nnɔho asase mu nsɛm sua nsa suas kɔ 50 percent tia overhead sprinkler systems tia, mulch sɛ asase nsuo agua, hwɛ asase nsuo ansa na woquench na gye wo ho fi quench schedule a ɛte so, siesie fields sɛ nsuo kɔ yie, na sa nsuo kwan mu holes ntɛm.

English Question: Farmer-based organisations (FBOs) in Ghana help members access group inputs at lower prices through bulk purchasing, negotiate better prices for produce, access credit collectively, share knowledge and technology, access extension services more easily, participate in government programmes, and market their produce jointly. To find an FBO in your area contact your District Department of Agriculture under MOFA. Joining a recognised FBO also helps you qualify for government subsidies and NGO support programmes.
Twi Question: Okuafo kuo adwuma yɛ dɛn wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Okuafo kuo (FBOs) wɔ Ghana boa wɔn members sɛ wɔgye group inputs wɔ bo sua mu de bulk buying, bɔ wɔn nnuaba bo yie, gye credit kaa bom, fa nyansa ne nkyerɛkyerɛ, gye extension services mmerɛw, ka aban programmes ho, na tɔ wɔn nnuaba kaa bom. Sɛ wohia FBO wɔ wo hɔ a, ka wo District Department of Agriculture wɔ MOFA ase ho. Ka FBO a wɔakyerɛw ho ho nso boa sɛ woatwa abo aban subsidies ne NGO mmoa programmes ho.

English Question: Main farming risks include weather risks from drought or flooding, pest and disease outbreaks, price volatility at harvest time, input price increases, land tenure insecurity, and lack of market access. Manage these risks by diversifying crops so one failure does not ruin you entirely, using drought-resistant varieties, taking out crop insurance where available, joining farmer groups for collective bargaining, storing produce to sell when prices improve, securing formal land documents, and building relationships with multiple buyers.
Twi Question: Aho yɛ den bɛn na ɛwɔ okuafo adwuma mu na dɛn na menyɛ wɔn ho?
Twi Answer: Aho yɛ den kɛse a ɛwɔ okuafo adwuma mu ne: berɛ ho aho yɛ den fi bone anaa nsuo, adwummaker ne yadeɛ ba ntɛm, dwa bo sesa bere a wuyiyɛ, inputs bo kɔ so, asase ho gyinae ankyɛ, na dwa kɔ ho hia. Boa ho de nnuaba ahorow to sɛ baako a atua ho nhia wo a ennye wo ho nyinaa, de drought-resistant varieties to mu, gye crop insurance wɔ hɔ a ɛwɔ, ka okuafo kuo ho ma wobɔ bo kaa bom, guina nnuaba sɛ wotɔ bere a bo yɛ yie, hwɛ sɛ asase ho krataa pa wɔ wo nkyɛn, na kora wo adwene ho buyers kuo mmerantee ho.

English Question: Drip irrigation is the best method for tomatoes in Ghana. It delivers water directly to the root zone reducing disease incidence from leaf wetness, improving water use efficiency, allowing fertigation where fertilizer is applied through the drip system, and reducing weed growth. Furrow irrigation is also acceptable for flat land. Avoid overhead sprinkler irrigation for tomatoes as wet foliage encourages fungal diseases like late blight. Irrigate in the morning to allow foliage to dry before evening.
Twi Question: Quench nhyiamu bɛn na ɛhia pa ara ma tomatoes wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Drip quench ne nhyiamu pa ara ma tomatoes wɔ Ghana. Ɛde nsuo kɔ nnɔho asase mu nsɛm a ɛhia yadeɛ a ɛba efisɛ nhaban nsuo, ɛboa nsuo de pa, ɛma fertigation a wɔde ferefere fa wɔ drip system mu to, na ɛhia nhaban foforo. Furrow quench nso yɛ yie ma asase a ɛtee. Gye wo ho fi overhead sprinkler quench ma tomatoes efisɛ nhaban nsuo boa fungal yadeɛ te sɛ late blight. Quench anɔpa sɛ nhaban tew ansa na anwumere aba.

English Question: Staking tomatoes keeps the plant upright reducing soil contact and disease. Use bamboo stakes or wooden sticks about 1.5 metres tall. Insert the stake 15 cm into the soil beside the plant without damaging roots. Tie the plant loosely to the stake using soft twine in a figure-8 pattern at every 20 to 30 cm of growth. Begin staking when plants are 20 to 30 cm tall. Indeterminate varieties need continuous staking as they grow while determinate varieties need staking only once.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ tomatoes stake pa?
Twi Answer: Tomatoes stake ma nnuaba gyina straight na ɛhia asase ne yadeɛ nka ho. De bamboo stakes anaa dua bio a ɛtelɛ sɛ metres 1.5. De stake si sɛntimita 15 asase mu bɛn nnuaba no ho a nnɔho nsɔre. Kyekyere nnuaba no de twine mmerɛw wɔ stake no ho wɔ figure-8 nhyiamu wɔ bere biara a nnuaba rekɔ sɛntimita 20 kɔ 30 so. Fi ase de stake bere a nnuaba bɛyɛ sɛntimita 20 kɔ 30 tenten. Indeterminate varieties hia stake bere nyinaa a wɔreba mu na determinate varieties hia stake mprɛn baako pɛ.

English Question: Dry fresh pepper by washing and removing stems then spreading on clean raised platforms in full sun for 7 to 10 days turning daily. The pepper is dry when it shrivels and rattles when shaken. Alternatively use a mechanical dryer at 60 to 65 degrees Celsius for 8 to 12 hours. Store dried pepper in sealed airtight containers away from moisture and sunlight. Dried pepper lasts 12 to 18 months. You can also grind dried pepper into powder or process into pepper sauce for added value.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ pepper tew na kata so sɛ ɛtena mu akyi?
Twi Answer: Ma fofor pepper tew de hohoro na yi abɔ afei terɛ wɔ platforms a ɛtele na ɛpaa owia so adays 7 kɔ 10 a wogye mu adan bere biara. Pepper tew bere a ɛkɔ yɛ ketewa na ɛkeka bere a woyɛ no. Anaa de mechanical dryer wɔ degrees 60 kɔ 65 Celsius aanos 8 kɔ 12 mu. Guina pepper a ɛatew wɔ containers a wɔato mu paa fi nsuo ne owia ho. Pepper a ɛatew tena agyapade 12 kɔ 18 mu. Wobetumi nso de pepper a ɛatew fɛn yɛ powder anaa yɛ pepper sauce ma ɛbo kɔ so.

English Question: Deworm sheep every 3 months using Albendazole or Ivermectin. Rotate between dewormers to prevent resistance. Check for signs of heavy worm burden including pale gums and eyelids which indicate anaemia, bottle jaw from protein loss, poor body condition and weight loss, diarrhoea and rough coat. The FAMACHA method uses eyelid colour scoring to decide which animals need deworming rather than deworming the whole flock unnecessarily. Consult your veterinary officer for a proper deworming schedule.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ internal parasites wɔ oguan ho?
Twi Answer: Wia oguan adwummaker mprɛnsa mmiɛnsa de Albendazole anaa Ivermectin. Sesa dewormers ntam sɛ wɔantumi aho nsɔhwɛ so. Hwɛ nsono a ɛkyerɛ adwummaker pii a ɛwɔ mu te sɛ anom ne ani ho fitaa a ɛkyerɛ mogya hia, bottle jaw fi protein ahunu, ho ba nni yie ne nnoa hun, ayamtuo ne afohyɛ a ɛnte yie. FAMACHA nhyiamu de ani ho bo no sɛ hwɛ mmoa bɛn hia deworming na amma flock nyinaa enni deworm kwa. Bisa wo vet offisa ma deworming schedule pa.

English Question: Build a simple sheep pen using locally available materials. Make the floor raised 50 to 60 cm off the ground using wooden planks or bamboo to keep the sheep dry and reduce parasite buildup. Use wooden poles and wire mesh or bamboo for the walls. The pen should be well ventilated but protected from rain and predators. Allow 1 to 1.5 square metres per adult sheep. Include a feeding trough and water trough. Clean the pen and remove manure weekly to prevent disease buildup.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ oguan pen ketewa wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Tu oguan pen ketewa de nneɛma a ɛwɔ ho wɔ ɛhɔ. Ma asase no tele sɛntimita 50 kɔ 60 fi asase so de dua anaa bamboo krataa sɛ oguan tena dɛ na parasites nni mu pii. De dua abɔ ne wire mesh anaa bamboo yɛ ho. Pen no nini yie sɛ mframa fa mu nanso ɛhwɛ so fi nsuo ne adwummaker. Ma square metres baako kɔ 1.5 biara oguan panyin. Ka aduan trough ne nsuo trough ka ho. Hohoro pen no na yi aguare biara nnansas sɛ yadeɛ nni mu.

English Question: The yam beetle is one of the most destructive yam pests, tunnelling into tubers causing rot. Control by treating setts with insecticide before planting, harvesting at the right time without leaving tubers in the ground too long, storing yams properly, rotating crops to break the pest cycle, and applying carbofuran granules around the base of plants. Yam nematodes cause small lesions on tubers. Use certified clean planting material and avoid replanting in infested soil.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ yam beetles ne adwummaker foforɔ ho?
Twi Answer: Yam beetle ne adwummaker a ɛsɛe bayerɛ paa baako, ɛkɔtɔ bua no mu a ɛma ɛsɛe. Boa ho de de insecticide hware setts ansa na wode to mu, yi bere a ɛyɛ papa a womfa bayerɛ na agyina asase mu akyiri, guina bayerɛ yie, sesa adekuo adwuma sɛ ɛbu adwummaker bere, na de carbofuran granules to nnuaba no ase ho. Yam nematodes ma nsono ketewa ba bua so. De certified clean planting material na nni de to mu wɔ asase a adwummaker wɔ mu.

English Question: Curing yams after harvest helps heal minor skin injuries and extends storage life. Place harvested yams in a warm humid location at 29 to 35 degrees Celsius with 90 to 95 percent relative humidity for 4 to 8 days. Traditional yam barns provide natural curing conditions. After curing store yams in a cool well-ventilated barn off the ground. Check stored yams monthly removing any showing rot immediately. Well-stored yams last 3 to 6 months.
Twi Question: Ɛkwan pa bɛn na mede bayerɛ twew na guina yi akyi?
Twi Answer: Bayerɛ twew yi akyi boa sɛ nsono ketewa wɔ ho so sa na aguina bere tenten. De bayerɛ a woyii sie wɔ baabi a ɛhyehyɛ kakra ne nsuo wɔ mu wɔ degrees 29 kɔ 35 Celsius ne relative humidity 90 kɔ 95 percent mu adays nnan kɔ nwɔtwe. Traditional bayerɛ barns de natural curing conditions to. Twew akyi guina bayerɛ wɔ barn a ɛdɛ ne mframa fa mu na ɛfiri asase so. Hwɛ bayerɛ a woguina bere biara na yi a ɛreyɛ sɛe wɔn ntɛm. Bayerɛ a woguina yie tena agyapade mmiɛnsa kɔ nsia mu.

English Question: After harvesting onions remove tops and roots and spread bulbs on clean raised platforms in the shade with good air circulation for 2 to 3 weeks. This curing process dries the outer skin creating a protective wrapper. Store cured onions in mesh bags or slatted crates in a cool dry well-ventilated place. Never store in sealed plastic bags as moisture builds up causing rot. Well-stored onions can last 3 to 6 months. Inspect monthly and remove any rotting bulbs immediately.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ me twew na guina abɔnkɔ yi akyi?
Twi Answer: Abɔnkɔ yi akyi yi atifi ne nnɔho na terɛ bulbs wɔ platforms a ɛtele wɔ hare ha a mframa fa mu yie nnansa mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa. Twew no ma ho ban fotoo tew a ɛyɛ twamfo. Guina abɔnkɔ a ɛatew wɔ mesh bags anaa slatted crates wɔ baabi a ɛdɛ, dɛ ne mframa fa mu yie. Mma wo mpo guina wɔ sealed plastic bags efisɛ nsuo adɔ so a ɛma ɛsɛe. Abɔnkɔ a woguina yie tena agyapade mmiɛnsa kɔ nsia. Hwɛ bere biara na yi bulbs a ɛreyɛ sɛe wɔn ntɛm.

English Question: Add value to cocoyam by processing into cocoyam flour which has good market demand for use in porridge, soup thickening and pastries. You can also process into cocoyam chips which are dried slices that store well. Boiled and pounded cocoyam sold pre-packaged is popular in urban markets. Cocoyam leaves are also edible and can be sold separately as a vegetable. Targeting supermarkets, restaurants and food processors with processed cocoyam products gives better prices than selling fresh at local markets.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ kɔkɔnte bo kɔ so ma sika pa?
Twi Answer: Kɔkɔnte bo kɔ so de yɛ kɔkɔnte flour a dwa pa wɔ mu ma porridge, soup thickening ne pastries ho. Wobetumi nso de yɛ kɔkɔnte chips a yɛ slices a ɛatew a ɛguina yie. Kɔkɔnte a wodom ne dome no a wɔde kura paapa nso pɛ wɔ dwa kɛse mu. Kɔkɔnte nhaban nso edi na wubetumi atɔ wɔn atɔ nnuaba. De kɔkɔnte nneɛma a wɔayɛ so kɔ supermarkets, adidibea ne food processors dwa bo yɛ sen tɔ foforɔ wɔ local dwa mu.

English Question: Common carrot problems include forking where the root splits into multiple branches caused by rocky soil or fresh manure, carrot fly larvae tunnelling into roots, alternaria leaf blight causing dark lesions, cavity spot causing elliptical depressions, and poor germination from planting old seed. Solve forking by preparing deep loose soil and using only well-composted manure. Control carrot fly by covering beds with insect-proof netting. Use fresh certified seed for good germination.
Twi Question: Aho yɛ den bɛn na ɛtaa ba carrot nnoa mu?
Twi Answer: Aho yɛ den a ɛtaa ba carrot ho ne: forking a ɛkyerɛ sɛ nnɔho no pae yɛ mmerantee pii a ɛba efisɛ asase a abo wɔ mu anaa aguare foforɔ, carrot fly larvae a ɛkɔtɔ nnɔho mu, alternaria leaf blight a ɛma nsono tuntum ba, cavity spot a ɛma holes yɛ elliptical, na aba a ɛntua fɔw yie efisɛ aba dada. Sa forking ho de siesie asase tia na ɛte na de aguare a ɛawie pɛpɛɛpɛ pɛ de. Boa carrot fly ho de kata beds de insect-proof netting. De certified aba foforɔ ma tua fɔw yie.

English Question: The main pest of garden eggs is the epilachna beetle which eats large holes in leaves reducing the plant's ability to produce fruit. Control by hand-picking beetles and larvae in the early morning, using neem leaf extract spray, applying spinosad insecticide in severe cases, and destroying heavily infested plants. Aphids and whiteflies also attack garden eggs and can be controlled with insecticidal soap spray. Fruit borers may require systemic insecticides.
Twi Question: Adwummaker bɛn na ɛtaa tu mako ntorɔ na dɛn na menyɛ wɔn ho?
Twi Answer: Adwummaker kɛse a ɛtuu mako ntorɔ ne epilachna beetle a ɛdi nhaban holes kɛse a ɛhia nnuaba tumi nnuaba boa mu. Boa ho de nsa yi beetles ne larvae anɔpa, de neem nhaban extract hware, de spinosad insecticide to ho bere a ɛyɛ yiye, na sɛe nnuaba a adwummaker tuu mako pii. Aphids ne whiteflies nso taa tu ntorɔ mako na wobetumi abo wɔn ho de insecticidal soap hware. Fruit borers bɛtumi ahia systemic insecticides.

English Question: Coconut can be processed into coconut oil by grating mature coconut extracting the milk and boiling until oil separates, coconut cream and milk for cooking, desiccated coconut from dried grated flesh, coconut shell charcoal and crafts, coconut fibre from the husk for mats and ropes, and coconut water which is a popular beverage. In coastal Ghana there is good market for fresh coconuts coconut oil and coconut water. Value addition significantly increases income from coconut farming.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ kuuku yɛ nneɛma ahorow ma sika?
Twi Answer: Wobetumi de kuuku yɛ: kuuku ɔman de grate kuuku a ɛatwa so yi nsuo afei hyehye kosi sɛ ɔman pae fi, kuuku cream ne nsuo ma aduan, desiccated kuuku fi dried grated flesh, kuuku ano faako charcoal ne adwuma, kuuku saa fi husk ma dua mpaboa ne tow, na kuuku nsuo a ɛyɛ nsuo a wɔpɛ. Wɔ Ghana mpoano hɔ, dwa pa wɔ kuuku foforɔ, kuuku ɔman ne kuuku nsuo ho. Value addition ma sika a ɛfiri kuuku adwuma kɔ so pii.

English Question: Manage suckers by allowing only one follower sucker per stool at a time. Remove excess suckers using a sharp spade cutting them off at soil level. Choose the best positioned sword sucker as the follower. After harvest of the main bunch cut the harvested stem down to 1 metre and let it die naturally. A well-managed stool can produce continuously for 5 to 7 years. Fertilize each stool with 100 to 200 grams of NPK twice a year for sustained production.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ suckers sɛ me boɔde afuom ayɛ adwuma yie?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ suckers de ma sucker baako pɛ tena wɔ stool biara bere koro. Yi suckers a ɛboro so de spade akyer wɔ asase so. Yi sword sucker a ɛtete yie ma ɛyɛ follower. Ntama kɛse yi akyi twa abɔ a woyii no kɔsi metre baako na ma no wu ankasa. Stool a wohwɛ so yie tumi de nnuaba ba daadaa mfe 5 kɔ 7. De NPK gram 100 kɔ 200 to stool biara ho mprɛn mmienu biara afe ma nnoa tena so.

English Question: Small plantain bunches are caused by poor soil fertility, water stress during bunch formation, heavy pest or disease pressure especially black sigatoka, overcrowded suckers competing for nutrients, using inferior planting material, and not removing dead leaves promptly. Improve bunch size by applying NPK and potassium fertilizer regularly, irrigating during dry spells, controlling sigatoka with fungicide, desuckering to one sucker per stool, and using quality sword suckers for planting.
Twi Question: Dɛn ma boɔde ntama yɛ ketewa na dɛn na menyɛ sɛ ɛntɔ me?
Twi Answer: Boɔde ntama nketewa ba efisɛ asase aduan hia, nsuo ahia bere a ntama reyɛ, adwummaker ne yadeɛ a ɛhia pii a black sigatoka ka ho, suckers pii a wɔdi ferefere ho brε, planting material mfa ho, na amma wo nhaban a ɛawu asiesie ntɛm. Boa ntama bo kɔ so de de NPK ne potassium ferefere to ho bere biara, quench bone berɛ mu, boa sigatoka ho de fungicide hware, desuckering kɔsi sucker baako biara stool, na de sword suckers pa to mu.

English Question: Scout your maize field weekly by walking in a W or X pattern across the field. Examine at least 20 plants at each of 5 locations. Look under leaves for eggs and larvae, in the whorl for fall armyworm frass, on ears for silk damage, and on stems for borer entry holes. Record the percentage of plants affected. If more than 5 to 10 percent of plants are infested take action. Scout in the early morning when pests are most active. Keep a scouting notebook to track pest trends.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mehwɛ me aburoɔ afuom mu hwɛ adwummaker?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ wo aburoɔ afuom mu nnansas de kɔ wɔ W anaa X pattern wɔ afuom mu. Hwɛ nnuaba 20 pɛ wɔ baabi 5 mu. Hwɛ nhaban ase ma tammɛn ne larvae, wɔ whorl mu ma fall armyworm frass, wɔ ears so ma silk nsɔre, na wɔ abɔ so ma borer holes. Kora nnuaba a yadeɛ aba ho percent. Sɛ nnuaba 5 kɔ 10 percent a adwummaker tuu wɔn mako a, yɛ biribi. Hwɛ anɔpa bere a adwummaker yɛ adwuma pii. Kora scouting notebook ma wo hunu adwummaker trend.

English Question: Integrated pest management for maize combines multiple control methods to reduce pest damage while minimizing chemical use. It includes planting resistant varieties, using certified seeds, planting at the recommended time to escape peak pest pressure, regular scouting to detect pests early, using biological controls like natural enemies, applying chemical pesticides only when pest levels exceed economic thresholds, and crop rotation to break pest cycles. This approach reduces costs and environmental impact compared to calendar spraying.
Twi Question: Integrated pest management yɛ dɛn ma aburoɔ?
Twi Answer: Integrated pest management ma aburoɔ de nhyiamu ahorow ka bom sɛ ɛhia adwummaker nsɔre na ɛhia chemicals sua. Ɛka ho to resistant varieties mu, de certified seeds, to mu bere a wɔakyerɛw so sɛ adwummaker atia ktwa, hwɛ so bere biara ma wohunu adwummaker ntɛm, de biological controls te sɛ natural enemies, de chemical pesticides pɛ bere a adwummaker bore so kɛse sen economic thresholds, na sesa adekuo adwuma sɛ ɛbu adwummaker bere. Nhyiamu yi hia sika sua na ɛboa asase mu sen calendar spraying.

English Question: Make compost by layering crop residues dry matter like maize stalks alternating with green matter like grass clippings and kitchen waste. Add a thin layer of soil or finished compost between layers to introduce decomposing organisms. Keep the pile moist but not waterlogged and turn it every 2 weeks. The compost is ready in 8 to 12 weeks when it is dark brown crumbly and earthy smelling. Apply 2 to 3 tonnes of compost per acre before planting to significantly improve soil fertility.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ compost ma me aburoɔ afuom?
Twi Answer: Yɛ compost de layers a nnuaba a ato fɛw aba ntama a wɔatew te sɛ aburoɔ abɔ ka ho ne nnuaba foforɔ te sɛ nhawan ne efie ho nneɛma. De asase ketewa anaa compost a ɛawie to ntam biara mu sɛ ɛde organisms a ɛhia kɔ. Ma pile no nsuo ho kakra nanso nsuo nni mu agyina na gyinaso mprɛn mmienu biara nnansas. Compost no atwa so nnansas nwɔtwe kɔ duonum mmienu mu bere a ɛyɛ dark brown, ɛpepee yie na ɛwɔ nhwirɛ pa. De compost tonnes mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa to eka baako so ansa na wode aba to mu sɛ ɛboa asase aduan pii.

English Question: Cassava peels can be dried and used as animal feed for goats, sheep and pigs, providing a valuable energy source. Fresh peels fermented for 3 to 4 days make good pig and poultry feed. Cassava peel compost improves soil fertility. The starchy water from gari processing can be fermented and used as a fermented cassava drink called pito or as a substrate for mushroom growing. Using cassava by-products reduces waste and adds extra income streams.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ bankye ho ne nsononko ho adwuma yie?
Twi Answer: Bankye ho bɛtumi atew na de ma mmoa te sɛ birekyie, oguan ne prako aduan, de energy toɔ to. Bankye ho foforɔ a wɔde ferment adays mmiɛnsa kɔ nnan yɛ prako ne akoko aduan pa. Bankye ho compost boa asase aduan. Nsuo a starch wɔ mu fi gari yɛ ho bɛtumi aferment na de yɛ nsuo aduan a wɔfre no pito anaa de yɛ substrate ma mushroom noa. De bankye by-products de hyɛ nsono mu hia na ɛhia sika ahoma foforɔ.

English Question: Cassava is rich in carbohydrates providing a good energy source. It contains vitamin C, folate, magnesium and potassium. The leaves are highly nutritious containing protein, iron, calcium and vitamins A and C. Cassava leaves are eaten as a vegetable throughout West Africa. However cassava contains cyanogenic compounds which produce hydrogen cyanide. Processing methods like fermentation soaking grating and cooking remove these toxins making cassava safe to eat.
Twi Question: Ahoɔden bɛn na ɛwɔ bankye mu?
Twi Answer: Bankye wɔ carbohydrates pii mu a ɛde energy toɔ pa. Ɛwɔ vitamin C, folate, magnesium ne potassium. Nhaban no wɔ protein, iron, calcium ne vitamins A ne C pii mu. Wɔ di bankye nhaban sɛ nnuaba wɔ West Africa nyinaa mu. Nanso bankye wɔ cyanogenic compounds a ɛma hydrogen cyanide. Processing nhyiamu te sɛ fermentation, da mu, grate ne hyehye yi poisons yi wɔ mu a ɛma ɛtumi adi.

English Question: Select a site with clay soil that holds water well, near a reliable water source. Mark out the pond area typically 20 by 25 metres. Dig to a depth of 1.5 to 2 metres with sloping sides for stability. Build an inlet pipe to bring water in and an outlet pipe at the deepest point to drain. Pack the dikes firmly to prevent leaks. Fill with water and leave for 2 weeks to cure and establish algae before stocking. The total cost including excavation for a 500 square metre pond is typically GHS 3,000 to 6,000.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ earthen apataa pond a bo sua?
Twi Answer: Yi asase a ɛwɔ clay asase a ɛkora nsuo yie, bɛn nsuo kwan pa. Kyerɛ pond area a ɛtaa yɛ metres 20 ne 25. Boro kɔsi tia metres 1.5 kɔ 2 a ho mfimfini slopes wɔ gyinae ho. Tu inlet pipe sɛ nsuo aba mu na outlet pipe wɔ tia no so sɛ nsuo fa mu. Hyehye dikes no yie sɛ nsuo anyi. Ma nsuo kɔ mu na gyina nnansas mmienu sɛ ɛtena na algae ntua fɔw ansa na wode apataa to. Bo nyinaa a excavation ka ho ma pond a square metres 500 wɔ mu taa yɛ GHS 3,000 kɔ 6,000.

English Question: A recirculating aquaculture system or RAS is an indoor fish farming system where water is continuously filtered and recycled using biofilters mechanical filters and UV sterilizers. It allows high density fish farming in a small space with full control over water quality and temperature. RAS is suitable for Ghana for high-value fish species like catfish and tilapia especially in urban areas where land is limited. The main challenge is the high initial setup cost of GHS 50,000 to 200,000 and regular electricity requirement.
Twi Question: Recirculating aquaculture system yɛ dɛn na ɛhia wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Recirculating aquaculture system anaa RAS ne apataa adwuma fie mu a nsuo de filter na fa bio de biofilters, mechanical filters ne UV sterilizers. Ɛma apataa pii to mu kotoku ketewa mu a wɔhwɛ nsuo pa ne berɛ so yie. RAS hia wɔ Ghana ma apataa nhyiamu a bo yɛ so te sɛ catfish ne tilapia a ɛhia pii wɔ dɔn kɛse mu wɔ hɔ a asase hia. Aho yɛ den kɛse ne setup bo a ɛboro so a ɛyɛ GHS 50,000 kɔ 200,000 na electricity a ɛhia bere biara.

English Question: Market your fish effectively by selling live fish to restaurants and hotels which pay premium prices for freshness, supplying smoked or dried fish to markets for longer shelf life, building relationships with female fish traders at Kumasi Central Market and Accra markets who buy in bulk, using social media like Facebook to reach direct buyers, selling during festive seasons like Christmas and Eid when demand and prices are highest, and joining fish farmer cooperatives that negotiate group prices.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ metɔ me apataa wɔ bo pa wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Tɔ wo apataa pa de tɔ apataa a wɔte so kɔ adidibea ne hotels a wɔtua sika pa ma foforɔ ho, de apataa a wɔahye anaa atew to kɔ dwa ma ɛtena mu akyi, kyɛ wo adwene ho okuafo bea a wɔtɔ apataa wɔ Kumasi Central Market ne Accra dwa mu a wɔgye pii, de social media te sɛ Facebook kɔ buyers straight ho, tɔ bere a afenhyia ba te sɛ Bosome Dɔ ne Eid bere a nhia ne bo yɛ so sen, na ka apataa okuafo kuo ho a wɔbɔ bo kaa bom.

English Question: For commercial fish farming the minimum recommended pond size is 500 square metres. This size allows you to stock approximately 1,500 to 2,500 tilapia or 5,000 to 10,000 catfish fingerlings. Smaller ponds are possible but make it harder to achieve economies of scale and recover your investment. Ideally a commercial fish farm should have at least 2 to 3 ponds to allow rotation for pond maintenance and continuous production and staggered harvesting for regular income.
Twi Question: Pond ketewa bɛn na ɛhia ma adwuma kɛse apataa?
Twi Answer: Ma adwuma kɛse apataa, pond ketewa a wɔakyerɛw so ne square metres 500. Kɛse yi ma wubetumi ade tilapia bɛyɛ 1,500 kɔ 2,500 anaa catfish fingerlings 5,000 kɔ 10,000 to mu. Ponds nketewa yɛ bebiara nanso ɛyɛ den sɛ wonya mfaso yie na wonya wo sika bio. Bere biara, adwuma kɛse apataa afuom nini yie sɛ ponds mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa wɔ hɔ sɛ ɛboa pond hwɛ ne nnoaboa toa so pɛ ne yi aba bere biara ma owuo-teetee bere biara.

English Question: The standard Newcastle disease vaccination schedule in Ghana is Lasota live vaccine eye or nose drop at day 7, Lasota booster at day 21, and then Lasota every 2 months thereafter. For layers continue every 2 months throughout the laying period. Use inactivated oil-emulsion Newcastle vaccine at 8 weeks for additional protection especially in high-risk areas. Store vaccines at 2 to 8 degrees Celsius and use within the expiry date. Never vaccinate sick birds.
Twi Question: Newcastle yadeɛ vaccination schedule bɛn na ɛhia wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Newcastle yadeɛ vaccination schedule pa wɔ Ghana ne Lasota live vaccine ani anaa afi drops wɔ da 7, Lasota booster wɔ da 21, na Lasota bere biara mprɛn mmienu mu saa akyi. Ma layers tena so mprɛn mmienu mu so wɔ tamma gu bere nyinaa. De inactivated oil-emulsion Newcastle vaccine to ho wɔ nnansas nwɔtwe sɛ ɛboa hwɛ so a ɛhia pii wɔ hɔ a ɛyɛ den. Guina vaccines wɔ degrees 2 kɔ 8 Celsius na de fi mu ansa na bere a wɔakyerɛw so abu. Mma wo mpo hware nnomaa a wayarɛ so.

English Question: Manage poultry litter by starting with 5 to 7 cm of dry wood shavings rice husks or sawdust as bedding. Turn the litter every 2 to 3 days to prevent caking and ammonia buildup. Add fresh dry litter as needed. Keep the moisture content below 25 percent. Replace wet patches immediately. After each flock clean the house completely remove all litter fumigate with formaldehyde and rest the house for 2 to 4 weeks before the next flock. Good litter management prevents respiratory disease and foot problems.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ litter wɔ akoko fie mu?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ akoko litter de fi ase de wood shavings, rice husks anaa sawdust tia 5 kɔ 7 sɛntimita yɛ bedding. Gyinaso litter no mprɛn mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa biara nnansas sɛ ɛnkakra na ammonia nntea. De litter foforɔ a ɛtew ka ho sɛ ɛhia. Ma nsuo a ɛwɔ mu nkyɛ 25 percent. Yi baabi a ɛposo so ntɛm. Flock biara yi akyi hohoro fie no pɛpɛɛpɛ yi litter nyinaa fumigate de formaldehyde na ma fie no ho mprɛnsa mmienu kɔ nnan ansa na flock foforɔ aba. Litter hwɛ pa gye asufufuo yadeɛ ne nan ho aho yɛ den fi ho.

English Question: Reduce poultry feed costs by formulating your own feed using locally available ingredients like maize, soybean meal, fishmeal, rice bran and mineral premix. This can reduce feed cost by 20 to 30 percent compared to commercial feeds. Buy feed ingredients in bulk when prices are low. Use fermented feed to improve digestibility and reduce feed conversion ratio. Reduce waste by using appropriate feeders and filling them only two-thirds full. Grow fast-growing varieties and slaughter at the right age before feed efficiency declines.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ me aduan bo sua wɔ akoko adwuma mu?
Twi Answer: Sua akoko aduan bo de yɛ wo ankasa aduan de nneɛma a ɛwɔ ho te sɛ aburoɔ, soybean meal, fishmeal, rice bran ne mineral premix. Eyi bɛtumi asua aduan bo 20 kɔ 30 percent tia commercial feeds. Gye aduan nneɛma pii bere a bo sua. De fermented feed ma digestibility kɔ so na sua feed conversion ratio. Hia adefoforo de feeders pa na ma wɔn mu mprɛnsa mmienu pɛ. To fast-growing varieties mu na kum bere a ɛyɛ papa ansa na feed efficiency huna.

English Question: A healthy goat has bright clear eyes without discharge, a shiny coat without bare patches, firm well-formed droppings, good body condition not too thin or too fat, pink gums and eyelids indicating good blood levels, active and alert behaviour, no lameness or limping, good appetite, and clean hooves without overgrowth or rot. Avoid buying goats with dull sunken eyes, rough dull coat, pale gums, visible ribs or hip bones, nasal discharge, coughing or limping.
Twi Question: Dɛn na ɛkyerɛ birekyie pa bere a megye?
Twi Answer: Birekyie pa wɔ ani a ɛhann na nsononko nni, afohyɛ a ɛhann na baabi amma nnyina, adesoa a ɛwɔ gyinae, ho ba pa na ɛnyɛ hunu mpa anaa ahoɔden, anom ne ani ho kɔɔ a ɛkyerɛ mogya pa, nneyɛe pa ne adwene wɔ mu, nan ahia anaa nim, nhia aduan, na anan a ɛpaa yie a anyi dua pii anaa sɛe. Gye wo ho fi birekyie a ani sian ne ho nfiti, afohyɛ a ɛnte, anom fitaa, nnɔha anaa mu abɔ a wɔhunu, hwam fi afi, wu anaa nan ahia.
