English Question: Improve goat production through selective breeding by keeping only the best performing does and bucks for breeding. Choose bucks from does with high milk production and good kid growth rates. Introduce improved breeds like Boer goat for meat or Saanen for dairy by crossing with local does. Maintain good breeding records tracking which bucks served which does and offspring performance. Avoid inbreeding by rotating bucks or introducing new blood every 2 to 3 years.
Twi Question: Ɛkwan bɛn na ɛhia pa ara sɛ mede birekyie bɔhyɛ sɛ nnoa kɔ so?
Twi Answer: Boa birekyie nnoa ho de selective breeding de guina mmirikyi ne mmɔfraase pa pɛ sɛ bɔhyɛ. Yi mmɔfraase fi mmirikyi a wɔwɔ nsuo pii na mma a wɔbo sɔ yie. Ka improved breeds te sɛ Boer birekyie ma nam anaa Saanen ma nsuo ho de cross ne local mmirikyi. Kora bɔhyɛ ho nsɛm yie sɛ mmɔfraase bɛn na wɔde baa mmirikyi bɛn ho na mma nnoa ho nsɛm. Gye wo ho fi inbreeding de gye mmɔfraase anaa de mogya foforɔ kɔ mfe mmienu kɔ mmiɛnsa mu.

English Question: Deworm cattle every 3 to 4 months using broad-spectrum anthelmintics like Ivermectin which controls both internal and external parasites, Albendazole or Levamisole. Deworm at the start of the rainy season when parasite burden peaks and again at the start of the dry season. Always weigh or estimate the body weight of each animal to administer the correct dose. Underdosing causes resistance. Rotate between dewormers annually. Calves need more frequent deworming every 6 to 8 weeks.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ nnwan mu adwummaker na bere bɛn?
Twi Answer: Wia nnwan mu adwummaker mprɛnsa mmiɛnsa kɔ nnan de broad-spectrum anthelmintics te sɛ Ivermectin a ɛboa internal ne external parasites mmienu, Albendazole anaa Levamisole. Wia nsuo berɛ akyirikyiri bere a parasites taa pii ne bone berɛ akyirikyiri bio. Bu anaa hunu nnwan biara nnɔho sɛ wobɛma dose a ɛyɛ papa. Dose hiana ma resistance. Sesa dewormers afe biara. Calves hia deworming a ɛtaa sen nnansas nsia kɔ nwɔtwe.

English Question: Good fodder crops for cattle in Ghana include Napier grass which produces high biomass and can be harvested every 6 to 8 weeks, Guinea grass, Stylosanthes guianensis which is a nutritious legume that fixes nitrogen, Centrosema which is a climbing legume, Leucaena trees which provide protein-rich pods and leaves, and Mucuna which is an excellent dry season fodder. Establish a fodder plot of at least 0.5 hectares per cow. Cut and carry feed to cattle rather than letting them graze uncontrolled to improve feed efficiency.
Twi Question: Fodder nnuaba bɛn na mede ato mu sɛ mede ma me nnwan wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Fodder nnuaba pa ma nnwan wɔ Ghana ne Napier grass a ɛde biomass pii ba na wubetumi ayi bere biara nnansas nsia kɔ nwɔtwe, Guinea grass, Stylosanthes guianensis a ɛyɛ legume pa a ɛde nitrogen ka, Centrosema a ɛyɛ climbing legume, Leucaena nnuaba a ɛde pods ne nhaban a protein wɔ mu pii ba, na Mucuna a ɛyɛ bone berɛ fodder pa. Tu fodder plot a hectares 0.5 pɛ biara bɔ. Yi na de aduan kɔ nnwan nkyɛn na gye wo ho fi sɛ wɔnkɔ wɔ ho ho so sɛ ɛboa aduan de yie.

English Question: A simple farm budget lists all expected income and all expected costs for one season. Income includes expected yield multiplied by expected price. Costs include land preparation, seeds, fertilizer, pesticides, labour for planting weeding and harvesting, transport and packaging. Subtract total costs from total income to get expected profit. Always add a 10 to 15 percent buffer for unexpected costs. Review your actual results against the budget after each season to improve planning for the next season.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ afuom budget ketewa?
Twi Answer: Afuom budget ketewa kyerɛ owuo-teetee a wohwia ne costs nyinaa ma bere baako. Owuo-teetee ka ho nnoa a wohwia a wɔde dwa bo a wohwia bu. Costs ka ho asase siesie, aba, ferefere, pesticides, adwuma ma to mu, nhaban foforo yi ne yi, transport ne packaging. Gui costs nyinaa fi owuo-teetee nyinaa mu sɛ wohunu mfaso a wohwia. De 10 kɔ 15 percent buffer ka ho ma costs a onhwia. Hwɛ wo actual results tia budget akyi bere biara sɛ ɛboa wo siesie adwuma pa ma bere a ɛdi hɔ.

English Question: Agricultural insurance in Ghana includes the Ghana Agricultural Insurance Programme which covers crop losses from drought, flood and pests, the GIRSAL guarantee scheme which reduces risk for banks lending to farmers, and the National Agricultural Insurance Scheme. Some private insurance companies also offer agricultural products. MOFA collaborates with insurance companies to provide subsidised premiums for smallholder farmers. Contact your nearest MOFA office or Ghana Insurers Association for current products and premium rates.
Twi Question: Agricultural insurance schemes bɛn na ɛwɔ wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Agricultural insurance wɔ Ghana ne Ghana Agricultural Insurance Programme a ɛboa nnuaba ahunu fi bone, nsuo ne adwummaker, GIRSAL guarantee scheme a ɛhia banks a wɔde mfɛdomhyɛw ma okuafo yɛ den, na National Agricultural Insurance Scheme. Private insurance companies bi nso de agricultural nneɛma to. MOFA ka insurance companies ho sɛ wɔde premiums a wɔde asua ma smallholder okuafo. Ka wo MOFA ofisi a ɛbɛn anaa Ghana Insurers Association ho ma products a wɔwɔ saa ara ne premium rates.

English Question: Access farming land in Ghana through several ways including purchasing outright if you have capital, sharecropping where you farm another person's land and share the harvest usually 50 50, leasing land through a written agreement typically 5 to 20 years in peri-urban areas, accessing communal lands through the chief or family head in rural areas, and government land allocations for special farming zones. Always secure a written land use agreement even for sharecropping arrangements to protect your investment.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ menya asase ma okuafo adwuma wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Nya asase ma okuafo adwuma wɔ Ghana de akwan ahorow a ɛka ho de gye to sɛ wo wɔ sika, sharecropping a woto obi asase so na fa nnoa twa mmienu pɛ taa yɛ 50 50, lease asase de nhyiam krataa taa bɛyɛ mfe 5 kɔ 20 wɔ dɔn ho, nya communal asase wɔ ohene anaa abusua panyin nkyɛn wɔ kurow ho, na aban asase kyɛ ma okuafo adwuma zones a wɔayɛ. Hwɛ sɛ wotwerɛ asase de nhyiam krataa bere biara naaso sharecropping nhyiamu ma wo sɛ ɛhwɛ wo sika so.

English Question: To export farm produce from Ghana register your business with GIPC if it involves foreign investment, obtain an export licence from the Ghana Export Promotion Authority, ensure your produce meets destination country phytosanitary standards by getting certificates from the Plant Protection and Regulatory Services Directorate under MOFA, have your produce inspected by Ghana Standards Authority, work with a licensed freight forwarder for logistics, and target markets with high demand for Ghanaian products like the EU for chilli and pineapple and the UK for yam and plantain.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ mede me afuom nnuaba tɔ amansan foforɔ fi Ghana?
Twi Answer: Sɛ wobɛde wo afuom nnuaba tɔ amansan foforɔ fi Ghana a, si wo adwuma ho wɔ GIPC sɛ obi fi amansan foforɔ wɔ mu, gye export licence fi Ghana Export Promotion Authority, hwɛ sɛ wo nnuaba to country a wɔde kɔ phytosanitary standards mu de certificates fi Plant Protection ne Regulatory Services Directorate wɔ MOFA ase, ma Ghana Standards Authority hwɛ wo nnuaba so, ka licensed freight forwarder ho ma logistics, na tia markets a wɔpɛ Ghana nneɛma pii te sɛ EU ma pepper ne pineapple ne UK ma bayerɛ ne boɔde.

English Question: Training opportunities for farmers in Ghana include the Farmer Field Schools organized by MOFA where farmers learn by doing in their own fields, training by agricultural NGOs like SEND Ghana, Opportunity International and SNV, agricultural colleges and vocational institutions, online courses through platforms like Coursera and the FAO e-learning academy, cooperative training programmes, and the government-sponsored Youth in Agriculture Training Programmes. Many input suppliers also offer free agronomic training when you buy their products.
Twi Question: Training nhyiamu bɛn na ɛwɔ ma okuafo wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Training nhyiamu ma okuafo wɔ Ghana ne Farmer Field Schools a MOFA de sɛ okuafo sua wɔ wɔn ankasa afuom mu, training de agricultural NGOs te sɛ SEND Ghana, Opportunity International ne SNV, agricultural colleges ne vocational institutions, online courses wɔ platforms te sɛ Coursera ne FAO e-learning academy, cooperative training programmes, na aban-sponsored Youth in Agriculture Training Programmes. Input suppliers bi nso de free agronomic training to bere a wogye wɔn nneɛma.

English Question: Climate change in Ghana is causing more erratic rainfall, longer dry seasons, increased temperatures, more frequent flooding and drought. Adapt by using drought-tolerant varieties, adopting water harvesting techniques like half-moon pits and tied ridges, diversifying into drought-resistant crops like cowpea cassava and sorghum, using mulching to conserve soil moisture, agroforestry which involves planting trees with crops, joining early warning systems for weather forecasts, and timing planting to match current rainfall patterns rather than traditional calendars.
Twi Question: Dɛn na climate change yɛ okuafo adwuma den wɔ Ghana na dɛn na menyɛ?
Twi Answer: Climate change wɔ Ghana ma nsuo tɔ bere sesa daa, bone berɛ tenten, berɛhyɛ tɔ so, nsuo ne bone tɔ so. Siesie wo tiri ho de de drought-tolerant varieties to mu, de water harvesting nhyiamu te sɛ half-moon pits ne tied ridges, sesa kɔ drought-resistant nnuaba te sɛ bɔde, bankye ne sorghum, de mulching sɛ ɛkora asase nsuo, agroforestry a ɛkyerɛ to nnuaba ne nnuaba kaa bom, ka early warning systems ho ma berɛ nkra, na to aba bere sɛ nsuo a ɛtaa tɔ saa ara ho na gye traditional calendars.

English Question: Follow this fertilizer programme for tomatoes: at transplanting apply NPK 15-15-15 at 1 bag per acre in the planting holes. At 2 weeks after transplanting apply calcium nitrate to prevent blossom end rot. At 4 weeks apply NPK 15-15-15 top dressing. At 6 weeks switch to a high potassium fertilizer like NPK 12-12-17 to support fruit development. Add micronutrient foliar sprays containing boron zinc and magnesium every 2 weeks. Stop nitrogen fertilizer once fruit set begins to prevent excess leafy growth at the expense of fruit.
Twi Question: Ferefere programme bɛn na mede to tomatoes ho?
Twi Answer: De ferefere programme yi to tomatoes ho: bere a wode transplant to, de NPK 15-15-15 to mu bag baako biara eka baako wɔ planting holes mu. Nnansas mmienu akyi a wode transplant a, de calcium nitrate to ho sɛ blossom end rot annya. Nnansas nnan akyi de NPK 15-15-15 top dressing to ho. Nnansas nsia akyi sesa kɔ ferefere a potassium wɔ mu pii te sɛ NPK 12-12-17 ma nnuaba kɔ so. De micronutrient foliar sprays a boron, zinc ne magnesium wɔ mu to mprɛn mmienu biara nnansas. Gyae nitrogen ferefere bere a nnuaba fi ase bo sɛ ɛnhia nhaban pii a ɛdi nnuaba bo ho brε.

English Question: Main onion varieties in Ghana include Bawku Red which is the most popular local variety adapted to northern Ghana with good storage quality, Nazifi which is an improved variety with good yields, Galmi Violet from Niger which is widely grown, and Onex which gives high yields. For the southern forest zone use short-day varieties like the Texas Grano type. Avoid long-day varieties designed for temperate climates as they will not bulb properly in Ghana.
Twi Question: Onion varieties bɛn na wɔtaa to mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Onion varieties kɛse a wɔtaa to mu wɔ Ghana ne Bawku Red a ɛyɛ local variety pa ara a ɛbɛn Ghana atifi na ɛguina yie, Nazifi a ɛyɛ improved variety a ɛde nnoa pii ba, Galmi Violet fi Niger a wɔtaa to mu, na Onex a ɛde nnoa pii ba. Ma kwaeɛ zone a ɛwɔ apuei fam, de short-day varieties te sɛ Texas Grano nhyiamu. Gye wo ho fi long-day varieties a wɔayɛ ma temperate berɛ efisɛ wɔrenbua yie wɔ Ghana.

English Question: Onion downy mildew appears as pale oval lesions with a grey purple fuzzy growth on leaves causing them to collapse. Prevent it by ensuring good spacing for air circulation avoiding overhead irrigation, removing volunteer onion plants from previous seasons, applying copper-based fungicides preventively, using resistant varieties where available, and avoiding planting in heavily infested fields. Once severe infection occurs it is difficult to control and crop loss can be significant.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ onion downy mildew annya me nnuaba?
Twi Answer: Onion downy mildew kyerɛ ho te sɛ nsono fitaa a ɛyɛ oval na ɛwɔ grey-purple fuzzy nnoa wɔ nhaban so a ɛma wɔhwe. Gye wo ho fi mu de hwɛ sɛ ahodɔ pa wɔ hɔ sɛ mframa fa mu, gye wo ho fi overhead quench, yi volunteer onion nnuaba fi bere a atwam mu, de copper-based fungicides hware ansa, de resistant varieties wɔ hɔ a wɔwɔ to mu, na gye wo ho fi afuom a yadeɛ wɔ mu pii. Yadeɛ no a ɛatɔ so den a, ɛyɛ den sɛ woboa ho na nnuaba ahunu bɛtumi ayɛ den.

English Question: Bell pepper for supermarkets and export requires strict production standards. Use certified hybrid seeds like California Wonder or Yolo Wonder. Start in a nursery and transplant at 60 by 45 cm spacing. Install drip irrigation for consistent moisture. Apply balanced NPK fertilizer and calcium nitrate regularly. Stake plants to prevent lodging. Harvest when fruits reach full size with firm flesh still before colour change for green bell pepper or after colour change for red or yellow. Pack in perforated clamshell containers. Target Accra supermarkets and export companies.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ bell pepper ma dwa a bo wɔ so wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Bell pepper ma supermarkets ne export hia production standards pa ara. De certified hybrid seeds te sɛ California Wonder anaa Yolo Wonder. Fi ase wɔ nursery na transplant wɔ ahodɔ 60 ne 45 sɛntimita. Si drip quench ma nsuo so yie. De balanced NPK ferefere ne calcium nitrate to ho bere biara. De stakes si nnuaba ho. Yi bere a nnuaba bɛbo kɛse pa na flesh yɛ den da ansa na ɛregyina so ma green bell pepper anaa yi akyi bere a bo gyina so ma red anaa yellow. Kura wɔ perforated clamshell containers mu. Tia Accra supermarkets ne export companies.

English Question: Common garden egg varieties in Ghana include the white round type which is the traditional variety most common in Ghana, the striped type with green and white stripes, the elongated purple type, and improved varieties like Sinabung and Takii Hybrid. The white round variety is preferred by most Ghanaian consumers for the traditional use in raw vegetable platters with groundnut paste. Improved hybrid varieties give higher yields but require more inputs.
Twi Question: Garden egg varieties bɛn na wɔtaa to mu wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Garden egg varieties a wɔtaa to mu wɔ Ghana ne white round nhyiamu a ɛyɛ traditional variety a ɛtaa ba wɔ Ghana, striped nhyiamu a green ne white stripes wɔ so, elongated purple nhyiamu, na improved varieties te sɛ Sinabung ne Takii Hybrid. White round variety na Ghana consumers pɛ pii ma traditional de sɛ raw vegetable platters ne groundnut paste. Improved hybrid varieties de nnoa pii ba nanso ɛhia inputs pii.

English Question: Yes you can grow yam on flat land or ridges without traditional mounds but yields may be lower. On flat land use ridges 30 to 40 cm high. Staking is still essential. This method works better in areas with good rainfall and fertile soils. The advantage of flat or ridge planting is easier mechanization and lower labour cost. The disadvantage is that water can accumulate around the yam causing rot especially in heavy rainfall areas. Mounds remain the preferred method for most yam varieties.
Twi Question: Metumi ato bayerɛ a afe amma?
Twi Answer: Aane wobetumi ato bayerɛ wɔ asase a ɛtee anaa ridges a afe amma nanso nnoa bɛtumi ayɛ nketewa kakra. Wɔ asase a ɛtee so, de ridges a ɛtelɛ sɛntimita 30 kɔ 40 to. Staking da hia bere nyinaa. Nhyiamu yi yɛ adwuma yie wɔ hɔ a nsuo pa ne asase aduan wɔ. Mfaaso ne ɛyɛ mmerɛw sɛ wode machines yɛ adwuma na adwuma sika sua. Aho yɛ den ne sɛ nsuo bɛtumi adɔ so ho bayerɛ no ho a ɛma ɛsɛe a ɛhia pii wɔ hɔ a nsuo tɔ pii. Afe kyɛ sɛ ɛyɛ nhyiamu pa ma bayerɛ varieties bebree.

English Question: Cocoyam has good market opportunities in Ghana especially in urban areas. Fresh cocoyam corms sell well in all major markets. Cocoyam leaves sold as kontomire are very popular for stews and palava sauce and command good prices especially in Accra and Kumasi. Processed cocoyam flour has growing demand in the food processing industry. Export opportunities exist for dried cocoyam to the diaspora market in Europe and North America. Value addition through processing into chips flour or paste significantly improves profitability.
Twi Question: Dwa nhyiamu bɛn na ɛwɔ ma kɔkɔnte wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Kɔkɔnte wɔ dwa nhyiamu pa wɔ Ghana a ɛhia pii wɔ dɔn kɛse mu. Kɔkɔnte corms foforɔ tɔ yie wɔ dwa kɛse nyinaa. Kɔkɔnte nhaban a wɔtɔ sɛ kontomire pɛ paa ma nkwan ne palava sauce na dwa bo yɛ so pii a ɛhia pii wɔ Accra ne Kumasi. Kɔkɔnte flour a wɔayɛ so nhia taa pɛ wɔ food processing adwuma mu. Export nhyiamu wɔ ma kɔkɔnte a ɛatew kɔ diaspora dwa wɔ Yurop ne North America. Value addition wɔ de yɛ chips, flour anaa paste de ma mfaso kɔ so pii.

English Question: Select firm unripe green plantains for crispy chips or ripe ones for sweet chips. Peel and slice thinly using a mandoline or sharp knife. Soak slices in salted water for 10 minutes to reduce browning. Drain and pat dry thoroughly. Fry in hot vegetable oil at 170 to 180 degrees Celsius until golden and crispy. Drain on paper towels. Season with salt and optional spices. Package in sealed airtight bags immediately while still warm for a shelf life of 2 to 4 weeks. Plantain chips have strong market demand from supermarkets and snack distributors.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ boɔde chips ma tɔ?
Twi Answer: Yi boɔde fitaa a ɛyɛ den ma chips a ɛkɔkɔɔ anaa a ɛatwa so ma chips a ɛdɛ. Yi ho na twa nkoko de mandoline anaa akyer akyer. Da slices no mu nsuo a salt wɔ mu simma 10 sɛ ɛnnatoa yɛ tuntum. Yi fi mu na tew yie pɛpɛɛpɛ. Hyehye wɔ vegetable oil a ɛhyehyɛ paa wɔ degrees 170 kɔ 180 Celsius kosi sɛ ɛyɛ sikafuo na ɛkɔkɔɔ. Yi fi mu de ntama so. De salt ne spices ka so sɛ wopɛ. Kura wɔ sealed airtight bags ntɛm bere a ɛda so sɛ tena 2 kɔ 4 nnansas. Boɔde chips wɔ dwa nhia pa fi supermarkets ne snack distributors ho.

English Question: Care for young coconut trees by watering deeply twice a week for the first 2 years especially during dry season. Apply NPK fertilizer with high potassium every 6 months. Keep the area around the base of the tree free from grass and weeds for 2 metres. Mulch around the base to retain moisture. Protect from cattle and goats which will eat young fronds. The rhinoceros beetle is a major pest that bores into the crown. Control it by removing dead palms from the vicinity and using a hooked tool to remove beetles from the crown.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ kuuku nnuaba a wɔ mmofra ho?
Twi Answer: Hwɛ kuuku nnuaba mmofra ho de quench tia mprɛn mmienu biara nnansas mfe mmienu a ɛdi kan mu a ɛhia pii bone berɛ. De NPK ferefere a potassium wɔ mu pii to ho mprɛnsa nsia biara. Kora baabi a ɛbɛn nnuaba no ase nhawan ne nhaban foforo fi ho sɛntimita mmienu. Mulch ho sɛ ɛkora nsuo. Hwɛ nnwan ne birekyie a wɔbɛdi mmofra nhaban ho. Rhinoceros beetle yɛ adwummaker kɛse a ɛbɔ kɔtɔ wɔ crown mu. Boa ho de yi nnuaba a awu wɔ ho fi ne de hooked tool yi beetles fi crown mu.

English Question: Form a farmer cooperative in Ghana by gathering at least 10 interested farmers, electing officers including a chairman secretary and treasurer, drafting a constitution or bylaws, opening a group bank account, registering with the Department of Cooperatives under the Ministry of Employment and Labour Relations, and obtaining a certificate of registration. A cooperative enables members to access group credit, buy inputs in bulk at lower prices, market produce collectively and access government programmes. Meet regularly and keep proper financial records.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ sɛ meyi okuafo kuo wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Yi okuafo kuo wɔ Ghana de gye okuafo 10 pɛ a wɔpɛ no, yi officers a ɔpanyin, secretary ne treasurer ka ho, yɛ constitution anaa bylaws, bue group bank account, si ho wɔ Department of Cooperatives wɔ Ministry of Employment ne Labour Relations ase, na gye registration certificate. Kuo de ma members bɛtumi agye group credit, gye inputs pii wɔ bo sua, tɔ wɔn nnuaba kaa bom na gye government programmes. Gyina mu bere biara na kora financial records yie.

English Question: Reduce input costs through organic farming by making your own compost from crop residues and animal manure, using biological pest controls like neem leaf extract and predatory insects instead of chemical pesticides, planting legumes in rotation to fix nitrogen naturally reducing need for nitrogen fertilizer, using intercropping to suppress weeds naturally, collecting and saving open-pollinated seeds rather than buying hybrid seeds each season, and building soil health over time to reduce fertilizer dependence.
Twi Question: Dɛn na menyɛ organic farming sɛ ɛhia inputs sika sua?
Twi Answer: Sua inputs sika de organic farming de yɛ wo ankasa compost fi nnuaba a ato fɛw ne mmoa aguare, de biological pest controls te sɛ neem nhaban extract ne predatory insects na gye wo ho fi chemical pesticides, to legumes mu wɔ rotation sɛ ɛde nitrogen ka asase mu ankasa a ɛhia nitrogen ferefere sua, de intercropping hia nhaban foforo ankasa, pam na guina open-pollinated aba na gye wo ho fi gye hybrid aba bere biara, na tu asase ho bere biara sɛ ferefere nhia nansen.

English Question: Soil testing before farming is critical because it tells you the pH level of your soil which determines nutrient availability, the levels of major nutrients like nitrogen phosphorus and potassium, micronutrient deficiencies, the presence of toxic elements, and the organic matter content. This information allows you to apply the right fertilizer at the right rate saving money on unnecessary inputs and improving crop yields. Soil testing can be done at CSIR research institutes, some MOFA offices and private agricultural laboratories.
Twi Question: Ɛho hia sɛn sɛ wɔhwɛ asase ansa na wode aba to mu?
Twi Answer: Asase hwɛ ansa na wode aba to mu ho hia paa efisɛ ɛkyerɛ wo wo asase pH level a ɛkyerɛ ferefere a wubetumi anya, major nutrients te sɛ nitrogen, phosphorus ne potassium levels, micronutrient ahia, poisons a ɛwɔ mu, na organic matter a ɛwɔ mu. Nsɛm yi boa wo sɛ de ferefere a ɛhoa to ho wɔ measure a ɛhoa mu a ɛhia sika suas wɔ inputs a ɛhia na ɛboa nnoa kɔ so. Asase hwɛ bɛtumi ayɛ wɔ CSIR research institutes, MOFA offices bi ne private agricultural laboratories.

English Question: What are the common diseases affecting poultry in Ghana and how can they be prevented?
Twi Question: Yare bɛn na ɛtaa yɛ akokɔ wɔ Ghana na yɛbɛyɛ dɛn atua ano?
Twi Answer: Akokɔ yare a ɛtaa ba wɔ Ghana ne Newcastle Disease, Gumboro (Infectious Bursal Disease), ne Fowl Pox. Sɛ wopɛ sɛ wotua ano a, ɛsɛ sɛ wode nnuru bɔ wɔn, hwɛ yiye wɔ ahwehwɛde ho, na wode ahobammɔ ho nhyehyɛe di dwuma te sɛ ahɔho a wobɛtew wɔn so ne akokɔdan mu nnuru a wobɛtwa.

English Question: How often should I vaccinate my chickens against Newcastle Disease?
Twi Question: Ɛsɛ sɛ mede nnuru bɔ m'ankokɔ tia Newcastle Disease mpɛn ahe?
Twi Answer: Ɛsɛ sɛ wode nnuru bɔ akokɔ tia Newcastle Disease wɔ bere pɔtee bi mu, mpɛn pii no efi da a ɛtɔ so 7, afei wode nnuru foforo bɔ wɔn wɔ dapɛn 3-4 ne 8-10 mu, a egyina nnuru no su ne yare no so. Kɔhwɛ wo mpɔtam hɔ nnuataban sohwɛfo na ɔmma wo nhyehyɛe pɔtee bi.

English Question: What are the best feeding practices for goats and sheep in Ghana?
Twi Question: Akwan bɛn na ɛyɛ papa a yɛfa so ma apɔnkye ne nguan aduan wɔ Ghana?
Twi Answer: Apɔnkye ne nguan yɛ yiye wɔ sare so, nnuaba funu te sɛ aburo dua, ne nnua a wɔde yɛ aduan. Sɛ wode nkyene ne aduan foforo ka ho, titiriw wɔ ɔpɛ bere mu anaa mmoa a wɔyem/wɔma nufusu, a ɛboa. Hwɛ hu sɛ wɔnya nsu pa a ɛho tew bere nyinaa.

English Question: How can I protect my goats and sheep from common diseases like PPR?
Twi Question: Mɛyɛ dɛn abɔ m'apɔnkye ne nguan ho ban afi yare a ɛtaa ba te sɛ PPR ho?
Twi Answer: PPR (Peste des Petits Ruminants) yɛ yare a emu yɛ den. Nnuru a wɔde bɔ mmoa no ne akwan a ɛyɛ papa sen biara a wɔfa so tua ano. Akwan foforo a wɔfa so yɛ ne mmoa foforo a wobɛto wɔn nko, ahwehwɛde pa, ne mmoa a wɔyare a wobɛtew wɔn ho ntɛm. Kɔhwɛ nnuataban sohwɛfo na ɔhwɛ wɔn yare na ɔmma wɔn nnuru.

English Question: What are the advantages of using hydroponics for vegetable farming in Ghana?
Twi Question: Mfaso bɛn na ɛwɔ hydroponics a wɔde yɛ nnuaba adwuma wɔ Ghana so?
Twi Answer: Hydroponics ma wotumi dua nnuaba a asase nni mu, na wode nsu kakraa bi na edi dwuma (ɛkɔ soro kosi 90% sua) ne asase. Ɛma wotumi nya nnuaba pii, nyini ntɛm, na wotumi yɛ adwuma afe mũ no nyinaa, titiriw wɔ nkuraase anaa mmeae a asase no nyɛ papa.

English Question: How can smallholder farmers implement cost-effective drip irrigation systems?
Twi Question: Akwan bɛn na akuafo nketewa betumi afa so de nsuo gu fam nkakrankakra (drip irrigation) nhyehyɛe a ɛnsɛ sika pii adi dwuma?
Twi Answer: Akuafo nketewa betumi de nneɛma a ɛwɔ mpɔtam hɔ te sɛ plastic nsuo kɛse, taya dedaw, ne mpa di dwuma de ayɛ nsuo gu fam nkakrankakra nhyehyɛe a ɛnsɛ sika pii. Mpɔtam hɔ nhyehyɛe ne ntetee nso betumi aboa ma wɔanya saa nhyehyɛe yi na wɔakora so.

English Question: What are the main symptoms of African Cassava Mosaic Disease (ACMD) and how is it managed?
Twi Question: Nsɛnkyerɛnne titiriw bɛn na ɛwɔ African Cassava Mosaic Disease (ACMD) ho na yɛbɛyɛ dɛn ahwɛ so?
Twi Answer: ACMD nsɛnkyerɛnne ne nhaban a ɛyɛ mosaic, nhaban a ɛyɛ basaa, ne nyini a ɛbrɛ ase. Nnomaa fitaa ne nnuaba a wɔayare na ɛtaa trɛw yare no. Sɛ wopɛ sɛ wohwɛ so a, ɛsɛ sɛ wode nnuaba a ɛho tew, nnua a ɛntumi nyare, ne nnomaa fitaa a wobɛtua ano di dwuma.

English Question: How can cocoa farmers prevent Black Pod Disease?
Twi Question: Akwan bɛn na koko akuafo betumi afa so atua Black Pod Disease ano?
Twi Answer: Black Pod Disease yɛ asiane kɛse ma koko. Akwan a wɔfa so tua ano ne nnua a wobɛtwa bere nyinaa de ama mframa atumi afa mu yiye, nnuaba a wɔbɛtwa no mpɛn pii de ayi nnuaba a wɔayare afi hɔ, nnuaba a wɔayare a wobɛsie anaa wobɛhyew, ne nnuru a wɔagye atom a wobɛde agu so. Nnua a ɛntumi nyare a wobɛdua nso boa.
